801 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Upton County v. Brown


No. 08-96-00378-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


960 S.W.2d 808; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4969



September 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 1, 1998. Rehearing Overruled October 8, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 112th District Court of Upton County, Texas. (TC # 93-02-U3259-IDO). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Brock Jones.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a judgment of the 112th District Court of Upton County (Texas), which found that appellant violated the Whistleblower Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-16a (recodified as Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 554.001-.009 (1994)), and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, when it terminated appellee decedent from employment. The jury awarded damages against appellant for violating the Act and for infringing appellee's free speech rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county fired appellee decedent after he reported safety violations, misuse of county property and personnel, and other misconduct. Appellee died after filing an action under the Whistleblower Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-16a (recodified as Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 554.001-.009 (1994)), that was later amended to add a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. At trial, appellee prevailed on both claims. The court affirmed on appeal. Rejecting appellant's statute of limitations arguments, the court held that appellee timely filed the initial claim because he immediately grieved his termination to appropriate county officials, which tolled the filing time by thirty days. The § 1983 free speech claim was timely because it related back to the initial filing date. Relying on the Survival Statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.021 (1986), and the remedial purposes of the Act and § 1983, the court held that both actions survived appellee's death. The statute requiring claims to be presented to the commissioner's court before filing suit was held inapplicable. Concluding that the evidence in support of the judgment was sufficient, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: Affirming the judgment, the court held that appellee's free speech and whistleblower claims were not time-barred; nor were they subject to a statute requiring claims to be presented to the commissioner's court prior to filing suit. Relying on the Texas Survival Statute, the court held that both claims survived appellee's death. The court also held that sufficient evidence was presented at trial to support the jury's findings.

 

802 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hagopian v. State


NO. 14-95-01101-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4820



September 4, 1997, rendered  
September 4, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9521781.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of violating the Texas Alcohol & Beverage Code by refusing to allow the police to inspect the premises of the club where he worked.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was the manager of a club that was licensed to sell liquor. Police officers went to the club to check for a liquor violation and to serve an arrest warrant. Appellant refused to allow the officers to inspect the portion of the club behind the bar without a search warrant. The officers arrested him and he was found guilty of violating the Texas Alcohol and Beverage Code. The court affirmed and held that although Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 101.04 (1995) did not provide that refusal to permit inspection was a code violation, Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 61.71, 61.77 provided that a refusal to permit an inspection constituted a violation of the code. The court also held that § 101.04 was not overbroad and that it did not prohibit speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of violating state liquor control laws because appellant's refusal to permit the police to inspect the premises of the club where he worked was sufficient to establish a violation of the law. The court held that the liquor control laws did not prohibit constitutionally protected speech.

 

803 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Borg-Warner Protective Servs. Corp. v. Flores


NUMBER 13-96-028-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


955 S.W.2d 861; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4848



September 4, 1997, delivered  
September 4, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 13, 1997. Rehearing Denied November 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the decision of the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee employee on common law and statutory claims for sexual harassment and related intentional torts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer was held liable for claims of sexual harassment and related intentional torts arising from the rape of appellee employee by her supervisor. The court affirmed the judgment. It found there was sufficient evidence to support a finding that appellee was constructively discharged because the rape occurred in the course of a business outing, she was unable to report the rape because the rapist was the person to whom she was to report the incident, and appellant responded to the rape report by putting appellee on administrative leave. The court held this would compel a reasonable person in employee's position to resign. The court upheld the award of future lost earnings because it was a legitimate exercise of the trial court's equity. It held the award of punitive damages was not unconstitutional because the trial court's instruction placed reasonable constraints on the exercise of the jury's discretion and the award was based on objective criteria. The court determined that the calculation of attorney fees was proper and that appellate attorney fees were properly awarded because they were conditioned on appellate success.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment holding appellant employer liable for claims of sexual harassment and related intentional torts because appellee employee was raped by her supervisor during the course of a business outing, appellee was unable to report rape to appellant because the person to whom she was to report the rape was the rapist, and appellant responded to rape by placing appellee on administrative leave.

 

804 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re E.T.M.


NO. 01-96-00235-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4713



August 29, 1997, Opinion issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 315th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 84,916.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the order of the 315th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which transferred him from the Texas Youth Commission to prison to complete the remainder of his five-year determinate sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was adjudicated a delinquent for committing murder and sentenced to the Texas Youth Commission. As appellant approached age 18, the state moved to transfer him to prison to serve the remainder of the sentence. The trial court agreed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the grand jury approved the state's petition to adjudicate appellant a delinquent as it would an indictment. Thus, the petition upon which he was transferred to prison was an indictment under the language of Tex. Fam. Code § 53.045(d). Further, his transfer to prison was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of transfer of appellant juvenile to prison to serve the remainder of his sentence because the grand jury approved the state's petition to adjudicate him a delinquent in the same manner as it would an indictment. The legislature was constitutionally authorized to consider the grand jury's approval to be an indictment.

 

805 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Broaddus


NO. 14-96-00512-CR, NO. 14-96-00514-CR, NO. 14-96-00515-CR, NO. 14-96-00516-CR, NO. 14-96-00517-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


952 S.W.2d 598; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4619



August 28, 1997, rendered  
August 28, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd Judicial District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 30,507, 30,508, 30,509, 30,510, & 30,511.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Texas challenged an order of the 23rd Judicial District Court, Brazoria County (Texas), which quashed five indictments against appellee for official misconduct on grounds that the special grand jury that returned the indictments was unlawfully impaneled.


OVERVIEW: During appellee's term as county commissioner, he was investigated for misconduct. To avoid conflicts of interests, a district court appointed a special prosecutor and summoned jury commissioners to impanel a second, special grand jury to investigate appellee's activities. The grand jury returned five indictments against appellee. Appellee filed a motion to quash the indictments, claiming the district court had no authority to impanel a second grand jury during a regular term of court. After examining Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 19.01 et seq., the district court agreed with appellee and granted the motion to quash the indictments on grounds the second grand jury was unlawfully impaneled. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding no statutory authority to permit a district court to impanel more than one grand jury during a regular term of court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order quashing the indictments against appellee, holding that there was no statutory authority permitting a district court to impanel more than one grand jury during a regular term of court and, therefore, impaneling a second grand jury to investigate appellee was unlawful.

Battles v. State


NUMBER 13-96-587-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4600



August 28, 1997, delivered  
August 28, 1997, filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 329th District Court of Wharton County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 329th District Court of Wharton County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1994). Appellant's prior burglary conviction caused his second offense to be elevated to a first-degree felony and he was sentenced to 75 years in prison. Appellant sought review of the sentence pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary. Pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1994), appellant's prior burglary conviction elevated his second offense to a first-degree felony and enhanced his sentence to a term of 75 years in prison. Appellant sought review of the sentence pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The court determined that, although the Eighth Amendment disfavored imposition of a sentence that was grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime, substantial deference should be given to the trial court. The court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing appellant in compliance with the statute. The court held that the Cruel and Unusual Punishments Clause was not automatically violated when the trial court imposed a penalty greater than that imposed for an offense of equal or greater gravity. The court determined that the state statute was constitutional and affirmed the judgment of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which convicted appellant of burglary. Appellant's Eight Amendment rights against cruel and unusual punishment were not violated because a Texas statute elevating a second conviction to a first-degree felony and enhancing the sentence term was constitutional. The lower court was within its discretion in imposing a 75-year imprisonment term.

 

807 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Schmitz v. State


NO. 2-96-387-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


952 S.W.2d 922; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4763



August 28, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 2, 1997. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF DENTON COUNTY. Trial Court Case Number: CR-96-02572-AA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the County Court at Law No. One of Denton County, Texas that denied his motion to quash and convicted him of theft of property under $ 20 under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(1) (1994, Supp. 1997). Appellant claimed Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 45.17 (1979) complaint was vague and violated his rights under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.04 (1989), U.S. Const. amend. V, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by complaint of theft of property under $ 20 in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(1) (1994 and Supp. 1997), and appealed to the county court for a trial de novo when the justice court convicted him of the offense. The county court denied appellant's motion to quash the complaint and sentenced him pursuant to a plea agreement. On appeal, the court held that although the complaint followed the procedural form required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 45.17, and although the complaint to the justice court did not need to show the same specificity required by an indictment or information, the complaint did not allege how the property was stolen and did not describe the stolen property with specificity. Thus, the complaint did not meet the specificity requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.04 (1989) of U.S. Const. amend V and XIV or Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. However, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.181(a) (Supp. 1997) prohibited the county court from dismissing an appeal from the justice court because of a defective complaint. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied appellant's motion to quash and convicted him of theft of property under $ 20. The court held that although the complaint was defective because it was insufficiently specific, because the complaint was filed in the justice court, the county court was statutorily precluded from dismissing the complaint when appellant appealed his justice court conviction for a trial de novo in the county court.

Davis v. City of Palestine


NO. 12-95-00180-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


973 S.W.2d 319; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4749



August 27, 1997, Delivered  
August 27, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand February 26, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1508. Rehearing Denied October 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 3RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF ANDERSON COUNTY, TEXAS. Hon. Sam Bournais, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants business property owners sought review of the order from the 3rd Judicial District Court of Anderson County (Texas) granting appellee city's summary judgment motion in appellants' suit against appellee pursuant to the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq., for damages to their business property and an unconstitutional taking of that property.


OVERVIEW: Appellants business property owners sued appellee city under the Texas Tort Claims Act (act), Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq., for damages to their business property. Appellants also alleged an unconstitutional taking of that property. The lower court granted appellee's summary judgment motion. This appeal followed. Appellants contended summary judgment was improper because they stated a cause of action under the act, sovereign immunity did not protect appellee, and appellee failed to meet its summary judgment burden by establishing that no genuine issue of material fact existed as to its affirmative defenses or at least one element of each of appellants' causes of action. Since the lower court did not specify upon what basis it granted judgment for appellee, the court evaluated every theory set forth in appellee's motion to determine if summary judgment was proper. The court noted that appellee failed to offer any summary judgment proof to dispute appellants' charge. Further, appellee failed to establish its affirmative defense of sovereign immunity as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting appellee city's summary judgment motion in appellant property owners suit for damages to their property because there were no grounds upon which the lower court could properly grant summary judgment for appellee. The matter was remanded for further lower court proceedings.

Dewillis v. State


NO. 14-96-01486-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


951 S.W.2d 212; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4402



August 21, 1997, rendered  
August 21, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9642912.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the County Criminal Court at Law, Number 15, Harris County (Texas), that denied appellant's application for a writ of habeas corpus following the revocation of his probation, which was imposed after appellant violated Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the offenses of telephone harassment and stalking under Tex Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(4) and (7)(A), respectively. Appellant received probation for both offenses. Subsequently, the state moved to revoke appellant's probation. After a hearing, the trial court revoked appellant's probation on the harassment charge and sentenced him to 150 days of incarceration. However, the trial court continued appellant's probation for the stalking charge. Appellant then filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus, challenging the constitutionality of § 42.07. The trial court granted appellant's application to the extent of the stalking conviction and denied it as to the harassment conviction. As a result, appellant sought review, claiming § 42.07 was unconstitutionally vague on its face in violation of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. On review, the court affirmed the denial of appellant's request because appellant failed in his burden of demonstrating § 42.07(a)(4) was unconstitutional as it was applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's request for a writ of habeas corpus because appellant failed to explain how the harassment statute was unconstitutional as applied to him.

Camacho v. Samaniego


No. 08-95-00329-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


954 S.W.2d 811; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4517



August 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' and Appellees' Motions for Rehearing Denied October 29, 1997.
Rehearing denied by, 10/29/1997
Petition for review denied by, 05/21/1998
Costs and fees proceeding at Justice Bail Bonds v. Samaniego, 68 S.W.3d 811, 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 8600 (Tex. App. El Paso, 2001)
Related proceeding at Telles v. Samaniego, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 8536 (Tex. App. El Paso, Sept. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 34th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 88-679). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Jack Ferguson, Judge Presiding.
Camacho v. Samaniego, 831 S.W.2d 804, 1992 Tex. LEXIS 57, 35 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 734 (Tex., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, various bail bond companies, sought review of the summary judgment entered by the 34th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, in favor of appellees, sheriff and county, in an action to determine whether appellants were entitled to refunds for past illegal surety bonds fees they had paid.


OVERVIEW: Following a judgment by the Texas Supreme Court that past surety bond fees paid by appellant bail bond companies were illegal, the case was remanded to the trial court for determination of whether appellants were entitled to refunds. The trial court entered a final take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellees, sheriff and county, and appellants sought review. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded in part. The court, inter alia, affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the county finding that appellee county was not a proper party to this suit. The court held that acts performed by officials that were subsequently declared to lack statutory authority could not be attributed to a unit of state government, and therefore could not be a party to the action. The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee sheriff in his individual capacity, but reversed as to his official capacity. The Texas Supreme Court's invalidation of the bail bond fees applied retroactively. Appellants demonstrated that they paid the bond approval fees under implied duress, and thus they were entitled to a refund. The action was remanded to determine the amount of refund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part, the decision of the trial court which entered a final take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee sheriff and county. The court remanded finding that appellants were entitled to refunds. The court affirmed the summary judgment as to appellee sheriff in his individual capacity, but reversed the judgment as to the suit brought against him in his official capacity.

Gonzalez v. State


No. 04-96-00130-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


954 S.W.2d 98; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4373



August 20, 1997, Delivered  
August 20, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From the 290th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-CR-3363. Honorable Sharon MacRae, Judge Presiding 1.


1 Honorable Sharon MacRae signed the judgment of conviction and sentence, but Honorable Raymond Angelini of the 187th Judicial District Court presided over the trial.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS REFORMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 290th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, which found appellant guilty of misapplication of fiduciary property of the value of $ 200 or more but less than $ 10,000, contending that an incorrect standard was applied in determining that appellant was a fiduciary, that no agreement existed under which appellant held property, and that the restitution order was unsupported by the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant worked at a plumbing supply store as a store clerk. When his employer noticed shrinkage in the inventory, an investigation was conducted, which revealed that appellant had been making off-premises sales of his employer's supplies. Appellant was convicted of misapplication of fiduciary property of the value of $ 200 or more but less than $ 10,000, placed on community supervision, and ordered to pay restitution. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the essential elements for a finding of a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.45 were met. The evidence showed that appellant acted in a fiduciary capacity in that he worked in a position of trust and received money on behalf of his employer. In that capacity, he misapplied property contrary to a duty created by the understanding between himself and his employer as to appellant's duties as a store clerk with regard to the handling of money and the control and access to the inventory. The court reversed the monetary restitution order for losses independent of the charged offenses where the bulk of the restitution payment was awarded to a non-victim, contrary to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.037.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of misapplication of fiduciary property, holding that the evidence was sufficient to show that appellant, in a fiduciary capacity, violated the law by selling his employer's supplies on the side. The court reversed a restitution order as improperly entered because restitution to insurance company was unavailing under applicable law.

 

812 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Schneider v. State


No. 06-96-00097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


951 S.W.2d 856; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4230


July 25, 1997, Submitted  
August 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 727148.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his felony conviction from the 208th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), contending that his conviction for delivery by offer to sell was void because Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of delivery by offer to sell one kilogram of crack cocaine to an undercover police officer, in violation of Texas Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112. Appellant sought review, asserting that § 481.112 was unconstitutionally vague because it was uncertain whether the word offer as used in § 481.112 meant either the mere suggestion of an exchange or actual presentation of a controlled substance. The court affirmed the conviction. The statute prohibited delivery, which was defined by Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002(8) to include offering to sell a controlled substance. Further, the court found that the term offer meant both verbal conduct alone and actual presentation of a controlled substance. Because the statutory provisions clearly placed persons of reasonable intelligence on notice that they could not promote an exchange of a controlled substance to another person for value either by words or deeds, the word offer was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's felony conviction, holding that the word "offer" was not unconstitutionally vague because the statutory provisions placed persons of reasonable intelligence on notice that the promotion of an exchange of a controlled substance to another person for value by words or deed was prohibited.

San Benito Consol. Indep. Sch. Dist. v. McGinnis


NO. 03-96-00643-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4284



August 14, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-14336, HONORABLE SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district challenged the ruling of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas) that granted appellee law firm's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school district brought suit against appellee law firm, alleging legal malpractice in failing to file, on the school district's behalf, a suit for judicial review of an order issued by the Commissioner of Education. The trial court granted the law firm's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the school district contended in three points of error that the trial court erroneously applied the substantial evidence rule and that the evidence raised a fact issue as to the existence of an attorney-client relationship. The school district also argued that the commissioner's decision was not supported by substantial evidence. After review, the court concluded that the trial court correctly applied the pure-substantial-evidence review and that the commissioner's decision was supported by substantial evidence. Having overruled these two points of error, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted appellee law firm's motion for summary judgment because the trial court did not erroneously apply the substantial evidence rule and the commissioner's decision was supported by substantial evidence.

 

814 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. State


NO. 01-96-00401-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


961 S.W.2d 396; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4331



August 14, 1997, Opinion issued


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 209th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 514070. Michael McSpadden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that imposed a jury assessed sentence of 17 years imprisonment for non-capital murder, following the admission, over defendant's objection, of victim impact testimony from the victim's sister during the punishment phase of defendant's trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 12 years imprisonment, but the sentence was reversed on appeal and remanded for resentencing. At the new penalty phase hearing before the jury, the trial court admitted into evidence certain victim impact testimony from the victim's sister. The jury assessed punishment at 17 years imprisonment and defendant appealed, arguing that the victim impact evidence was irrelevant and inadmissible. In affirming, the court ruled that, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a) (Supp. 1997), evidence relevant to sentencing included evidence concerning the circumstances of the offense. It was not an abuse of discretion to admit the victim impact evidence here because the impact that the offense had on the victim's sister was relevant as a circumstance of the offense because it bore on defendant's personal responsibility and moral guilt. The prejudicial effect of such evidence did not outweigh its probative value under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 403.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed because it was not abuse of discretion for the trial court to admit victim impact testimony during the punishment phase; such evidence was relevant to sentencing since the effect of the offense on others is a circumstance of the offense that may be considered by the jury in assessing punishment.

 

815 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Austin v. City of Cedar Park


NO. 03-96-00209-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


953 S.W.2d 424; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4281



August 14, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 368TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 95-317-C368, HONORABLE BURT CARNES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant releasing municipality sought review of a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee adopting municipality from the District Court of Williamson County, 368th Judicial District (Texas), contending that Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 42.024 (1997) was a local law regulating appellant's affairs in violation of Tex. Const. art. III, § 56.


OVERVIEW: In a suit against appellant releasing municipality, appellee adopting municipality's sought a declaratory judgment regarding the constitutionality of Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 42.024 (1997). The statute permitted a municipality to compel the transfer a municipality's unincorporated area adjacent and contiguous to its corporate boundaries that was declared extraterritorial jurisdiction upon satisfaction of certain requirements. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of § 42.024 and appellant sought review therefrom. The court reversed the decision, sustaining appellant's argument that § 42.024 was a local law targeting a single geographic area and was of no statewide significance in violation of Tex. Const. art. III, § 56. Although the court found no fault with the statute's general purpose of curbing abusive extraterritorial jurisdiction practices, the statute's classifications relating to requirements of limited-purpose annexation, electric utility ownership, and transbasin diversion permits had no reasonable basis. Further, the requirements did not legitimately distinguish the parties from other municipalities with regard to the statute's public purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment in favor of appellee adopting municipality, holding that challenged statute was unconstitutional. The statute, which singled out a particular local area for special treatment without a reasonable basis for doing so violated the prohibition against special, rather than general local laws.

 

816 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Osterberg v. Peca


No. 08-95-00223-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


952 S.W.2d 121; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4221



August 8, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 205th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 94-2825). Trial Court Judge: Paul Nye, presiding judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and rendered in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of an order from the 205th District Court, El Paso County (Texas), which entered judgment in favor of appellee candidate on his claim against appellants for a violation of Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 253, because they failed to comply with reporting requirements after making direct campaign expenditures for television ads in favor of the candidate appellee opposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizens sought review of an order finding that they had violated Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 253 by failing to comply with reporting requirements after making direct campaign expenditures for television ads. Appellants waived their claims that Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 253 was unconstitutional, or that they substantially complied with the statute, because those issues were not properly preserved for appellate review. The court found that the jury was properly instructed that appellants could not be civilly liable unless they were aware that the expenditures were in violation of the election code. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's findings that one of the appellants knowingly violated the election code. Because the record was completely devoid of evidence that the other appellant participated in the expenditures with knowledge that they were in violation of the election code, the judgment against her was reversed. Regarding appellee's cross-appeal, the court held that appellee waived recovery of his attorney's fees by failing to obtain a jury finding on attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict against an appellant citizen because there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's findings that he knowingly violated the election code. However, because there was no evidence presented on that issue regarding the other appellant, the judgment against her was reversed.

Owens v. State


NO. 01-95-01365-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4163



August 7, 1997, Opinion issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 615522.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, which adjudicated him guilty of aggravated robbery and assessed punishment at eight-years confinement.


OVERVIEW: After pleading guilty without an agreed recommendation as to punishment, the trial court granted appellant deferred adjudication on an aggravated robbery charge. The state later filed a motion to adjudicate guilt and the trial court assessed punishment at eight-years confinement. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. Appellant, by his guilty plea, waived his right to argue that the statutory procedure for the acceptance of his guilty plea was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in entering a judgment when the record was silent as to a waiver of his right to compulsory process and to present evidence on his behalf. Error that could be raised on appeal despite a guilty plea was error of a constitutional dimension. Both of appellant's complaints went to presenting evidence and witnesses to the court. Neither involved questions of the court's jurisdiction, nor questioned the constitutionality of the statute prescribing his offense. By not objecting in the trial court to the alleged disproportionality of his sentences, appellant waived any error with respect thereto. Appellant failed to establish the ineffectiveness of counsel during the trial's punishment phase.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the judgment adjudicating appellant guilty of aggravated robbery and imposing sentence, holding appellant, by his guilty plea, waived his right to appeal certain alleged errors because these errors did not involve questions of the court's jurisdiction and did not question the constitutionality of the statute prescribing his offense.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:

Cases cited by appellant that mandated reversal were distinguishable because they were cases where no admonishments were given at all. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(2)(B) (1997) was constitutional because classifications based on age for offenses involving deviant sexual acts furthered the state's legitimate interest in protecting children.


OUTCOME: Appellant juvenile's adjudication of delinquency for the aggravated sexual assault of two female juveniles was affirmed because he was represented by counsel and did not argue that he was harmed by the trial judge's failure to completely admonish him.

Wade v. Commission for Lawyer Discipline


NO. 01-95-01080-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


961 S.W.2d 366; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4177



August 7, 1997, Opinion issued


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 333rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9456018.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lawyer challenged a decision from the 333rd District Court. Harris County, Texas, which suspended him from the practice of law, with the first 90 days to be active suspension, the remainder to be probated, and the order which revoked the probation.


OVERVIEW: Disciplinary proceedings were instituted against appellant lawyer for charging excessive fees and failing to account for costs in connection with his representation of five women on a sexual harassment claim. The trial court ordered a suspension of appellant's license with part to be active, and the remainder to be probated subject to various terms. The probation was subsequently revoked. Appellant challenged both rulings, arguing there was no finding of just cause and the unwillingness of the women to sign the complaint. The court held that the Commission for Lawyer Discipline found just cause was shown and that no abatement of an inquiry was justified. The five women had hired an attorney to sue appellant to get an accounting of the fees and expenses in their litigation with their former employer. This was legally sufficient evidence that appellant violated the disciplinary rules. Appellant had been afforded due process during the proceedings. When he failed to comply with the terms of his suspension, the probation period was properly revoked.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the suspension of appellant lawyer's license and the revocation of his probation period because he had to be sued before he provided an accounting for fees and expenses to his clients; he had been afforded his due process rights but failed to comply with the conditions of his suspension.

Gutierrez v. State


No. 04-95-00528-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


954 S.W.2d 86; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4022



July 31, 1997, Delivered  
July 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied September 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 25th Judicial District Court, Guadalupe County, Texas. Trial Court No. 94-1081-CR. Honorable Dwight E. Peschel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 25th Judicial District Court of Guadalupe County (Texas) for first-degree murder and his sentence to life in prison, on the basis that his right to equal protection was violated by the county's grand juror selection process, and that the trial court erred in not granting his motion to transfer venue.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction and life sentence for first-degree murder on the basis that his right to equal protection was violated by the county's grand juror selection process, and that the trial court erred in not granting his motion to transfer venue. The court held that appellant did not establish a prima facie case of an equal protection violation. The court, applying a three-pronged test, held that Spanish-surnamed Americans of Mexican descent were recognized as a clearly identifiable class with a history of being subject to discriminatory treatment, and that the "key-man" system, where a district judge is appointed to maintain a list of prospective jurors, was susceptible to abuse. The court held, however, that appellant failed to establish that the class had been underrepresented on the county grand juries by a legally significant amount over a legally significant period of time. The court reversed appellant's conviction on the basis that appellant's uncontroverted motion for change of venue complied with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 31.03, and that the court erred in denying the motion without evidentiary hearing because it was untimely filed.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were reversed and remanded because the trial court erred in not considering the merits of appellant's motion to transfer.

 

821 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hearn v. Servos


NO. 14-95-01105-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3963



July 31, 1997, rendered  
July 31, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Civil Court at Law No. 4. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 627823.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a summary judgment from the Civil Court at Law No. 4, Harris County, Texas, entered on appellee dentist's motion in appellant's malpractice suit. Appellant contended that the limitations period in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1997) had not run on her claim.


OVERVIEW: A fax letter adduced in evidence at summary judgment indicated that appellant patient knew that appellee dentist had cracked the root of her tooth at the time that it happened, and that, in fact, she had told him so at that time. In light of the two year limitations period of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1997), an action commenced by appellant more than three years after this dental surgery was untimely, and the court affirmed the summary judgment for appellee. The court held that although art. 4590i, § 10.01, contained three variants for determining when a cause of action accrued, it was clear that if a specific instance of negligence was alleged the cause of action arose at that incident. The court noted that the complaint alleged no other negligence, and although it did relate certain additional treatment provided by appellee, or in some cases that he failed to provide, this was not a case involving a course of treatment. Because appellant was immediately aware that something went wrong, there was no issue of discovery or concealment, and there was no question of a violation of the Texas constitutional open courts provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellee dentist. The court found that appellant patient was immediately aware of appellee's negligence, thus her suit, brought a full year after the limitations period had run, was untimely.

DE PRINS v. VAN DAMME


NO. 12-97-00082-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


953 S.W.2d 7; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4091



July 31, 1997, delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied June 1, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4589.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 114TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS. Galloway Calhoun, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonresident appealed from the order of the 114th District Court of Smith County (Texas) that sustained the special appearance of defendants foreign journalist, foreign editor, and foreign magazine, pursuant to Tex. R. Civ. P. 120(a), and dismissed, for lack of personal jurisdiction, plaintiff's action alleging that defendant foreign journalist slandered plaintiff during a telephone call from Belgium to two residents of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff nonresident brought a defamation action in Texas court against defendants foreign journalist, foreign editor, and foreign magazine. The complaint alleged that defendant foreign journalist had telephoned two Texas residents from Belgium and slandered plaintiff. The parties were all Belgian residents and none of them engaged in any business in Texas. Accordingly, defendants filed a special appearance pursuant to Tex. R. Civ. P. 120(a) and moved for dismissal for lack of personal jurisdiction. The trial court sustained the special appearance and dismissed the complaint. Plaintiff appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that defendants had not established sufficient minimum contacts with Texas and an assertion of long-arm personal jurisdiction over defendants by Texas courts, where the only contact was a telephone call, would violate traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice so as to deny defendants due process of law. The state of Texas had no substantial interest in the dispute, there was no showing that there was not a convenient forum in Belgium, and it was unreasonable to require defendants to defend themselves in a Texas court.


OUTCOME: The order sustaining defendants' special appearance and dismissing plaintiff's complaint was affirmed because plaintiff failed to show defendants had sufficient minimum contacts with Texas and the assertion of jurisdiction would not comport with notions of fair play and substantial justice; long-arm jurisdiction was not established when all the parties were nonresidents and the only contact with Texas involved a telephone call into the state.

State v. Condran


No. 05-96-01313-CR, No. 05-96-01314-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


951 S.W.2d 178; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3895



July 25, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication. Appellee's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 366th District Court. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 366-80406-96 and 366-80588-95.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the 366th District Court, Collin County (Texas), which dismissed prosecution against appellee and barred further prosecution. The state asserted error where appellee was indicted before a habeas corpus hearing, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01and 28.061 (1989) were in violation of the separation of powers doctrine, and the trial court abused its discretion in finding no good cause for delay of the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was arrested and indicted for sexual assault and for aggravated sexual assault. Appellee filed an application for writ of habeas corpus requesting that the sexual assault indictment be dismissed because the state had not obtained the indictment pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989). The lower court dismissed the prosecution pursuant to art. 32.01 and barred further prosecution pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 (1989). The state sought review. On appeal, the court reviewed the timing of grand jury indictments and the rules governing dismissal in detail. The court determined that the state was entitled to protection under the separation of powers doctrine and art. 28.061 violated the separation of powers doctrine. As such, the law was unconstitutional. Also, because the state could proceed with its case against an accused and seek an indictment after a dismissal under art. 32.01, appellee was required to obtain a ruling on his art. 32.01 motion before the grand jury returned an indictment or the question was moot. Therefore, the court reversed the order dismissing the indictments against appellee and remanded the cases for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the indictments for sexual assault and aggravated sexual assault against appellee and remanded the cases for trial because the criminal rule limiting appellee's prosecution under the facts of the case violated the separation of powers doctrine and was therefore unconstitutional.

Andrews v. Proctor


NO. 07-95-0399-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


950 S.W.2d 750; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3905



July 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellees' Motions for Rehearing Overruled September 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 140TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY;. NOS. 94-547,743; 94-549,239; 94-548,310;. HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Overrule of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 6, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3385.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment from the 140th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which granted appellee officers' motion for summary judgment and declared Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.057 (1988) constitutional and issued a writ of mandamus compelling appellant to comply with the provisions of § 143.057.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted appellee officers' motion for summary judgment against appellant city, declared Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 143.057 (1988) constitutional, and issued a writ of mandamus ordering the city to comply with the statute. Appellant challenged the order, contending the statute was unconstitutional because it deprived them of their due process and equal protection rights and conferred legislative authority on a private entity without providing guidelines for the selection of arbitrators. The court reversed the trial court's judgment. First, the court overruled appellant's contention that its rights had been violated because appellant was a political subdivision of the state and could not assert rights of a person. Secondly, the court held that appellant had standing to challenge the statute because it affected appellant's interests, where the city had a duty to operate within the confines of the state law, when it believed the state law to be unconstitutional. Finally, the court held the statutory language was impermissibly vague as to the qualifications of the arbitrators, and because no standards were set forth by the legislature, § 143.057 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee officers'. The underlying statute regarding the qualifications of arbitrators to hear appellees' grievances was vague and unconstitutional. Additionally, the court reasoned that appellant city had standing to challenge the statute where its interests were adversely affected when the statute failed to provide guidelines for the arbitrators.

Hernandez v. State


NO. 03-95-00696-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


952 S.W.2d 59; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3818



July 24, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand of March 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1836.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0954710, HONORABLE WILFORD FLOWERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas), where he was found guilty of capital murder. Appellant asserted he did not knowingly and voluntarily waive his rights before making his incriminating statements to the police, and that the statements were in fact involuntary, as well asserting error in juror service issues and other alleged errors.


OVERVIEW: After police investigation and resulting confession, appellant was found guilty of capital murder. Appellant sought review and asserted he did not knowingly and voluntarily waive his rights before making his incriminating statements to the police, and that the statements were in fact involuntary. On review, the court noted that appellant did not speak English, but a Spanish speaking officer conducted the interrogation. Appellant signed a written confession. The court examined the details of the interrogation and found that appellant was given proper warnings and the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by concluding that appellant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his statutory and constitutional rights before giving his oral and written confessions. The court also examined issues regarding the jury and found that, although a juror was excludable due to a criminal record, the fact that the juror remained on the panel was not in and of itself reversible error. Further, it was for appellant ask specific questions and move to exclude the juror. As there was no reversible error, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for capital murder was affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion by concluding that appellant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his statutory and constitutional rights before giving his oral and written confessions. Also, there was no error in retaining an excludable juror where the juror's service was a statutory, not a constitutional, error.

Elston v. Resolution Servs.


NO. 03-96-00414-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


950 S.W.2d 180; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3825



July 24, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-06720, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a decision of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), 250th Judicial District, that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee collection agency in appellant's suit for alleged violations of the Debt Collection Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 5069-11.01 to 11.12 (1987 & Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant debtor brought suit against appellee collection agency alleging appellee violated the Debt Collection Act (act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 5069-11.01 to 11.12 (1987 & Supp. 1997). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee and appellant sought review. Appellant challenged the trial court's ruling in that it denied his request for damages. Under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Gordon v. Western Steel Co.


NUMBER 13-95-512-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


950 S.W.2d 743; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3843



July 24, 1997, delivered  
July 24, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 21, 1997. Rehearing Denied August 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, contractors, challenged summary judgments granted by the 319th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) for appellees, subcontractors, based on appellees' substantial completion of a construction project that triggered a 10 year statute of repose under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.009 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, contractors, brought actions for contribution and indemnity against appellees, subcontractors, which alleged that appellees performed defective work on a construction project. The court affirmed the summary judgments entered by the trial court for appellees based the 10 year statute of repose for the construction of improvements to real property under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.009 (1986). The trial court correctly ruled for appellees because they proffered uncontroverted proof that their improvements were substantially completed more than 10 years before appellants brought the action. The court ruled that each appellee's substantial completion of its share of the project constituted an improvement to real property which then triggered the statute of repose. Therefore, the court rejected appellants' contention that the statute was not triggered until the entire construction project was completely finished and held that appellants' action was time-barred. The court found that appellees' affidavits and supporting documentation were sufficiently clear, positive, and direct proof of completion to support the summary judgments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments granted by the trial court against appellants, contractors, because when appellees, subcontractors, substantially completed their portions of a construction project, the statute of repose was triggered, and appellees proffered uncontroverted proof that their work was finished over 10 years before appellants brought their actions for contribution and indemnify for allegedly defective work.

Stautzenberger v. State


NO. 03-96-00665-CR, NO. 03-96-00666-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3923



July 24, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF COMAL COUNTY NOS. 95CR-822A & 95CR-823A, HONORABLE FRED CLARK, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders from the County Court at Law, Comal County (Texas). A jury found him guilty of speeding and operating an unregistered motor vehicle under Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 502.002, 545.351 (1997). The county court at law assessed punishment at fines. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the county court erred in failing to prove its jurisdiction over him and that §§ 502.002, 545.351 violated his constitutional right to travel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of speeding and operating an unregistered motor vehicle under Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 502.002, 545.351 (1997) for which he was fined. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the county court lacked jurisdiction over him as he was born free as a natural American citizen and not a participant in the Texas forum and that it failed to prove its jurisdiction after his demand that the proceeding be vacated for want of jurisdiction. He also claimed that §§ 502.002, 545.351 violated his constitutional right to travel on public roads. The court affirmed the judgment of defendant's guilt on grounds that the county court had jurisdiction over defendant, as he could not unilaterally immunize himself from the laws of the state. The county court was under no obligation to prove its jurisdiction and Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 502.002, 545.351 (1997) was a valid constitutional exercise of the state's police power. The court noted that driving was a privilege, not a constitutionally protected right, and that motor vehicle registration fees were a constitutional levy on the privilege of operating a motor vehicle on public roads.


OUTCOME: The judgment upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of speeding and operating an unregistered motor vehicle was affirmed where the county court had jurisdiction over defendant, as he could not unilaterally immunize himself from the laws of the state. The statute under which defendant was found guilty was a constitutional exercise of the state's police power, and the county court was under no obligation to prove its jurisdiction.

Elston v. Bank of N.Y.


NO. 03-96-00411-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3938



July 24, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of the order of the 353rd Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee bank in appellant's action for alleged violations of the Debt Collection Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-11.01 to 11.12 (1987 & Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant debtor filed an action against appellee bank for violations of the Debt Collection Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-11.01 to 11.12 (1987 & Supp. 1997). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court affirmed, rejecting appellant's contention that the trial court erred in ruling that he was required to prove actual damages in order to recover under the Act. He contended that a person who established a violation of the Act was automatically entitled to the measure of damages set forth in subsection (c) thereof without regard to whether the person had suffered actual damages. The court found that this section provided a minimum amount of damages for parties who successfully proved violation of the Act that resulted in actual damages. Appellant alleged various physical and psychological injuries but did not link them to the actual violation of which he complained. He failed to establish conclusively that he had suffered actual damages related to the violations, therefore he failed to carry his burden of proof on summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee bank because appellant debtor failed to carry his burden of proving that he suffered actual damages related to the violations under the Debt Collection Act.

Box v. State


NOS. 01-95-01036-CR, 01-95-01037-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3894



July 24, 1997, Opinion issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 78,784B and 78,785B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Court No. 3 at Brazoria County (Texas), which convicted appellant of 10 counts of telephone harassment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07 (1993) after a complaint was filed regarding several obscene phone calls which were traced to appellant's place of business.


OVERVIEW: Obscene calls were traced to appellant's place of business, and appellant was convicted under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(1) (1993) for telephone harassment. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. Appellant claimed ineffective counsel because counsel had failed to obtain a ruling on a motion to produce telephone recordings and records. While there had been no ruling, the court found counsel's actions reasonable and any harm cured by a ruling on appellant's objection to the introduction of documents on the same grounds. Similarly, the court held that counsel's failure to object to the admission of payroll records and to leading questions would not make counsel's actions unreasonable when the record was silent as to why counsel had not objected. The court also found that § 42.07(a)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague because it made clear to a person of ordinary intelligence the distinction between what was forbidden and what was lawful. Finally, the court found sufficient testimony to establish the necessary predicate for admitting telephone records under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 803(6), and sufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted appellant of 10 counts of telephone harassment because the necessary predicate had been established for admitting telephone records as evidence, and the evidence sufficiently supported the verdict, while appellant's counsel had not been ineffective, and the harassment statute under which appellant had been convicted was not unconstitutionally vague.

Rainey v. State


NO. 03-95-00573-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


949 S.W.2d 537; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3817



July 24, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BURNET COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 7770, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder under Tex. Penal Code § 19.02(b) (1994) in the District Court of Burnet County 33rd Judicial District, (Texas), and he was sentenced to a long term. On appeal, defendant claimed, inter alia, that § 19.02(b) was unconstitutional, the jury charge was erroneous, an instruction was improperly refused, the search warrant affidavit was insufficient, and the state did not name a punishment witness before the hearing.


OVERVIEW: A person had raped defendant's sister, so defendant killed the person. He was convicted of murder under Tex. Penal Code § 19.02(b) (1994). On appeal, the court held that §19.02(b) was constitutional even though voluntary manslaughter was not a separate crime. Although sudden passion was later held to be a factor in the punishment phase, shifting the burden of proof did not violate substantive due process rights. The court stated that defendant's challenge was to the sufficiency of the indictment, which was a claim he had not preserved. Nor did the statute violate the separation of powers by abridging the duties of district attorneys and grand juries. The factual evidence was sufficient because the court could not say that the jury's finding was manifestly unjust. Evidence did not support a requested instruction on voluntary intoxication, and any error was harmless. The search warrant affidavit was not in the record, so it could not be reviewed. Even if the court assumed that the trial court had abused its discretion in allowing the state's nondisclosed witnesses to testify, the error made no contribution to the punishment because the evidence was cumulative. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder conviction because the statute was not unconstitutional and the factual evidence was sufficient. Evidence did not support the claimed error in the charge, and any error was harmless. Evidence did not support the requested instruction on voluntary intoxication. There was no review of the search warrant affidavit because it was not in the record.

Khatib v. Husain


NO. 2-96-302-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


949 S.W.2d 805; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3776



July 17, 1997, DELIVERED


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE 48TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband and appellant wife challenged the order of the 48th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee treating physician, appellee radiologist, appellee surgeon, and appellee professional association on the ground that appellants' medical malpractice suit was time-barred under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and appellant wife sued appellee treating physician, appellee radiologist, appellee surgeon, and appellee professional association for malpractice in diagnosing and treating appellant wife's breast cancer. Appellees moved for summary judgment, asserting that the suit was time-barred under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art.4590i, § 10.01. The trial court granted appellees' motions. Appellants challenged that decision. On appeal, the court reversed the summary judgment granted to appellee treating physician and affirmed the summary judgments granted to other appellees. Appellants' claim against appellee treating physician was timely because the limitations period did not start to run until the final day of appellee treating physician's continuing course of treatment. Appellants' claims against the other appellees, who only had one-time encounters with appellant wife, were time-barred. Also, because appellants unreasonably delayed in filing suit, the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 did not render the statute of limitations unconstitutional as applied to the claims against other appellees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment granted to appellee treating physician, on the medical malpractice claim filed by appellant husband and appellant wife, and affirmed the summary judgments granted to appellee radiologist, appellee surgeon, and appellee professional association. The statute of limitations did not bar appellants' claim against appellee treating physician who provided appellant wife with a continuing course of treatment.

Sharp v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3587



July 10, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 6. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MA95-51333-G, MB95-51240-G, & MA95-51332-G.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, appealed judgments from the County Criminal Court of Dallas County (Texas) which convicted each of them of resisting arrest, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.03 (1994), and additionally convicted appellant husband of failure to identify, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.02(a) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Observing that appellants husband and wife were not wearing seat belts, police pulled over their vehicle. Appellant husband, the driver, refused repeated requests to produce his license or proof of insurance. An officer informed appellants they were under arrest. Each appellant allegedly struggled with one or more of the officers. After his arrest, appellant husband refused to give the officers his name, address, or date of birth. Because police had a specific basis for believing appellant had committed a traffic offense and appellant was under lawful arrest when he refused to give the police his name, address, or date of birth, the court held that his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions for resisting arrest. The court also affirmed appellant husband's conviction for failure to identify, rejecting his contention that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him.

Norris v. State


NO. 14-94-01078-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3592



July 10, 1997, rendered  
July 10, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9400157.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of capital murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of capital murder of a bank's night depositor, argued trial court error in denying his motion to discover the identity of the confidential informant who "fingered" appellant. The court disagreed, ruling that the exception to appellee state's right to withhold the identity of an informer under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 508(a) was not met by appellant, in that he failed to show that the informer could have supplied evidence relative to appellant's guilt or intent to kill. Moreover, Tex. R. Crim. P. 613, precluding witnesses from hearing each other's testimony, did not bar appellee from speaking with the state's witnesses as a group. And appellant cited no authority in support of his claim that the capital murder statute was unconstitutional. Further, no jury instruction was necessary on how the parole law applied to a defendant for whom the death penalty was waived when the jury had yet to decide appellant's guilt. That appellee "spoke to appellant" during final argument was not error as appellee was moving around and pointing to a chart behind appellant. And the trial court lacked jurisdiction to rule on a new trial motion not made within the time allowed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed convicting appellant of capital murder and sentencing him to life imprisonment, because appellant not entitled to learn identity of informant who "fingered" him, as he failed to show that informant could have provided evidence of his innocence, because no authority was cited in support of unconstitutionality of murder statute, and because trial court lacked jurisdiction to rule on new trial motion not timely filed.

Marx v. State


NO. 03-95-00333-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


953 S.W.2d 321; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3472



July 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BURNET COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 7693, HONORABLE CHARLES J. HEARN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Burnet County, 33rd Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child and he appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. The court held that allowing a 14-year-old victim with the emotional maturity of a six or seven-year-old and a six-year-old eyewitness to testify by closed-circuit television did not violate appellant's due process rights or right to be presumed innocent where the procedure was necessary to protect the welfare of the children who would be traumatized and suffer emotional distress by the presence of appellant. Even though an additional instruction that televised testimony was not to be taken as a comment on appellant's guilt should have been given, the court held that the instructions given were adequate where appellant did not request a special instruction and the trial court gave instruction that state statutes authorized closed-circuit televised testimony. The court held that confession that was typed and read to appellant who claimed he could not read or write was admissible where appellant signed each page of the confession and the voluntary statement form and officer testified that he gave appellant required warnings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child because the trial court did not abuse its discretion.

Rodriguez v. State


NO. 03-95-00742-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


953 S.W.2d 342; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3453



July 3, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0952816, HONORABLE BOB PERKINS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 331st Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which convicted appellant of felony murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(b)(3) (1994). The felony murder charge was based upon the underlying felony of deadly conduct, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.05 (1994), which was itself the act that caused the homicide.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of felony murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(b)(3) (1994). Appellant challenged his conviction, alleging that the felony murder rule had no application because the underlying felony of deadly conduct, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.05 (1994), which was used as the basis for the felony murder charge was the very act which caused the homicide. The court held that in enacting § 19.02(b)(3) the legislature exempted only manslaughter as an underlying felony for a felony murder charge. The court held that this inclusion of the manslaughter limitation excluded all other limitations. The court held that the legislature had not expressly adopted the merger doctrine. Therefore, the court held that deadly conduct could serve as the underlying felony for a felony murder charge. The court held that appellant's conviction for felony murder with the underlying felony being deadly conduct by repeatedly firing a firearm into an automobile known to be occupied which, in fact, caused the homicide was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of felony murder because the felony of deadly conduct, which served as the basis of the felony murder charge, was not statutorily exempted as an underlying offense for felony murder, and the legislature had not expressly adopted the merger rule. Thus, it was proper to use the offense of deadly conduct as the predicate offense even though this conduct caused the homicide.
