Ex parte Mallares


NO. 03-96-00529-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


953 S.W.2d 759; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3475



July 3, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 274TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-0782, HONORABLE JACK ROBISON, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 1, 1997, Previously Reported at: 944 S.W.2d 802, 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2508.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the District Court of Hays County (Texas), which denied the dismissal under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989) of appellant's prosecution for possession of the controlled substances morphine and Demerol.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was arrested for possession of morphine and Demerol, the grand jury failed to return an indictment. Under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 32.01 (1989), appellant sought to have prosecution dismissed because of the delay. The trial court denied, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed and found that a dismissal pursuant to art. 32.01 would be denied if good cause for the delay was shown. The court found good cause for the delay because the state was confronted with a short three-month court term, another district court in the county had six-month grand jury terms, and the state was ready to submit appellant's case to the next grand jury. Furthermore, the court found that the state did not have to show good cause until appellant sought dismissal under art. 32.01. In addition, the court found that the state, as a matter of policy, had not sought an indictment until the contraband was analyzed, which was held to be a prudent course of action, and found that there was no evidence showing that the state had deliberately delayed the prosecution. Finally, the court found, in addressing an argument by the state, that art. 32.01 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that denied the dismissal of appellant's prosecution for possession of controlled substances because although the state, as required by statute, had not presented an indictment against appellant prior to the next term of the court held after appellant's arrest, the state had shown good cause for the indictment's delay once appellant sought a dismissal pursuant to statute.

NO. 2-95-231-CR, NO. 2-95-233-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


950 S.W.2d 140; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3547



June 27, 1997, DELIVERED

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of State's Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 27, 199, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2666.



DISPOSITION: Appellants' point of error is overruled and the trial court's denial of habeas relief is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the denial of their petitions for habeas corpus relief by the 279th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), contending that the "Trial Court C' of Tarrant County was unconstitutional due to the manner of its creation and operation, and that the judicial assignments made to that court were done in violation of statutory authority.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were indicted by a grand jury for the offense of possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver, and filed pretrial applications for writ of habeas corpus, contending that the Tarrant County Trial Court C was unconstitutionally created and lacked the jurisdiction of a district court. The trial judge denied both applications. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed the denial of the requested relief. It held that the proper assignment of the trial judge in one district court authorized him to sit in the other district courts of the state, and that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 74.052, 74.056(a) (1988) authorized the presiding judge of the administrative region to assign judges to Court C. The court further held that the notice of assignment of attorneys given in Court C was adequate under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 74.053 (1997).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of habeas relief, and held that the trial court judge, who was properly assigned to sit in another county district court, was thus also authorized to sit in the 297th District Court C, and that the assignment of judges to that court was authorized by statute. The court further held that the notice of assignment of attorneys to cases in the court was adequate.

 

840 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Pauli v. State


NO. 14-95-01269-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3331



June 26, 1997, rendered  
June 26, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 641,253.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the revocation of his deferred adjudication by the 184th District Court, Harris County, Texas after appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child and placed on deferred adjudication probation for 10 years.


OVERVIEW: After appellant violated the conditions of his probation, he was adjudicated guilty. Appellant argued that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 § 5(b) (1994), which prohibited him from appealing such adjudication, denied him his rights of due process and equal protection. Specifically, appellant contended that article 42.12 § 5(b) denied him of his right to seek appellate review of the trial court's determination to adjudicate his guilt, whereas another defendant, who received regular probation, could have sought appellate review of the sufficiency of the state's allegations. Appellant's right to appeal was statutory and not constitutionally guaranteed; therefore, an adjudication of guilt did not violate his rights under either the United States or the Texas Constitutions. Furthermore, the court noted that a regular probationer was found guilty before being placed on probation, whereas under deferred adjudication probation, there was no finding of guilt unless the terms of probation were violated, thus, if the adjudication probationer successfully completes his probation, he will have no criminal record.


OUTCOME: Because the right to appeal was statutory and the constitution expressly authorized the legislature to regulate appeals, appellant's constitutional rights were not infringed upon, and the case was affirmed, by the Texas legislature's decision to deny appeals from a trial court's decision to adjudicate guilt after the revocation of a deferred adjudication probation.

Yu Chi Chuang v. State


NO. 14-95-00212-CR, NO. 14-95-00213-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3315



June 26, 1997, rendered  
June 26, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 559,676 & 559,677.
Yu Chi Chuang v. State, 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 325 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., Feb. 6, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction in the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, for unlawfully redeeming food stamps for which she was sentenced to three years' deferred adjudication probation. Appellant had previously plead guilty to the indictment, which was affirmed by the court, and discretionary review denied, then original postconviction application for writ of habeas corpus was granted and her judgments reversed and remanded.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled no contest to unlawfully redeeming food stamps, the trial court placed her on three years deferred adjudication probation and she sought review, arguing that the indictments were unconstitutionally vague and that she was subjected to multiple punishments. The court affirmed and held that in appellant's previous case, her challenge of the indictment was held to be nonjurisdictional, and therefore, not reviewable. Under the doctrine of the law of the case, where determinations as to questions of law have already been made on prior appeal to a court of last resort, the court held it was bound by its previous conclusion that the constitutional challenge was a nonjurisdictional issue. Further, the court held that once appellant made her no contest plea, she waived any nonjurisdictional defects occurring before the entry of the plea. The court also held that the second prosecution was permissible and did not violate double jeopardy as appellant's first conviction was set aside.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the issue of vagueness of the indictment had been previously decided in appellant's first appeal as nonjurisdictional and therefore the court would not review it. Further, the court affirmed that since appellant's first conviction had been set aside, double jeopardy was not violated by a second prosecution.

Travis Cent. Appraisal Dist. v. FM Props. Operating Co.

Hungaski v. State


No. 05-96-00185-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3295



June 25, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 5. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MA95-32333-F.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the County Criminal Court No. 5, Dallas County (Texas), for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated and contended that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash, and that the penal code provision under which he was charged was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of misdemeanor driving while intoxicated under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.04(a) (1994) (DWI statute) after a plea of nolo contendere. The court affirmed the conviction. It rejected the contention that the trial court should have quashed the information because it did not allege a culpable mental state as required under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.01 (1994). The court found that the offense of DWI never required a culpable mental state even though the DWI statute did not, at the time of the offense, specifically require a mental state or explicitly dispense with one. The court also disagreed with the contention that the DWI statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied. Appellant did not file a pretrial motion on this issue and did not obtain permission to appeal thus, the court could only consider jurisdictional issues. Appellant's challenge to the statute as applied was not jurisdictional and could not be considered as it would not render the statute void. The court noted that there was also no evidence in the record that would have permitted it to determine whether it was unconstitutional as applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated because the information was proper and the constitutional challenge was not properly before it.

Reames v. Hawthorne-Seving, Inc.


No. 05-95-01768-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


949 S.W.2d 758; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3101; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,044



June 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 14th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-3140-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant plant worker sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellees conveyer belt manufacturer and construction company pursuant to a statute of repose, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.009 (1986), in appellant's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant plant worker was injured on a conveyor belt while working at a ceramic tile plant. The workers' compensation carrier brought a suit in appellant's name against appellees conveyor belt manufacturer and construction company. It was unclear who physically installed the conveyor. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees based on Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.009 (1986), a statute of repose requiring that suits against one who constructs an improvement to real property be brought within 10 years after the construction of the improvement. On appeal the court affirmed. Based on the plant owner's intent that the conveyor be an addition to the freehold, the court held that the conveyor was an improvement as a matter of law. Finding that appellee manufacturer's relationship to the conveyor's installation was that of a general contractor, the court concluded that appellee manufacturer constructed the conveyor as an improvement. The court held that appellee construction company was entitled to summary judgment because either it played no role in installing the conveyor or, if it did install the conveyor, appellant's suit would be barred by § 16.009.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellees conveyor belt manufacturer and construction company, because it found that appellant plant worker's personal injury suit was barred by the statute of repose.

Texas Comm'n of Licensing & Regulation v. Model Search Am.


NO. 03-96-00349-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


953 S.W.2d 289; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3030



June 12, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-14409, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Cause Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Texas Commission of Licensing and Regulation, sought review of the declaratory judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), that appellee, a model search company, was not required to obtain a certificate of registration under the Texas Talent Agency Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 5221a-0. 911 (Supp. 1997), and that the Act was inapplicable to appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a company that provided training and advice to aspiring models for a fee, filed suit against appellant, the Texas Commission of Licensing and Regulation, seeking a declaratory judgment that it was not required to obtain a certificate of registration and that rules regulating talent agencies under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 5221a-9, 9100, and Tex. Admin. Code § 78.20(b) were inapplicable. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee, and appellant sought review. The court reversed the trial court judgment and dismissed the action. It held that the district court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act (Act), Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.004, because the Act did not in itself create subject matter jurisdiction in the district court to review an otherwise non-reviewable agency action. The court further held that the district court lacked jurisdiction because appellant had not attempted to enforce against appellee any consequences of operating a talent agency without a certificate of registration, but had merely offered the opinion that appellee was obligated to obtain the certificate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered the case dismissed, holding that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act to review an otherwise non-reviewable agency action, and further that appellant, in expressing an opinion on the issue of whether registration was required, had undertaken no official agency action that could be reviewed by the court.

 

846 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Estep v. State


No. 05-94-00584-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3056



June 12, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 9. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB93-19323-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the County Criminal Court No. 9, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted and sentenced him, upon a jury verdict, for telephone harassment in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(2) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was engaged to a girl and conceived a child with her. The relationship ended, and the girl accused defendant of abusing their daughter. Defendant's parental rights were terminated and, according to the girl, defendant telephoned her and threatened to kill both her and the child. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for telephone harassment. Defendant appealed, contending the harassment statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(2) (1997), was unconstitutionally void for vagueness and overbreadth. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to quash the information because defendant's statement was constitutionally protected speech, as it could be said in a context where it did not constitute a threat under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07. The reviewing court stated that U.S. Const. amend. I did not protect threats. The reviewing court took defendant's statement in context and found that the statement was not constitutionally protected. Therefore, the court concluded that defendant's statement was a true threat, and the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to quash the information. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of telephone harassment was affirmed, as the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to quash the information. When defendant's statement threatening to kill his ex-fiancee and her daughter was taken in context, the court found the statement was not constitutionally protected as free speech.

Stevenson v. State


NO. 14-96-00213-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3070



June 12, 1997, rendered  
June 12, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 670665.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which, based upon the state's motion to adjudicate appellant's guilt on a charge of credit card abuse, adjudicated appellant guilty and sentenced appellant to a term of imprisonment pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 32.31, 12.34 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a plea of guilty to the offense of credit card abuse. The lower court found that the evidence substantiated appellant's guilt, and placed appellant on deferred adjudication probation. The state subsequently filed a motion to adjudicate guilt. The lower court adjudicated appellant's guilt and assessed punishment at six years confinement pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.34 (1974). Appellant contended that the lower court erred in not sentencing him under the new penal code, and that his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the federal and state constitutions. The appellate court affirmed the sentence, holding that because the legislature specifically included a savings provision clause within 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 3586 and 3714, the law in effect at the time appellant's offense was committed governed the disposition of his case. The appellate court applied a substantial deference standard and determined that because appellant's sentence was well within the statutory provision for the offense committed, the punishment did not offend either the Texas or the United States Constitution's prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The lower court's assessment of appellant's sentence for credit card abuse was affirmed. The appellate court held that the lower court properly applied the proper savings provision clause and that, because appellant's sentence was well within the statutory provision for the offense committed, his sentence was not unconstitutional.

In re T.L.C.


NO. 14-95-00829-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


948 S.W.2d 41; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3075



June 12, 1997, rendered  
June 12, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 315th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89044.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought reversal of an order from the 315th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which transferred his prosecution for aggravated robbery to the adult division.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile challenged a juvenile judge's ordering transferring his aggravated robbery prosecution to the adult division. Appellant argued that the juvenile judge erred when he ordered his case transferred to the adult division based on an inadequate statement of reasons, and when he based his transfer decision on an involuntary and unconstitutionally acquired custodial statement. The court rejected both arguments and affirmed. As to the juvenile judge's rationale for transfer, the court held that the judge had properly identified all required factors and had articulated his rationale for transfer. The mere fact that his transfer order parroted the language of the transfer statute was not erroneous. As to appellant's custodial statement, the court opined that even if that statement would be inadmissible at appellant's trial, it was admissible at his transfer hearing because it was the sort of evidence which would be admissible before a grand jury.


OUTCOME: The order transferring appellant juvenile's case from the juvenile court was affirmed. The juvenile judge's stated rationale for transfer was sufficient, even if it merely tracked the language of the transfer statute, and there was nothing improper in the juvenile judge's considering what appellant contended was inadmissible evidence in the course of making his decision as to transfer.

City of Dallas v. Nickels & Dimes


No. 05-95-01507-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2870



May 30, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 101st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-12881-E.



DISPOSITION: Appellees' crosspoint overruled. Trial court's judgment reversed and rendered dismissing appellees' causes of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and police chief, challenged the order of the 101st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which declared that appellants improperly interpreted the penal code's anti-gambling statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4) (1997), and issued an injunction enforcing their interpretation of the statute against appellees, amusement arcades.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, amusement arcades, were raided because appellants, city and police chief, interpreted the penal code as not permitting the awarding of a prize using tokens worth more than five dollars. Appellees sought a declaration that appellants improperly interpreted the penal code's anti-gambling statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4) (1997), and issued an injunction enforcing their interpretation of the statute. The trial court declared that appellants unconstitutionally applied the statute to appellees and enjoined enforcement. The court reversed the judgment and held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant any injunction enjoining the enforcement of a penal statute. The court held that because the trial court did not find that the statute was unconstitutional or otherwise void, it lacked jurisdiction to declare appellants' interpretation of the relevant portions of the statute incorrect and unenforceable and to enjoin appellants from enforcing the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaration and voided the injunction issued in favor of appellees, amusement arcades, against appellants, city and police chief. Because the trial court did not find that the statute was unconstitutional or otherwise void, it lacked jurisdiction to declare appellants' interpretation of the relevant portions of the statute incorrect and unenforceable and to enjoin appellants from enforcing the statute.

Bochas v. State


NUMBER 13-96-275-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


951 S.W.2d 64; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2865



May 29, 1997, delivered  
May 29, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 1997. Rehearing Denied July 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 357th District Court of Cameron County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged forfeiture proceedings in the 357th District Court of Cameron County (Texas) regarding a home where 1,500 pounds of marijuana were discovered by the police, title to which residence was forfeited to the State of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant son's wife was convicted for possession of 1,500 pounds of marijuana found in a home. At the time of the warrant execution, title to the real property was vested in a third party, but utility services for the home were obtained by appellant mother, who did not live in the home. Essentially contemporaneously with the trial for possession of the marijuana found in the home, title was transferred to appellant. The state filed a petition for forfeiture pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 59, naming appellant mother, appellant son, and third party owner, who waived interest in the property, as defendants. A bench trial resulted in forfeiture. The court affirmed the judgment on the basis that appellants failed to establish their innocent owner defense, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. 59.02(c), as appellant mother did not prove her ownership interest in the property arose before date of discovery of the marijuana, there was no written contract of sale or evidence of parol sale as the testimony of third party owner did not corroborate the authenticity of receipts for payment of consideration, and there was no evidence that permission had been obtained to make repairs to the property.


OUTCOME: The judgment of forfeiture was affirmed because appellants' innocent owner defense was not conclusively established and was never properly raised in the trial court. As some evidence supported the trial court's failure to find that appellants were innocent owners, in light of the entire record, the determination was not manifestly unjust.

Pruitt v. State


NO. 14-95-01248-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2796



May 29, 1997, rendered  
May 29, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 678,422.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas, convicting him of capital murder. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in granting the state's challenge for cause to certain veniremen, commenting on the weight of the evidence, and in overruling appellant's motion to set aside the indictment.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of the offense of capital murder. The court assessed his punishment at confinement for life, and appellant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court erred in granting the state's challenge for cause to certain veniremen, commenting on the weight of the evidence, and in overruling appellant's motion to set aside the indictment. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that appellant could not challenge the ruling regarding the veniremen excused for cause because he had failed to object at the time they were excused. The court also held that appellant had waived any error regarding the trial court's comment on the evidence because he made no objection to the judge's response. Finally, the court held that appellant's motion to set aside the indictment was properly denied because a mandatory life sentence was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder because appellant failed to object when a venireman was excused for cause and thus could not challenge that ruling on appeal, and appellant waived his right to contest the trial judge's comment on the evidence by failing to object at trial.

Schleuter v. City of Fort Worth


NO. 2-96-028-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


947 S.W.2d 920; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2881



May 29, 1997, DELIVERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 96TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, sports bar and owners, sought review of an order from the 96th District Court of Tarrant (Texas) that issued a permanent injunction to prevent them from operating a "sports bar" that featured exposed female dancers. The trial court found that operation of the "sports bar" violated appellee City of Fort Worth's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The issue in this appeal from the permanent injunction was whether the trial court erred in upholding the applicable provisions of the Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance (CZO) against claims that the definition of nudity in the ordinance violated the Texas Equal Rights Amendment. Appellants, sports bar and owners, claimed that the CZO restrictions were unconstitutional on first amendment grounds. On appeal, the court held that the CZO restriction on sexually oriented businesses was content-neutral because the city's predominant concern in passing the ordinance was to limit the negative secondary effects of sexually oriented businesses. It was narrowly tailored because it effectively promoted the city's stated interest. It provided alternative channels for communication because appellants had not proved that there were an insufficient number of available sites that did not have legal or physical barriers to development. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment and permanent injunction of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against appellants, sports bar and owners. The court ruled in favor of appellee City of Forth Worth, holding that its comprehensive zoning ordinance's time, place, and manner restrictions passed constitutional muster because it was content-neutral, narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest, and left open ample alternative avenues of communication.

Ex parte Elliott


NO. 2-96-229-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


950 S.W.2d 714; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4175



May 22, 1997, DELIVERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 24, 1997. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 4 OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 4, Tarrant County (Texas), which denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus following the court's modification of the terms of bond related to charges against appellant of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After being arrested for driving while intoxicated (DWI), appellant argued that the trial court's decision to require the installation of an interlock device on appellant's vehicle as a condition of bond was improper. Appellant also contended that the statute authorizing the imposition of such a condition was unconstitutional. The court first held that the trial court, after finding that appellant had been previously convicted of DWI and that installation of the interlock device was in the best interests of justice, was required to order installation of the interlock device, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 17.441 (1997). Because the trial court did not have the inherent power to ignore the statute's express provisions, the court held the trial court had not abused its discretion in complying with the statute. The court then held that requiring the installation of the interlock device pursuant to art. 17.441 served a narrow government purpose and was less severe a punishment than revocation of a driver's license, which the court noted had previously been upheld as a constitutionally valid punishment. Thus, the court held that art. 17.441 was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellant's motion for a writ of habeas corpus because the modification of the terms of appellant's bond to mandate the imposition of an interlock device on appellant's car was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion, and the statute allowing for such a modification was constitutionally valid.

Limon v. State


NO. 03-96-00468-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


947 S.W.2d 620; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2674



May 22, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-11327, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Modified and, as Modified, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, eleven bar owners, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), which determined that the "good conduct" bond requirements of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 11.11 and 61.13 (Supp. 1997) were constitutional, and denied appellants' request for a declaratory judgment declaring the sections unconstitutional and enjoining their enforcement by theTexas Alcoholic Beverage Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, eleven bar owners, sought a judgment declaring that the recently enacted "good conduct" bond requirements of the Texas Alcoholic Beverage Code, Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 11.11 and 61.13 (Supp. 1997) were unconstitutional and enjoining their enforcement by the Alcoholic Beverage Commission. The trial court determined §§ 11.11 and 61.13 were constitutional and denied the requested relief. Appellants sought review. As a preliminary matter, the court held that appellants had standing to challenge only the actual imposition of the bonds (addressed in §§ 11.11(a) and 61.31(a)) but not their forfeiture (addressed in §§ 11.11(b) and 61.31(b)), and modified the trial court's judgment to address only §§ 11.11(a) and 61.31(a). The court affirmed the judgment as modified, holding that appellants were not entitled to due process of law because the alcohol beverage permit was merely a privilege. Appellants had no constitutionally protected interest in obtaining it. The court held that the state had a rational basis for making a distinction between businesses licensed for more and less than three years and for increases in the bond amount depending on the business's location.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment determining that the "good conduct" bond requirements of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 11.11 and 61.13 (Supp. 1997) were constitutional, holding that §§ 11.11(a) and 61.13(a) did not violate the due course of law and equal protection clauses of the Texas Constitution. The court also held that appellants did not have standing to challenge the statute as it related to forfeiture of the bond upon a code violation.

Northwest Indep. Sch. Dist. v. City of Fort Worth


NO. 03-96-00397-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2679



May 22, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 9604583, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district challenged the order of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas) that dismissed appellant's lawsuit against appellees, city, public corporation, private corporations, and public officials, challenging the constitutionality of the application of an ad valorem tax exemption to property owned by a public corporation for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellee public corporation was created to purchase property owned by appellee private corporation. Appellee public corporation leased the property back to appellee private corporation. Public property is exempt from ad valorem taxation. Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.11 (1992); Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5190.6, § 4B(k) (1997). The parties anticipated application of a tax exemption to the property. Appellant school district filed suit to prevent the application of a tax exemption to the property. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the action because the case presented no justiciable controversy. According to the record, the county appraisal district, which is in charge of initially determining the applicability of a tax exemption, had not considered applying a tax exemption to the property. The court found that there was no indication that the appraisal district intended to apply an exemption to the property. The court held that it was forbidden to issue advisory opinions and could not issue an opinion in this case because whether the appraisal district would in fact apply a tax exemption depended upon hypothetical, contingent facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed the case. The case presented no justiciable controversy because the county appraisal district had not determined that the property was tax-exempt and there was no indication that the appraisal district intended to apply a tax exemption to the property.

 

858 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Loving v. State


NO. 03-95-00343-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


947 S.W.2d 615; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2690



May 22, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0945017. HONORABLE TOM BLACKWELL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas) for aggravated robbery, asserting that the trial court erred in admitting in evidence before the jury a witness's in-court identification of appellant because that identification was tainted by an impermissibly suggestive pretrial identification procedure and by improperly submitting an Allen charge to the jury during its deliberations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed his conviction for aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon, claiming that the trial court erred in admitting a witness's in-court identification into evidence and by submitting an Allen charge to a jury that was not deadlocked. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that the witness's pre-trial, inadvertent viewing of a copy of appellant's photograph was not shown clearly and convincingly to have been impermissibly suggestive. The witness's in-court identification of appellant was properly admitted into evidence, and therefore, admission of the in-court identification into evidence did not violate appellant's federal due process rights or state due course of law rights. The court also held that the trial court did not err in giving the Allen charge to the jury before it indicated it was unable to reach a verdict and deadlocked. The Allen charge did not deprive defendant of federal due process, and the Allen charge did not deprive defendant of his state due course of law rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the trial court correctly ruled that the in-court identification of the appellant was reliable and not the result of an improperly suggestive pre-trial procedure, and that the Allen charge was not premature, and did not violate appellant's federal due process rights or state due course of law rights.

Graff v. Whittle


No. 06-96-00056-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


947 S.W.2d 629; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2799


March 11, 1997, Submitted  
May 22, 1997, Decided  
May 22, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 6th Judicial District Court. Red River County, Texas. Trial Court No. 134-CV-5-93.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged an order from the 6th Judicial District Court, Red River County (Texas), which declared that a portion of appellant's property was a public road by implied dedication and that appellee adjacent landowners had an easement over the road. Appellant alleged inconsistent holdings, an error in a Batson challenge, insufficient evidence, and an erroneous finding on his counterclaim for damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellee adjacent landowners brought a successful declaratory judgment action against appellant landowner. The trial court declared that a strip of property on appellant's property was a public road and that appellees had an easement in the road. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that it would have been inconsistent for the trial court to find that the property was both a public road by implied dedication and an easement. The court held that the property was a public road and that the easement references were only an alternative determination in the event an appellate court did not uphold the public road determination. Secondly, the court held that the trial court's Batson ruling on appellees' peremptory challenge was deemed correct, even though there were no findings of fact or conclusions of law. Third, there was legally sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding of a public road, and the finding was neither clearly wrong nor unjust. Fourth, the determination that appellees had established that the property was a public road defeated appellant's counterclaims for damages for its use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the inconsistent holdings in favor of appellee adjacent landowners were alternative determinations. The trial court's ruling on the Batson challenge was presumed correct. The jury's findings were supported by legally sufficient evidence. Finally, the public road determination prevailed over appellant landowner's counterclaims for damages.

Bath v. State


NUMBER 13-94-460-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


951 S.W.2d 11; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2704



May 22, 1997, delivered  
May 22, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 14, 1997. Rehearing Denied August 14, 1997.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 01/07/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Bath v. Texas, 525 U.S. 829, 119 S. Ct. 80, 142 L. Ed. 2d 62, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5014 (1998)
Writ of mandamus denied In re Jaime Gonzalez Bath, 2015 Tex. App. LEXIS 3154 (Tex. App. Corpus Christi, Apr. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 28th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which convicted appellant of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(7)(A) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(7)(A) (1994), appellant was convicted of capital murder. The court affirmed and held that with direct evidence of appellant's guilt, the court could not hold that the verdict was contrary to the great weight of the evidence. There was sufficient evidence to show the identities of the victims. It was within the discretion of the judge to determine the credibility of witnesses when there was conflicting evidence in relation to alleged jury misconduct and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for new trial. The trial court's sustaining of state's objection of questions posed to a juror at hearing for a new trial was improper but constituted harmless error because it was the lack of diligence on the part of appellant's counsel that was responsible. No error occurred in relation to the vicinage provision of the Sixth Amendment in the transfer of appellant's case. The court held that the trial court erred by conducting voir dire and excusing veniremen in the absence of appellant, violating appellant's rights under the U.S. and Texas constitutions, but found that appellant was not harmed by his absence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder and found that there was sufficient evidence to show the identities of the victims and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining the credibility of witnesses regarding possible jury misconduct. The court held that although the trial court erred in conducting voir dire in the absence of defendant, it was harmless error.

Harrison v. State


No. 04-96-00697-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2665



May 21, 1997, Delivered  
May 21, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: 175th District Court of Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 93-CR-6043. Honorable Mary Roman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED FOR LACK OF JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 175th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), to revoke deferred adjudication of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child to which he had pleaded nolo contendere. Appellant did not obtain permission to appeal from the trial court as required by Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) and filed a general notice of appeal, contending that Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) violated due process.


OVERVIEW: The court dismissed an appeal of the trial court's decision to revoke deferred adjudication of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child to which appellant had pleaded nolo contendere for lack of jurisdiction. Appellant did not obtain the trial court's permission to appeal and instead filed a general notice of appeal complaining of a nonjurisdictional error. The court held that Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) bars an appeal by general notice of appeal from a plea-bargained conviction based on nonjurisdictional errors. As to appellant's contention that Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) violated due process because it made his ability to appeal contingent upon court approval, the court held that there was no constitutional infringement because the right of appeal is not of constitutional dimension. The court held further that appellant's reference to due process requirements in probation revocation hearings did not address his contention that Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) was unconstitutional and that a case holding that a defendant had a right to raise a complaint on appeal that a negotiated plea was unknowing or involuntary was inapposite where those were not the facts of appellant's case.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed an appeal of the trial court's decision to revoke deferred adjudication of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child to which appellant had pleaded nolo contendere. The court held that appellant violated a rule barring appeals by general notice from a plea-bargained conviction based on nonjurisdictional defects and that appellant's constitutional challenge of the rule was without merit.

 

862 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co. v. Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n


NO. 03-96-00317-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


945 S.W.2d 886; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2576



May 15, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-15855, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Vacated and Cause Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review from a District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas) judgment denying requested relief in appellant's suit against appellees workers, state workers' compensation commission, commission executive director, and compensation fund under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 409.023(a), 410.032, 410.169, 410.205.


OVERVIEW: After appellee state workers' compensation commission ordered appellant insurer to pay workers' compensation benefits to appellee workers, appellant filed suit against appellees, workers, state workers' compensation commission, commission executive director, and compensation fund, challenging the constitutionality of the immediate payment and reimbursement scheme of the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 409.023(a), 410.032, 410.169, 410.205. The lower court denied the relief sought, and appellant sought review. The court sua sponte held that the lower court lacked subject-matter jurisdiction because appellant had failed to establish imminent harm upon application of the statute, particularly where the record did not show any modification or reversal, or likelihood of such, of the adverse decisions upon which any reimbursement would be predicated. Thus, the court found that appellant was asking for an advisory opinion, which the lower court had no jurisdiction to render even under the declaratory judgment and injunctive relief statutes.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's judgment and dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction, holding that because appellant had failed to establish imminent harm upon application of the challenged statute, appellant requested an impermissible advisory opinion from the lower court.

 

863 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gerlacher v. Board of Regents of the Univ. of Houston Sys.


NO. 14-95-00684-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2645



May 15, 1997, rendered  
May 15, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-53566.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student sought review of a decision of the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee university, in appellant's suit claiming a refund of tuition because she was entitled to classification as a resident for tuition purposes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant student attended appellee university in Texas. She was classified as a nonresident student, which required her to pay higher tuition. Appellant brought suit against appellee for a refund of the difference between the resident and nonresident rates. The parties filed cross motions for summary judgment, and the trial court granted appellee's motion and denied appellant's motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that appellant's intent to establish a permanent home in Texas did not establish a 12-month residence in Texas for purposes of 19 Tex. Admin. Code § 21.22 (1994), because appellant did not actually reside in Texas for the 12 months preceding her enrollment. The court held that in light of the presumption of nonresidence in 19 Tex. Admin. Code § 21.23 (1994), appellee's decision not to reclassify appellant, despite appellant's having acquired a homestead and other indicia of residency, was rational and did not violate appellant's right to due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to appellee university, in appellant student's suit claiming a refund of tuition on the ground that she was entitled to classification as a resident. Appellant had not demonstrated that she met a 12-month residency requirement or that she overcame the statutory presumption that she was not a resident.

Dallas Cent. Appraisal Dist. v. Park Stemmons


No. 05-95-00691-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


948 S.W.2d 11; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2555



May 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 298th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-01734-M.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4269.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee property owners filed a motion for rehearing of the court's previous opinion regarding the challenge by appellants, appraisal district and review board, and appellees, to the judgment entered in the 298th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which granted summary judgment for appellees and ordered appellant review board to conduct an administrative hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners filed suit to compel appellants, appraisal district and review board, to conduct a hearing pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 25.25(d) to correct what appellees alleged were excessive 1993 appraisal values on their recently purchased properties. Both appellees and appellants filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court entered summary judgment for appellees and ordered appellant review board to conduct a hearing. The parties challenged. The court rendered an opinion, and appellees moved for a rehearing. The court granted appellees' motion and substituted this opinion for its original one. The court held that appellees did not have standing under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 25.25 to challenged the 1993 appraisal values because the previous owners had already challenged the appraisals and entered into a settlement agreement with appellants. The court further held that appellees were not denied procedural due process because the previous owners' due process satisfied appellees' right to due process. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered the judgment that the trial court should have rendered, that appellees take nothing.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellee property owners' motion for rehearing, vacated its original judgment, and substituted with its revised opinion. Upon rehearing, the court reversed the trial court's summary judgment for appellees and rendered a judgment that appellees take nothing because the previous owners of appellees' properties had already challenged the appraisal values. Therefore, appellees did not have standing to challenge same.

Watt v. State


NO. 07-95-0164-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2543



May 12, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE CRIMINAL COUNTY COURT NO. 8 OF DALLAS COUNTY; NO. MB94-40801-J; HONORABLE JOHN HENDRIK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated from the Criminal County Court No. 8 of Dallas County (Texas), arguing that the trial court erred in failing to suppress evidence gained as the result of an unlawful arrest and of his refusal to take a breath test. Defendant also argued that it was error to refuse to allow evidence of a negative finding in an administrative proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed. Defendant had moved to suppress the evidence gained from the traffic stop on the theory that his arrest was pursuant to an unconstitutionally vague statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 545.060(a) (1977). The court found that the officer had probable cause for a warrantless arrest for a traffic offense. The evidence discovered as a result of the bona fide arrest for the traffic offense was admissible in the prosecution for the offense of driving while intoxicated. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence of his refusal to take a breath test, arguing the trial court erred in refusing to allow the admission of testimony as to the negative finding in an administrative hearing. The court held that collateral estoppel did not bar reconsideration of the administrative law judge's ruling. Finally, defendant had made a motion in limine to conduct voir dire of an expert witness for underlying facts of an expert opinion, outside the jury's presence. It was granted, except as to nystagmus. Although trial court error, the court found it made no contribution to defendant's conviction or punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The arresting officer had probable cause to conduct a warrantless search subsequent to the traffic offense. The evidence discovered was admissible for the offense. Collateral estoppel did not bar reconsideration of the administrative judge's ruling. Although the trial court erred in not allowing voir dire of an expert to be held outside the jury's presence, it was harmless error.

Huntress v. McGrath


NO. 2-97-103-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


946 S.W.2d 480; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2523



May 8, 1997, DELIVERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Relators' Petition for Writ of Mandamus Conditionally Granted May 8, 1997.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus conditionally granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator city aldermen sought a writ of mandamus against respondent judge of the district court (Texas), who enjoined proceedings conducted by relators, pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002, for removal of a mayor from office in a general-law municipality.


OVERVIEW: One of relator city aldermen filed a complaint seeking to remove a mayor from office in a general-law municipality pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002. The mayor filed suit, claiming that the action was improper and unconstitutional. Respondent judge of the district court issued a temporary restraining order, which enjoined relators from proceeding with a hearing on the complaint. Relators filed mandamus proceedings with the appellate court, which granted leave to file a mandamus petition and stayed respondent's orders. After a hearing on the removal complaint, a relator signed a judgment removing the mayor. The mayor sought a second temporary restraining order in the trial court cause, which respondent granted, enjoining the enforcement of the removal. The appellate court stayed respondent's order while it considered the mandamus petition. The appellate court then conditionally granted relators' petition for writ of mandamus, holding that the legislature had provided an administrative procedure for removal of the mayor, vested by statute in relators, and that respondent had abused his discretion in enjoining the operation of the statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted a writ of mandamus to relator city aldermen against respondent judge of the district court, who had enjoined proceedings conducted by relators to remove a mayor from office, because respondent's enjoining of the statutorily prescribed scheme for removal from office was an abuse of discretion.

 

867 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


University of Texas Sys. v. Courtney


NO. 2-94-201-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


946 S.W.2d 464; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2372



May 1, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 12, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 48TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.

This Opinion Substituted, on Overrule of Appellee/Cross-Appellant's Motion For Rehearing, for Withdrawn Opinion of August 29, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3892.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee sought rehearing on the court's order reversing a judgment in his favor.


OVERVIEW: After his position as a lecturer was not renewed by appellants, appellee sued for breach of contract, detrimental reliance, and violations of federal and state due process. The jury found in appellee's favor and the trial court entered judgment for appellee. The court reversed. Appellant university was entitled to sovereign immunity on appellee's breach of contract claim. There was no such cause of action for detrimental reliance. Additionally, nothing in the Texas Constitution provided for a cause of action for monetary damages for unconstitutional conduct. Appellee university could not be sued under 42 U.S.C.S § 1983 because it was not a person under the statute. As for appellant individual, while he was not entitled to immunity on appellee's state claims where he did not act within the scope of his authority, he was nonetheless entitled to judgment in his favor. Appellee had no cause of action for monetary damages for a constitutional violation, he failed to challenge appellant individual's right to immunity under federal law, and no cause of action for detrimental reliance existed.


OUTCOME: Appellee's motion for rehearing was denied and judgment in appellee's favor was reversed because appellant university was entitled to sovereign immunity and appellant individual could not be held individually liable on appellee's claims.

Haro v. State


No. 11-96-058-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


946 S.W.2d 120; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2386



May 1, 1997, Decided  
May 1, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 118th District Court of Howard County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for sexual assault of a child from the 118th District Court of Howard County (Texas), alleging that the victim did not comply with either the former or amended outcry and corroboration statutes, that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.07 (1997) was unconstitutional as applied to him, that error occurred when the jury was not instructed on art. 38.07, and that the state's closing argument was improper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of sexual assault of a child. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction for several reasons. First, because the victim was under the age of 14 when appellant assaulted her, it was not necessary to corroborate her testimony nor for her to have made an outcry under Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 38.07 (1983) or as amended under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.07 (1997). The court found more than sufficient support in the record that the sexual assaults occurred when the victim was 12 and 13 years of age. Second, because the victim was under 14 years of age when she was sexually assaulted, the amendment of art. 38.07 did not affect her. Third, because the record supported a finding that the victim was under 14 years of age the trial court did not err by not giving an instruction on art. 38.07. The court noted that even if error occurred, it was not egregious after examining the entire jury charge, the evidence, the arguments of counsel, and other relevant information. Fourth, the state's remarks were supported by the record and were proper jury argument regardless of the fact that appellant had failed to preserve the issue for appeal.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed for several reasons. First, because the victim was under 14 years of age when she was assaulted, the statute on outcry or corroboration was inapplicable. Second, because sufficient evidence showed the victim was less than 14 years of age, the trial court did not err by failing to give an instruction on outcry. Fourth, appellant's objection to the state's remarks was not preserved for appeal.

De La Vega v. Taco Cabana


Appeal No. 04-94-00835-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2282



April 30, 1997, Delivered  
April 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the 37th Judicial District Court of Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 92-CI-15602. Honorable Carol R. Haberman, Judge Presiding. 1 


1 Although the Hon. Carol R. Haberman signed the judgment from which this appeal is taken, the Hon. David A. Berchelmann, Jr. presided over the trial and the hearing on the affidavit of indigency and signed the order entered after that hearing.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a ruling of the 37th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant on her personal injury claim against appellee employer and held that because appellant's appeal was frivolous, appellant was not entitled to a free statement of facts under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.003 (1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee filed an action against appellee employer in which appellant sought to recover damages for work-related injuries. Appellant claimed negligence in allowing an unsafe work environment. The trial court jury found that appellee was not negligent, and the trial court entered a take-nothing judgment against appellant. Appellant perfected her right to appeal by filing an affidavit of indigency, but the trial court ruled that appellant's challenge was frivolous and, therefore, that appellant was not entitled to a free statement of facts under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.003 (1997). Appellant challenged the trial court's ruling, which denied her appeal. She claimed that § 13.003 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it found that appellant's appeal was frivolous, and that § 13.003 was constitutional where the state's interest in conserving resources outweighed an indigent appellant's rights to expend those resources on a meritless appeal. The court held that § 13.003 was not overly vague where it satisfied the reasonable certainty requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant employee on her personal injury claim against appellee employer and held that because appellant's appeal was frivolous, appellant was not entitled to a free statement of facts. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court and overruled appellant's claims that the statute at issue was unconstitutional.

Crider v. Cox


NO. 12-95-00281-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


960 S.W.2d 703; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2425



April 30, 1997, delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied September 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF ANDERSON COUNTY, TEXAS. Clayton, Hon. Joe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the denial of his petition for writ of mandamus and motion for summary judgment by the Third Judicial District Court of Anderson County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney sought mandamus to require appellee county auditor to pay him for his legal services in defending his uncle, a county judge. Appellant claimed the trial court erred in denying his petition for mandamus and his motion for summary judgment. The court held that a writ of mandamus was not available because appellee, in deciding whether or not to approve appellant's claim, had to evaluate numerous complicated, unresolved issues concerning the legality of the claim, making her decision a discretionary, not mandatory act. Additionally, the court noted that the existence of disputed facts precluded mandamus. With respect to appellant's motion for summary judgment, the court held that due to its holding on the issue of mandamus and the paucity of appellant's summary judgment evidence, he was not entitled to summary judgment. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellant attorney's petition for writ of mandamus and motion for summary judgment because appellee county auditor's action in deciding not to pay for his services was a discretionary act not subject to mandamus relief and the evidence did not support an award of summary judgment.

White v. Young


NO. 14-96-879-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2794



April 29, 1997, rendered  
May 29, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 12th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 19,452.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prison inmate sought review from a 12th District Court, Walker County (Texas) judgment dismissing his suit against appellees prison officials for wrongful confiscation of personal property pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 14.005, arguing, among other things, that the statute used to dismiss was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prison inmate filed suit under the Texas Deceptive Trade Practices Act and U.S. Const. amend. V, VI, XIII, XIV against appellees prison officials for wrongful confiscation of personal property. The lower court dismissed pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 14.005, and appellant sought review, arguing that the dismissal was erroneous, that the statute used to dismiss was unconstitutional, and that the state department of criminal justice's grievance system was not certified as required under Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 500.08. The court held that even under the most lenient reckoning appellant had failed to file in timely fashion. Further, the court found that because there was no fundamental error the constitutional challenge raised by appellant for the first time on appeal was waived. Finally, the court held that appellant's mere assertions were insufficient to raise his claim that the state's grievance system was not certified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that appellant's constitutional challenge was waived because it was raised for the first time on review, and finding that appellant's untimely appeal also failed to sufficiently raise his claim to justify granting relief.

Hyde v. State


NO. 14-94-00794-CR, NO. 14-94-00840-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2117



April 24, 1997, rendered  
April 24, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number Eight. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 9406694 & 9406698.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their convictions from the County Criminal Court, Harris County (Texas) for knowingly carrying a firearm while performing duties as a security officer without being commissioned as a security officer, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb), §§ 13(a), 19(a)(1)-(2) (1995). Appellants alleged that the trial court erred in overruling appellants' objection to prosecutor's closing statement.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review of their convictions for knowingly carrying a firearm while performing duties as a security officer without being commissioned as a security officer in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb), §§ 13(a), 19(a)(1)-(2) (1995). Appellants contended that the trial court erred in overruling their objection when the prosecutor referred to matters outside the record during her final argument in the guilt/innocence stage of the proceedings. The court reversed and held that the trial court erred in overruling appellants' objection to the prosecutor's closing argument. The court held that the prosecutor's references to facts that were neither in evidence, nor inferable from the evidence were improper and outside the parameters of proper jury argument. Such a misstatement of the evidence could only have confused and prejudiced the jury's deliberation, because a juror would have most likely placed a significant amount of weight on this error. Because the statement prejudiced the decision-making process of the jury, the court concluded that appellants were denied a fair trial.


OUTCOME: Appellants' convictions for knowingly carrying a firearm while performing duties as a security officer without being commissioned as a security officer were reversed because the prosecutor's referral to matters outside the record during her final argument in the guilt/innocence stage of the proceedings prejudiced the decision-making process of the jury, and denied appellants a fair trial.

Smith v. State


No. 10-95-036-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


959 S.W.2d 1; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2373



April 23, 1997, delivered  
April 23, 1997, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From the 361st District Court. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court # 23,052-361.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university vice-president challenged his conviction from the 361st District Court, Brazos County (Texas), of the offense of solicitation of a gift by a public servant in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.08(d), contending inter alia that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of the ethical policies of the university and other organizations, allowing conviction on a theory of solicitation by implication.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant university vice-president of the offense of solicitation of a gift by a public servant in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.08(d). In 1990, appellant and a contractor entered into a contract for the operation of the university's bookstore. When the parties discussed the signing of the original contract in 1990, appellant asked whether his wife could join him for the trip to New York. Prior to trips in 1991 and 1992, appellant advised the contractor's officials that his wife would be joining him. On appeal of his conviction, appellant contended inter alia that the trial court erred in admitting evidence regarding the university's ethical policies on solicitation and spousal travel. He argued that the admission of this evidence confused the issues because it allowed the jury to convict him because he violated policy rather than the law. The court held that the solicitation policy did not unduly distract the jury. Thus, the court could not say that the lower court's decision to allow the recitation of the policy was outside the zone of reasonable disagreement. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant university vice-president for the offense of solicitation of a gift by a public servant, because while the trial court erred in admitting evidence regarding the university's ethical policies on solicitation and spousal travel, this did not unduly distract the jury.

Darby v. State


NO. 09-95-246 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2408


January 3, 1997, Submitted  
April 23, 1997, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Court No. 60903.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Jefferson County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault, where appellant challenged the constitutionality of Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 412, as applied, and also contended that the trial court erred by failing to grant his motion for mistrial and by improperly admitting certain evidence concerning his parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of his 12-year old daughter. On review, the court affirmed the conviction. The court limited appellant's constitutional challenge of Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 412, to an analysis of appellant's confrontation rights under U. S. Const. amend VI, and noted that appellant was not denied the opportunity to cross-examine the victim, because no evidence of the victim's sexual conduct was presented to the trial court and because appellant was not prevented from questioning the victim as to any material fact or element of the alleged offense. The court also ruled that a mistrial was not warranted, because the error created by the prosecution's outside the record argument was cured by the trial court's instruction to the jury to disregard and because the argument was not improper or extreme. The court also held that evidence of appellant's relinquished parental rights was admissible, because it was relevant to the case and because appellant waived his objection to any error by not invoking the trial court's duty to weigh the probative value of the testimony against its prejudicial effect, appellant waived error under Rule 403.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant accused's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because the court found: that appellant's constitutional confrontation rights were not violated, that the prosecution's outside the record argument was cured by the trial court's instruction to disregard, and that evidence concerning appellant's parental rights was admissible because it was relevant to the issue of whether he sexually abused his daughter.
