Harris County v. Hermann Hosp.


No. 11-95-074-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


943 S.W.2d 547; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2071



April 17, 1997, Decided  
April 17, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 234th District Court of Harris County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the order of the 234th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 104.002 (1997) for medical expenses incurred by a prisoner who was being guarded by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee hospital filed suit against appellant county under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 104.002 (1997) for medical expenses incurred by a prisoner who was being guarded by appellant. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and held that the trial court did not err in its construction of art. 104.002 and that the county was liable for the prisoner's medical expenses. The court held that there were no genuine issues of material fact concerning the prisoner's residency, his indigence, and appellee's compliance with the notification provisions of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 61.032. The court held that Tex. Const. art. III, §§ 51, 52 did not apply because it was a transfer of public funds for a public purpose. The court held that imposing liability on appellant did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 53 because there was no extra fee granted to appellee nor was there any agreement made without authority of law. The court held that the statutory cap of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 61.035 did not apply because the prisoner was not an eligible county resident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital against appellant county for medical expenses incurred by a prisoner who was being guarded by appellant. There were no genuine issues of material fact concerning the prisoner's residency, his indigence, and appellee's compliance with the notification provisions. Imposing liability on appellant did not violate the state constitution.

 

876 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


NO. 14-95-00811-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1963



April 17, 1997, rendered  
April 17, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 694777.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas) of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon, enhanced by two prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon. At trial, he testified that stress from his HIV-positive status brought on by the death of his friend from AIDS-related causes prevented him from realizing he was carrying a handgun outside his apartment. On appeal, he alleged error in failing to charge the jury on the insanity defense, ineffective assistance of counsel, and constitutional violations. The court affirmed. Appellant failed to object to the lack of insanity charge at trial, and the trial court had no duty to charge the jury on all defense theories raised. Appellant failed to overcome the presumption that counsel's actions were the result of sound trial strategy. Counsel consciously chose not to pursue an insanity defense and narrowed the case for the jury to whether appellant intentionally or knowingly possessed a firearm. Alleged constitutional violations were not preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The conviction of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon was affirmed because failing to charge the jury on the insanity defense was not fundamental error, counsel's assistance was not ineffective, and appellant failed to preserve for review an alleged constitutional violation.

Guillen v. State


NO. 03-96-00581-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1972



April 17, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, 119TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. B-95-0649-S, HONORABLE DICK ALCALA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accused sought review of the judgment of the 119th Judicial District Court, Tom Green County (Texas) which convicted appellant for the offenses of possessing marijuana and financing or investing funds to further the commission of the possessory offense, where appellant asserted that the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain his conviction and that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126, was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Following an undercover action where appellant and an accessory purchased and transported 24 bundles of marijuana, appellant was convicted for possessing marijuana and for financing or investing funds to further the commission of the possessory offense in violation of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126(a)(2). Subsequently, appellant sought review, contending that the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain his conviction for illegal investment and that section 481.126, was unconstitutionally vague. On review, the court affirmed the conviction. The court noted that, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02(a)(2), the trial court had authorized conviction either on a finding that appellant personally financed or invested funds intended to further the possession of marijuana, or on a finding that a party financed or invested the funds and that appellant aided the party with the intent to promote or assist in the offense. The court held that the facts were sufficient to support appellant's conviction as a party to the offense. In addition, the court, following case precedent, summarily rejected appellant's constitutional argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant accused's conviction for financing or investing funds to further the commission of a possessory offense, because the evidence was legally sufficient to support defendant's conviction as a party to the offense and because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Nash v. Perry


NO. 03-96-00580-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


944 S.W.2d 728; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1976



April 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Granted October 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-10045-B, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants individually and as next friends of their minor children challenged the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees in appellants' action against them averring causes of action for negligence.


OVERVIEW: Appellants parents filed an action alleging that their children were physically and sexually abused at a day-care center. Appellants alleged that appellees witnessed the abuse and that the failure to report the abuse breached common law and statutory duties pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 261.101(a) (1996) and proximately caused injuries to appellants and their children. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees. On the common law negligence claim, the court held that appellants did not allege that appellees controlled the premises where the abuse allegedly occurred or that appellees created a dangerous situation, therefore dismissal was affirmed. On the negligence per se claim the court determined that scienter was implicit in the requirements of controlling statutes. The court also that the statutes defined the conduct of a reasonable person; therefore, a violation could be the basis for a negligence action. Accordingly the judgment dismissing appellants' negligence per se claim judgment was reversed as the court held that the trial court erred in ordering as a matter of law that appellants take nothing by the claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed on the common law negligence claim. The judgment was reversed and remanded on the negligence per se and gross negligence under that theory as a statutory standard of conduct could be implied. The court stated it remained the burden of appellants to persuade the fact finder concerning a violation of the statutory duty and proximate cause and the burden of appellees to prove a permissible excuse.

Hallco Tex. v. McMullen County


Appeal No. 04-96-00681-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2020



April 16, 1997, Delivered  
April 16, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 156th District Court of McMullen County, Texas. Trial Court No. M-95-0003-CV-B. Honorable Joel B. Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the 156th District Court of McMullen County, Texas, that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, McMullen County and its commissioners, after appellees passed an ordinance barring any solid waste disposal facility from operating within three miles of Choke Canyon Lake.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation bought land within two miles of Choke Canyon Lake and filed for a permit with the Texas Natural Resource Conservation Commission (TNRCC) to build a solid waste disposal facility. Before the permit was issued, appellees, McMullen County and its commissioners, passed an ordinance barring any solid waste facility from operating within three miles of the lake. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, and the court affirmed. The court held that appellees' ordinance was not an unconstitutional taking of appellant's property, as the mere fact that a regulation prevented one use of the property did not establish a taking. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional, as it was not so arbitrary that it deprived property without due process and as it was rationally related to a legitimate government interest because appellees had an interest in protecting the lake. The court held that summary judgment was appropriate even though the matter involved complex land issues, and appellees' action was not preempted by the TNRCC action. The lower court did not abuse its discretion when it did not consider appellant's additional evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, the county and its commissioners, and held that appellant corporation had not shown that the ordinance that prohibited appellant from operating a solid waste facility on its property two miles from a lake did not deprive appellant of use or value of its property.

Rivera v. City of Laredo


Appeal No. 04-96-00058-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


948 S.W.2d 787; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2032



April 16, 1997, Delivered  
April 16, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied May 16, 1997. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 49th District Court of Webb County, Texas. Trial Court No. C-94-00140-D1. Honorable Carolyn Spears Petersen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers challenged a ruling of the 49th District Court of Webb County (Texas), which granted appellee city summary judgment and denied appellants' motion for summary judgment in appellants' action for a writ of mandamus and injunctive and declaratory relief for alleged violations of the Open Meetings Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city held meetings under the Open Meetings Act to select a police chief. One such meeting was recessed for two days and then resumed again, with no notice of the second meeting, which appellee considered an extension of the first meeting. At the resumed meeting, a new police chief was selected, and the new chief suspended one appellant police officer for alleged official misconduct. Appellant police officers filed an action against appellee, seeking a writ of mandamus and injunctive and declaratory relief for alleged violations of the Open Meetings Act. Appellants sought to have the police chief appointment nullified. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment, and appellee's motion was granted by the trial court for unspecified reasons. Appellants challenged that ruling. On appeal, the court reversed, rendered judgment for appellants, and held that the Open Meetings Act required notice for each meeting under the Act, even a continuation of a previously recessed meeting. The court held that appellants' challenge was proper, as public officials' offices were properly challenged under either quo warranto proceedings or alleged violations of the Open Meetings Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court ruling, which granted appellee city summary judgment and denied appellant police officers' motion for summary judgment in appellants' action for a writ of mandamus and injunctive and declaratory relief, because appellee appointed the police chief during a meeting of which appellants did not receive notice, and notice was to be provided for all meetings under the Open Meetings Act.

Ashford v. State


NO. 01-95-00492-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1893



April 10, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law Number 4. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9449591.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction by the County Criminal Court at Law Number 4, Harris County, Texas, for public lewdness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her conviction for public lewdness. The court affirmed the conviction. It held that it was proper to deny defendant's motion to suppress the pre-trial and in-court identifications and refuse to submit a jury instruction on the identifications because defendant voluntarily surrendered, there was no pre-trial identification, defendant was never in a lineup or photospread, and the confrontation between defendant and the police officer was an arrest, not a pre-trial identification procedure. The court held that defendant could not complain that she was not charged by her true name because did she not raise the issue at the trial level. The court held the variance between the business name in the information and its true name was not fatal because a reasonable jury could have concluded they were one and the same. The court held that the statutes defining public lewdness did not substantially reach constitutionally protected activity and rejected the facial overbreadth challenge. It held defendant was charged under the proper statute because the public lewdness statute required a knowing act of sexual conduct in public, while the prostitution statute did not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for public lewdness because there was no error in submitting the pre-trial and in-court identification of defendant when she voluntarily surrendered; defendant could not complain on appeal she was not charged in her true name because she did not raise the issue at the trial level; and the variance between the business name in the information and its true name was not fatal.

Harris v. State


NUMBER 13-95-132-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1728

April 3, 1997, filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 377th District Court of Victoria County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 377th District Court of Victoria County (Texas), convicting appellant of the felony offense of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. Appellant was placed on deferred adjudication for ten years. Following appellant's violation of his probation, the trial court adjudicated appellant guilty of the underlying offense and he was sentenced to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for the felony offense of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. He pleaded guilty to the offense and was then placed on deferred adjudication for ten years. The state filed a motion to adjudicate appellant guilty of the underlying offense after he allegedly violated the terms of his probation. Appellant pleaded guilty to five probation violations and stipulated to the evidence in support of the violations. The trial court accepted his pleas and adjudicated appellant guilty of the underlying offense, and sentenced him to life in prison. Appellant argued that he did not receive effective assistance of counsel and the state did not meet its burden of proving that he was convicted of an offense in violation of his deferred adjudication. Further, appellant alleged his life sentence was cruel and unusual punishment and the trial judge abused his discretion by failing to recuse himself from presiding over appellant's motion for rehearing. The appellate court affirmed the order because the record revealed that appellant was fully admonished of his rights by both his attorney and the trial court, thus his case was not prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction for the felony offense of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance following his probation violation because appellant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel regarding his hearing to determine whether the trial court should have proceeded with an adjudication of guilt was not allowed to be raised on direct appeal and he did not show that his guilty plea was involuntary.

Streetman v. Nguyen


Appeal No. 04-96-00606-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


943 S.W.2d 168; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1599



April 2, 1997, Delivered  
April 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied July 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 166th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 96-CI-07572. Honorable Michael Peden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient's estate and heirs, sought review of an order of the 166th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted summary judgement in favor of appellee physician on the basis that the two year statute of limitations under the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i § 10.01 (1997), had expired.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, patient's estate and heirs, brought a medical malpractice action against appellee physician. The suit was brought over two years after the alleged medical negligence occurred. Appellee was granted summary judgment by the trial court on the basis that the suit was statutorily time barred under the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i § 10.01 (1997). Appellants sought further review. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the Act imposed an absolute two-year statute of limitations. The Act alsoabolished the discovery rule in health care liability claims. The court held that § 4590i did not violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I § 13, because at common law a personal injury claim did not survive an injured party's death nor did a deceased's heirs have an action for their own losses. Article 4590i did not, therefore, restrict a well-recognized common law right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because Texas statutory law created an absolute two-year statute of limitation, and had abolished the discovery rule in health care liability claims for wrongful death and survival actions. The court held because wrongful death and survival actions were statutory, and not common law, claims the Texas open court provision was not applicable.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.

OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and wife challenged the summary judgment favoring appellee brother, city and city officials on all counts of their suit alleging malicious prosecution, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and civil rights violations arising out of their arrest for trespassing. The arresting officers had probable cause and their conduct did not violate appellants' civil rights. The court reversed on the claim of excessive force because a fact issue existed.

McDuff v. State


NO. 03-94-00307-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


943 S.W.2d 517; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1509



March 27, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 1, 1997. Released for Publication May 1, 1997. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 17, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5088.
Rehearing overruled by, 05/01/1997
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 09/17/1997
Writ of certiorari denied McDuff v. Texas, 522 U.S. 844, 118 S. Ct. 125, 139 L. Ed. 2d 75, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5088 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-5281, HONORABLE WILFORD FLOWERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.
McDuff v. State, 939 S.W.2d 607, 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Tex. Crim. App., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Rendered in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for aggravated sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping from the District Court of Travis County (Texas). Appellant had been tried and convicted of those offenses, along with the offense of capital murder, in another venue. The murder conviction was appealed directly to the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals, which affirmed the death penalty conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of capital murder and the separate offenses of aggravated sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping. The death penalty was imposed on the capital offense and the jury also assessed life imprisonment for each of the other two offenses. The capital murder conviction was appealed directly to the criminal appellate court, which affirmed that conviction. Appellant then challenged the non-capital offenses. The court reversed the conviction for sexual assault on grounds that it was not supported by any evidence other than that of the accomplice witness. Accomplice witness testimony could not, as a matter of law, form the basis of a conviction. The court upheld the conviction for aggravated kidnapping because there was evidence by non-accomplice witnesses, along with the accomplice testimony, which connected appellant to the crime, which was legally sufficient to support the verdict on that charge. The court found that the imposition of separate punishments for the capital offense and the non-capital offenses did not constitute double jeopardy because they were separate offenses and the sentences were consistent with the legislature's intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because it was supported solely by the testimony of the accomplice witness, which was insufficient corroborating evidence as a matter of law. The court upheld the conviction for aggravated kidnapping because non-accomplice testimony also connected appellant to the crime. The imposition of separate punishments for separate offenses did not constitute double jeopardy.

Soni v. State


NO. 03-96-00086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1282



March 20, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF HAYS COUNTY, NO. 40,825, HONORABLE HOWARD S. WARNER, II, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the County Court of Hays County, Texas, which convicted him of driving while intoxicated. Appellant argued that the trial judge erred in admitting evidence of an edited videotape showing appellant's attempts to pass sobriety testing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial-court judgment convicting him of driving while intoxicated. A police officer arrested appellant after observing his erratic operation of an automobile on a public way, his appearance and demeanor, a smell of alcohol about him, and his inability to perform three field-sobriety tests requested by the officer. Over appellant's objection, the trial judge permitted the jury to view an edited version of the videotape, a silent version showing only appellant's attempts to perform the sobriety tests. Appellant argued that testimony regarding his refusal to take a breath or blood test and the edited videotape, when admitted in evidence over his objection, violated his constitutional right against self-incrimination. The constitutional right extended, however, only to testimonial evidence and did not encompass purely physical evidence or evidence of physical characteristics. The judgment was affirmed because the trial judge therefore did not err by admitting in evidence the edited version of the videotape.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated was affirmed because the admission of the edited videotape showing appellant's attempts to pass sobriety testing did not violate appellant's right against self-incrimination.

Ex parte Chavfull


Appeal No. 04-96-00863-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


945 S.W.2d 183; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1301



March 19, 1997, Delivered  
March 19, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 187th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 96-CR-4895. Honorable Raymond Angelini, Judge Presiding 1


1 The writ of habeas corpus was referred to the Hon. Andrew W. Carruthers whose recommendation was accepted by Judge Angelini.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 187th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) in an accelerated appeal from an order denying a reduction in bail. Appellant's request for a reduction was denied after an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court considered an accelerated appeal from an order denying a reduction in bail. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to reduce the bond. The state responded by asserting that the trial court was without jurisdiction to enter the order. The reviewing court found that the trial court had jurisdiction to deny the reduction and affirmed the order. Appellant had been charged with knowingly and intentionally causing the death of another by shooting him with a firearm in the course of committing and attempting to commit a robbery. Evidence was presented that appellant was previously convicted of assault, that he was arrested for failure to identify himself, that he had two cocaine offenses, and that charges were pending against appellant for theft by check. Furthermore, evidence indicated that appellant was associating with individuals who were previously convicted, who had intentions of committing additional crimes on the night of the murder, and who were suspected in other crimes, including at least one additional murder. The court found that appellant posed a potential danger to the community as a whole based on his prior history.


OUTCOME: The order denying a reduction in bail was affirmed. The trial court had jurisdiction to deny the reduction. In affirming the denial, the court considered the evidence, particularly the violent nature of the crime, the absence of evidence regarding appellant's individual resources, and appellant's past history and the potential danger he posed to the community.

City of Grand Prairie v. M.B. Capital Investors


No. 05-95-00921-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1230



March 17, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 191st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-8460-J.

Original Opinion of August 27, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4023.



DISPOSITION: OVERRULED M.B. Capital's motion for rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee investment corporation moved for rehearing after the court found for appellant city, in its appeal from the 191st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) wherein summary judgment had been granted for appellee. Appellee maintained that appellant prohibited it from developing its land. The court had determined that appellant raised a fact issue of whether development of appellee's land would have been permitted.


OVERVIEW: Appellee investment corporation moved for rehearing after the court had found for appellant city, in its appeal from summary judgment for appellee, where a fact issue existed of whether appellant would have permitted appellee to develop its land. Appellee maintained, as it had argued in moving for summary judgment, that appellant had prohibited development of its property such that there was a taking. The court overruled appellee's motion for rehearing. The court opined that in arguing a taking, appellee had to show that appellant, purporting to act in the role of a neutral arbiter, acted for its own advantage and against appellee's economic interest. Noting that the issue was not just one of statutory construction but required review of all of the summary judgment evidence to determine whether appellant had acted to its own advantage in denying the plat, the court found that appellant had denied the plat as it failed to meet the technical requirements of the applicable statute and thus a fact issue existed as to whether appellant had completely prohibited development of appellee's property.


OUTCOME: Appellee investment corporation's motion for rehearing was overruled. On review from summary judgment for appellee, wherein appellee had argued that appellant city's denial of its plat was a taking, the court had determined that appellant city had raised a fact issue on whether appellant would have permitted appellee to develop its land and thus as to whether there was a taking. Therefore the court overruled appellee's motion for rehearing.

Ravenbark v. State


NO. 14-94-00830-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


942 S.W.2d 711; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1184



March 13, 1997, rendered  
March 13, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 2. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-04811.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2. Harris County, Texas, which found her guilty of stalking under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.02(a)(7).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was conviction for stalking under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.02(a)(7), and challenged her conviction, claiming ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The court held that the statute under which appellant was convicted was previously declared unconstitutional for vagueness and therefore reversed appellant's conviction and rendered a judgment of acquittal. While appellant did not challenge the constitutionality of the statute in the trial court, nor raise the issue in her appellate brief, nor file an amended brief raising the issue following the court's previous decision holding the statute unconstitutionally vague, the court held that appellant's actions did not amount to a waiver. The court noted that generally an unconstitutional statute was void from its inception and could not provide a basis for any right or relief; however, the rule was not without exception. The court concluded that the exception was not applicable to the facts, and accordingly, on direct appeal from a conviction under a void statute, the court held that the judgment was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant's conviction for stalking was vacated, as the criminal statute was unconstitutionally vague, and therefore on direct appeal from a conviction under a void statute, the judgment was also void.

Marroquin v. D & N Funding


NUMBER 13-96-292-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


943 S.W.2d 112; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1224



March 13, 1997, delivered  
March 13, 1997, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On appeal from the 275th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, sought review of a decision of the 275th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas that denied appellants' request for a temporary injunction to enjoin appellee, foreclosure purchaser, from proceeding with an action to evict appellants from their home.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife purchased a home in 1966. She later married appellant husband and they continued to live in the home. When appellants began to experience financial difficulties in 1987 they were denied refinancing because the home was homestead property. The home was subsequently twice sold to two different daughters. After both sales appellants continued to reside in the home. After the second daughter defaulted on the mortgage the bank foreclosed. In the meantime appellant wife filed for bankruptcy. The trial court denied appellants' request for a temporary injunction to enjoin appellee, foreclosure purchaser, from evicting them. The court affirmed holding that a temporary injunction would not be granted where there was a plain and adequate remedy at law. Appellee's forcible detainer action was automatically stayed whether appellee knew of appellant wife's bankruptcy or not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellants' injunction request. The court held that appellee's forcible detainer action was automatically stayed whether appellee knew of appellant wife's bankruptcy or not. A temporary injunction would not be granted where there was an adequate remedy at law.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 597,195.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas) which revoked his deferred adjudication for aggravated assault on a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it revoked his deferred adjudication for aggravated assault on a police officer. The court noted that appellant had waived indictment and entered a negotiated plea of guilty to aggravated assault on a police officer. Pursuant to the plea agreement, the trial court placed appellant on deferred adjudication probation for four years. During that time the state filed a motion to adjudicate appellant's guilt of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Appellant was found not guilty. The trial court then revoked appellant's deferred adjudication and assessed his punishment. The court stated that the case law indicated that the prohibition against a direct appeal of the trial court's determination to adjudicate was total. The court stated that it lacked jurisdiction to review the claim of error, and dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: An appeal of the trial court's determination to adjudicate a defendant's deferred adjudication was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because the prohibition against direct appeal of the trial court's determination was total.

Leach v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1143



March 11, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 283rd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F91-40902-HT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 283rd District Court, Dallas County, Texas, convicting him of delivery of less than 28 grams of cocaine. Appellant argued that his guilty plea was involuntary and that the trial court unconstitutionally imprisoned him for debt.


OVERVIEW: Appellant waived his right to a jury trial and pleaded guilty to delivery of less than twenty-eight grams of cocaine. The trial court found appellant guilty and assessed a sentence and a fine. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence, claiming that his guilty plea was involuntary and the trial court unconstitutionally imprisoned him for debt. The court affirmed the judgment and found that the trial court's written admonishment and appellant's written acknowledgment substantially complied with admonishment requirements, and appellant had not shown that he was unaware of the consequences of his plea or that the court's admonishment harmed or misled him. The court also held that appellant had not shown that his confinement was solely because of his inability to pay the court costs, and therefore the sentence did not violate appellant's rights to equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of delivery of less than 28 grams of cocaine because appellant had not shown that he was unaware of the consequences of his guilty plea or that the court's admonishment harmed or misled him.

Meadows v. State


NO. 07-95-0044-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1135



March 10, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 176TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HARRIS COUNTY; NO. 672,039; HONORABLE JIMMY JAMES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed. Reversed and remanded to the trial court for re-sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of orders of the 176th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas) that entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting appellant of the offense of aggravated sexual assault, and that assessed punishment at confinement for life.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for aggravated sexual assault. When the date scheduled for trial arrived, appellant filed a motion for continuance. The trial court granted the motion, provided appellant with an investigator, and reset trial. On the date set for trial, appellant filed a second motion for continuance. The motion was heard and denied, and trial commenced. After the state presented its evidence, appellant again sought more time. The request was denied, and trial proceeded. After the jury found appellant guilty, he filed an unsuccessful motion for a new trial. Based upon appellant's criminal record, a life sentence was imposed. Appellant then sought review, contending the indictment was flawed, the second motion for a continuance was denied in error, and the sentence was enhanced improperly. The court affirmed the conviction, because the indictment put appellant on notice of the charges against him, he failed to raise a pre-trial objection to any substantive defects, and it was not an abuse of discretion to deny the second continuance motion. However, the court reversed the sentence and remanded, because the state failed to show appellant's prior murder conviction was final.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's aggravated sexual assault conviction, reversed the sentencing order, and remanded for resentencing, because the indictment put appellant on notice of the charges against him and he failed to raise a pre-trial objection to any substantive defects; however, the state failed in its burden of proving the finality of appellant's prior conviction beyond a reasonable doubt.

Bohannan v. Tex. Bd. of Crim. Justice


NO. 03-95-00447-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


942 S.W.2d 113; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1109



March 6, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected on Overrule of Appellant's Motion for Rehearing April 24, 1997. Released for Publication April 24, 1997.
Writ denied by, 07/31/1997
Writ of habeas corpus denied Bohannan v. Johnson, 178 F.3d 1290, 1999 U.S. App. LEXIS 8049 (5th Cir. Tex., 1999)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Bohannan v. Dretke, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 3703 (N.D. Tex., Jan. 31, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Bohannan v. Thaler, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 40016 (N.D. Tex., Apr. 23, 2010)
Subsequent civil proceeding at In re Bohannan, 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 5737 (Tex. App. Beaumont, July 22, 2010)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Bohannan v. Griffin, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8126 (N.D. Tex., Jan. 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-00141, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas) that dismissed his suit pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 against appellee board and appellee department that alleged they wrongfully ceased the restoration of good conduct time after a mandatory supervision was revoked.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate had accrued good conduct time. After his mandatory supervision was revoked, appellee department refused to restore the good conduct time pursuant to a policy change by appellee board. Appellant sued appellees, and the trial court dismissed the suit as frivolous pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The standard of review of a § 13.001 dismissal was whether the trial court abused its discretion. The trial court abused its discretion if it dismissed a case that had an arguable basis in fact or law. Appellant's claim seeking a declaratory judgment pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code § 2001.038 was properly dismissed because the procedure set out in that statute did not apply to a rule or internal procedure of appellee board that applied to any inmate or other person under its custody or control. However, appellant's claims that appellee board exceeded its statutory authority and divested appellant of a property right should not have been dismissed. Sovereign immunity did not prevent appellant from alleging that appellees deprived him of property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part judgment dismissing appellant inmate's suit as frivolous. The trial court properly dismissed his declaratory judgment claim because the statute under which relief was sought did not apply to rules or internal procedures of appellee board that affected inmates. The trial court should not have dismissed the claim that appellee board exceeded its authority and deprived appellant of a property right.

 

896 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Queen v. State


NO. 03-95-00738-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


940 S.W.2d 781; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 896



February 27, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0954979, HONORABLE MICHAEL LYNCH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Dismissed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the District Court of Travis County (Texas) that convicted and sentenced him for capital murder, aggravated robbery, and engaging in organized criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder, aggravated robbery, and engaging in organized criminal activity. Appellant sought review of the convictions contending that the double jeopardy clauses of the Texas and United States constitutions were violated when he was adjudged guilty and punished for three offenses arising out of the same transaction. U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV; Tex. Const. art. I, § 14. With respect to appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery, the court reversed that conviction. Every element of the alleged aggravated robbery with serious bodily injury, including death, was included within the alleged capital murder in the course of robbery offense, and it was impossible for the state to prove the latter offense without also proving the former. The state relied on two opinions to justify appellant's convictions for both capital murder and aggravated robbery. The court distinguished these cases because, in each case, the two offenses challenged had a unique element and passed the Blockburger test. The court affirmed appellant's other convictions because they were not susceptible to appellant's double jeopardy attack.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that convicted appellant for aggravated robbery because all elements of aggravated robbery were included within capital murder as the two offenses were alleged in the indictment. Therefore, it is presumed that the two offenses were the same for double jeopardy purposes. The court affirmed convictions to capital murder and engaging in organized criminal activity, as double jeopardy did not apply.

State v. Porter


NO. 03-96-00005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


940 S.W.2d 391; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 897



February 27, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BLANCO COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 564, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the District Court of Blanco County, 33rd Judicial District (Texas), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of narcotics obtained during a warrantless search of personal belongings.


OVERVIEW: The state contended the trial court abused its discretion by granting defendant's motion to suppress heroin. The court found that the discovery of marihuana in defendant's motel room may have yielded probable cause but that alone was not sufficient to justify a search of his luggage without a search warrant or exigent circumstances. The court found that with defendant in police custody at the hospital and his belongings secure that there was no emergency and no reason the police could not delay the search until a warrant was obtained. The court found that defendant paid in advance for his room, so the motel manager had no property interest in the bags in the way of a hotel lien. The manager never took actual possession and control of the bags nor did he express any intent to do so, so the court concluded that the manager could not give consent to the police to open the bags. The court affirmed and found that there was no proof of a voluntary intent by defendant to abandon his bags, so his right to privacy in his belongings remained intact subject only to a valid search warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court found that a reasonable view of the evidence supported the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 1121

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 691,919.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of aggravated kidnapping, contending that the trial court erroneously deferred adjudication of guilt until after reviewing the presentence report, and that the sentence was cruel and unusual.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping and sentenced to life in prison. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that appellant's plea was voluntarily made, the trial court did not err in reviewing the PSI prior to adjudicating guilt, and appellant's sentence was not cruel or unusual because it was within the sentencing range provided by law.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of aggravated kidnapping was affirmed because appellant's plea was voluntarily made, the trial court did not err in reviewing the PSI prior to adjudicating guilt, and appellant's sentence was not cruel or unusual because it was within the sentencing range provided by law.

Cason v. E.I. Dupont De Nemours & Co.


NO. 01-94-01191-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 811



February 20, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-11874-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the summary judgments from the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas) granted in favor of defendant raw material supplier and defendant medical college, and the special appearance and plea to jurisdiction granted in favor of defendant university, in a products liability action for injuries plaintiffs alleged were caused by implants placed in their temporomandibular (jaw) joints.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs in a products liability action sued defendants alleging that they were injured by implants placed in their temporomandibular joints. The trial court granted summary judgments in favor of defendants, raw material supplier and medical college, and granted the special appearance and plea to jurisdiction for defendant university. On appeal, plaintiffs alleged that defendant raw material supplier had a duty to warn, arguing that the Teflon supplied to the implant manufacturer was defective due to contamination. Plaintiffs also alleged that defendant medical college was negligent in hiring the implant designer, and that defendant university was liable because one of its employees helped design and develop the implant. The court affirmed. The court held that defendant raw materials supplier did not have a duty, independent of the implant manufacturer, to analyze the design of the completed product that incorporated its non-defective component part. The court also found that defendant medical college was not negligent in hiring the implant designer. Further, the court affirmed the plea to jurisdiction sustained in favor of defendant university.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments granted to defendants, raw material supplier and medical college. The court found that defendant raw material supplier had no duty to warn because the raw materials used in the implants were non-defective products. The court also held that defendant medical college was not negligent in hiring the implant designer. Finally, the court sustained defendant university's plea to jurisdiction.

ACTIS v. CLAPP


NO. 01-95-00375-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 819



February 20, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-11874-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patients challenged a summary judgement granted in favor of appellee supplier and appellee medical school by the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, in a product liability case. Appellants also challenged the plea to the jurisdiction granted in favor of appellee foreign medical school. Appellants had brought the action for injuries they allege were caused by implants placed in their temporomandibular (jaw) joints (TMJ).


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted appellees, supplier and medical school, summary judgment on appellant patients' claim for injuries resulting from defective TMJ implants. Appellee supplier provided raw materials for manufacturing the implants. Appellee supplier had supplied the implant manufacturer with a medical use disclaimer letter. Appellee medical school employed the doctors who designed the implant. Affirming the judgment, the court held that appellee supplier was not strictly liable and had no duty to warn appellants because it did not provide a defective or inherently dangerous product to the implant manufacturer, who had an independent duty to warn appellants of the implant's dangers. Also, appellee supplier's investigation of a joint venture for a different product did not create a duty to warn appellants about the implants. Regarding appellee medical school, the court held there was no evidence that employing the doctor who designed the implant proximately caused appellants' injuries. Finally, out of deference to the foreign state's venue statute, the court could decline jurisdiction over appellee foreign medical school because it was a state university in the foreign state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgement in favor of appellee supplier and appellee medical school. The court also affirmed appellee foreign medical school's plea to the jurisdiction. Appellee did not supply a defective product to the manufacturer of implants that injured appellant patients. Appellee medical school did not cause appellants' injuries by hiring or employing the doctor who designed the implants.

Ex parte Torres


Appeal No. 04-96-00161-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 841



February 19, 1997, Delivered  
February 19, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 226th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-CR-3923. Honorable Sid L. Harle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant indicted for capital murder appealed the decision of the 226th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which denied defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus seeking dismissal of the charges because the indictment was returned during the third term of court following defendant's arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for capital murder of his son. Defendant filed an application for writ of habeas corpus seeking a dismissal with prejudice because the indictment was returned during the third term of court following his arrest. The trial court denied relief and defendant appealed. Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion in failing to dismiss the prosecution with prejudice when the indictment was delayed beyond the second grand jury term. The court held that the state was required to meet the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01, which stated that the state must either indict before the next term or show good cause for delay, and when the state failed to meet this burden, the trial court had no choice but to dismiss the indictment with prejudice. The court concluded that the state may have had good reasons for delaying the indictment that were never explored because the matter seemed moot as a result of a recent decision of the court. Thus the state should have an opportunity to be heard on the issue of good cause for delay, and the court remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court for consideration of whether or not there was good cause for the state's tardy indictment of defendant on murder charges. If no good cause was found, the indictment would have to be dismissed with prejudice because the state failed to indict defendant in the next term of court held after defendant's submission to bail.

Weightman v. State


NO. 14-93-01094-CR, NO. 14-93-01095-CR, NO. 14-93-01096-CR, NO. 14-93-01097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 688



February 13, 1997, rendered  
February 13, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted December 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182 District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 645211, 635638, 653936, 64708.

Original Opinion of December 12, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5472.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Reversed and Remanded in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brought a motion for rehearing from an order of the appellate court (Texas) affirming his criminal conviction. Appellant asserted that no trial objection was necessary to preserve the constitutional question for review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought a motion for rehearing in order to challenge the constitutionality of the penal statute upon which his conviction was based. The court looked at different categories of rights and determined that appellant challenged the constitutionality of the statute as applied and that this right was not a nonwaivable, absolute requirement, or prohibition. Because appellant contested only the constitutionality of the statute as applied he was required to object at trial. The court again declined to review the factual sufficiency of the evidence at trial because appellant failed to request the review in his original brief. The motion for rehearing was overruled.


OUTCOME: Appellant's motion for rehearing of his criminal conviction was overruled because appellant failed to object at trial to the constitutionality of a statute as applied, and failed to request a factual sufficiency review in his original appellate brief of the evidence used at his trial.

Connor v. State


NO. 03-95-00442-CR, NO. 03-95-00443-CR, NO. 03-95-00444-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 598



February 13, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LLANO COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 4242, 4243 & 4244, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part on All Causes


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the 33rd District Court of Llano County (Texas) for fraudulent sale of securities in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1944) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-4(F) (1964).


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered guilty pleas and was convicted for fraudulent sale of securities in violation of the Texas Securities Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1944) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-4(F) (1964). In an earlier decision the court affirmed the conviction, but the Court of Criminal Appeals remanded the cause to reconsider appellant's right-to-counsel claim. The court remanded to the trial court to reconsider appellant's motion for a new trial with legal representation. The trial court ultimately affirmed the denial of the motion for a new trial. The court held that the visiting trial judges docket entries granting a new trial, that was revisited by a different judge that denied the motion for a new trial was not error because the scope of the remand limited the trial courts review, which required a new hearing on the motion for a new trial, not a new trial automatically. The court held that appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel because his pleas were entered voluntarily. The court reversed on the order of restitution holding that restitution can only by ordered to victims of the crime appellant had been charged and convicted of.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for fraudulent sale of securities which affirmed on remand the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for a new trial with legal representation, and reversed the restitution order holding that restitution could only be ordered for victims of the crime.

Neary v. State


No. 05-96-00186-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 580



February 12, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MA95-18143-M.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED,


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 2, Dallas County, Texas, which denied appellant's pre-trial writ of habeas corpus based upon double jeopardy grounds under Tex. Const. art. 1, § 14, and U.S. Const. amend. V, where appellant's license had been suspended prior to his conviction for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After he was arrested for driving while intoxicated, appellant's driver's license was suspended pursuant to Tex. Trans. Code Ann. §§ 524.001-. 025 (1996). Thereafter, appellant was also criminally prosecuted for and convicted of driving while intoxicated. Appellant unsuccessfully filed an application for writ of habeas corpus, alleging that his criminal conviction violated double jeopardy under Tex. Const. art. 1, § 14, and U.S. Const. amend. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that no double jeopardy violation had occurred. The court found that the administrative license suspension did not constitute punishment for the purposes of double jeopardy. Moreover, the court held that the goal of the suspension statute was not so removed from standard revocation statutes as to constitute punishment for double jeopardy purposes.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying appellant's writ of habeas corpus was affirmed because the suspension of appellant's license by the Texas Department of Public Safety and the state's prosecution of appellant for driving while intoxicated did not unconstitutionally subject appellant to double jeopardy.

Robinson v. Texas


No. 05-91-02063-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 566



February 11, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F91-43279-K.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 4., Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of murder with an affirmative deadly weapon finding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant initially pleaded not guilty to murder. During jury deliberations, appellant withdrew his not guilty plea, waived his right to continued jury deliberations, and entered a guilty plea in exchange for state's recommendation of 40 years imprisonment, a fine and restitution to the public defender fund. The trial court followed the plea agreement in sentencing. Appellant then filed a general notice of appeal contending that his right to jury trial was not voluntarily waived as he did not do so in writing, that evidence was insufficient to support imposition of restitution, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel in filing his notice of appeal. State contended that the court did not have jurisdiction to consider any of appellant's points of error because his appeal did not comply with Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1), which required permission to appeal from the trial court, or that the matters appealed were raised by pretrial motion. The court agreed with state and held that because appellant filed a general notice of appeal and raised nonjurisdictional issues, it did not have jurisdiction to review the claims. Accordingly the appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed because appellant did not file a notice of appeal that complied with the requirements of the rules of appellate procedure.

Tate v. State


NO. 14-94-00450-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


939 S.W.2d 738; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 496



February 6, 1997, Rendered  
February 6, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 656,648. Hon. Ruben Guerrero, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 263rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his challenges, in denying his motion to suppress, and in making an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the judgment convicting him of aggravated robbery, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his challenges, in denying his motion to suppress, and in making an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon. In affirming the judgment of conviction, the appellate court concluded that because there was no discriminatory intent in the prosecutor's justification of its peremptory strikes, appellant failed to establish purposeful discrimination. Further, the motion to suppress was properly denied, as the evidence was obtained following a valid stop. Where the officer had a reasonable, articulable suspicion that appellant was involved in criminal activity, he had probable cause to detain appellant for purposes of an investigation, and such an investigative detention did not amount to an unlawful arrest. In modifying the judgment, however, the appellate court agreed with appellant's contention that the trial court erred in entering an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon. Where there was no specific finding that appellant knew that a deadly weapon would be used by his accomplice in the commission of the crime, the finding was redacted from the decree.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, as appellant failed to establish the prosecution's purposeful discrimination in exercising peremptory challenges and as evidence was legally obtained where an investigatory stop was conducted on the basis of probable cause. The judgment was modified, however, as the trial court erred in making a deadly weapon affirmative finding without finding that appellant knew his accomplice planned to use a weapon.

Tex-Air Helicopters v. Appraisal Review Bd.


NO. 14-95-00831-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


940 S.W.2d 299; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 486



February 6, 1997, rendered  
February 6, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 10th Judicial District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94CV0943. David E. Garner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order of the 10th Judicial District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee tax assessors on the grounds that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 21.05 (1992) was an unconstitutional tax exemption.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers, who operated a helicopter ferry service to offshore facilities, argued that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 21.05 (1992) did not grant a tax exemption, but allowed for apportionment of taxes by appellee tax assessors based on its property's use within the state. The court held that the statute was not a tax exemption simply because a portion of property went untaxed, but that it was valid as a valuation statute. The court reversed because the statute was permissible under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(b) since it allowed property to be taxed in proportion to its value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment to appellee tax assessors because appellant taxpayers were not granted a tax exemption, but were taxed based upon the value of their property that was used within the state.

Stringfellow v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-96-00231-CR, 04-96-00232-CR, 04-96-00233-CR, 04-96-00234-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 447



February 5, 1997, Delivered  
February 5, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 186th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court Nos. 94-CR-7182W, 93-CR-2653, 93-CR-6322 & 94-CR-3699. Honorable Terry McDonald, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the 186th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which revoked her probation for making harassing phone calls to her husband's ex-wife, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation on the grounds that defendant was making harassing telephone calls to her husband's ex-wife. The trial court revoked defendant's probation and defendant contended there was insufficient evidence to support such revocation. On appeal, the court reversed the decision. The state failed to prove by a preponderance of evidence that defendant placed repeated calls to her husband's ex-wife. Telephone records established that four calls were made from defendant's home to the ex-wife's home. Defendant admitted that she made two of the calls and hung up when she reached an answering machine. The remaining 50 hang up calls were not traced to defendant's home and there was no evidence that defendant made the calls. The state relied on the tumultuous relationship between defendant and the ex-wife to establish that defendant made the calls. Such evidence was insufficient to support the revocation decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision revoking defendant's probation because the state did not prove that defendant made repeated harassing calls to her husband's ex-wife. The mere fact that defendant and the ex-wife had a turbulent relationship was not sufficient to prove that defendant made the calls.

Myers v. State


No. 05-95-00842-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 410



January 31, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F94-04550-UK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child under age fourteen following a jury trial at the Criminal District Court No. 4, Dallas County, Texas. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, the jury charge as to his intending or knowing the result of his conduct, and the pretrial interview with the victim that he claimed violated his right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, appellant was convicted for aggravated sexual assault of a child under age fourteen and sentenced to life imprisonment. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove that he had penetrated the girl's vagina. A psychologist testified that the victim had told him that appellant had raped her and an examining physician confirmed that her vagina had been torn. The victim had testified pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071 (1997), which permitted her testimony to be videotaped and presented at trial. The trial court had determined that the procedures were necessary to protect the welfare of the victim who would be traumatized by appellant's presence. The court held that the procedure did not violate appellant's right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI. Rejecting appellant's claim that the jury instruction defining intentionally and knowingly was not limited to the result of his conduct, the court held that the charge caused no harm because the nature and result of appellant's conduct were the same. Finding no reversible error, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child under age fourteen because the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict. The court held that the victim's videotaped testimony that appellant had raped her did not violate his right to confrontation and the jury charge defining intentionally or knowingly caused no harm because the nature and result of appellant's conduct were the same.

In re R.A.T.


No. 11-96-124-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


938 S.W.2d 783; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 391



January 30, 1997, Decided  
January 30, 1997, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 326th District Court of Taylor County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the 326th District Court of Taylor County, Texas, which terminated her parental rights after the jury was instructed that it could use constructive abandonment under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.001(1)(N) (1996), as grounds for termination.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother's children had been in the custody of the Department of Protective and Regulatory Services (Department) for 32 months; the newly enacted constructive abandonment amendment to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.001 (1996), had been effective for five months when the department sought termination of appellant's parental rights. The jury found that appellant's parental rights should be terminated, and although there was no indication on which of five grounds the decision was based, one of the grounds advocated was appellant's constructive abandonment of her children under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.001(1)(N) (1996). On appeal, the court reversed, finding that inclusion of the constructive abandonment provision as a grounds for the termination decision was unconstitutional, because the the Department could not retroactively apply § 161.001(1)(N), even though appellant's children had in fact been in their care for more than the statutorily required one year period. The court found that the parental relationship was protected by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16, which prohibited the statute's retroactive application, and its use constituted reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial because the jury rendered an improper verdict on the basis of the constructive abandonment instruction, which was an unconstitutional ex post facto application of a newly enacted amendment to Texas' family law code.

Perez v. State


NO. 03-96-00121-CR, NO. 03-96-00122-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


938 S.W.2d 761; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 332



January 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 0946107 & 0950541. HONORABLE MIKE LYNCH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction on Both Causes


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order entered by the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), which ordered "shock probation" pursuant to Tex. Code. Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6(a) (1997), in connection with appellant's conviction for attempted aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to attempted aggravated sexual assault of a child and was assessed 10 years' confinement. His sentence was changed to a 10-year term of community supervision, which required that he register with appropriate law enforcement authority as a sex offender. In separate appeals consolidated before the court, he sought modification or reversal of the judgment to have the registration requirement deleted from the trial court's order and to keep confidential any information he provided under the sex offender registration law. The court dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because no statutory authority existed for a direct appeal from the trial court's order placing appellant on shock probation. Alternatively, if treated as an appeal from the judgment of conviction, the appeal was not timely perfected and was without merit. Further, there was no ex post facto application of the registration law because appellant's conviction was announced after the law was in place, and he could not show that the law was being applied to him unconstitutionally since he had not yet registered under the law.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal on the basis that the court lacked jurisdiction to entertain such appeal that was not timely perfected. Even if reviewable, there was no statutory or constitutional violation where the law was in place when appellant was convicted, and, at the time of the appeal, he had not yet registered as a sex offender under the law.
