Huckabee v. Texas Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation


NO. 03-95-00396-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 333



January 30, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 19, 1997. Second Correction April 17, 1997. Appellant's and Appellee's Motions for Rehearing Overruled April 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-05083, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of an order of District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed her cause of action for wrongful termination against appellee state agency on the basis of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former employee filed a civil rights suit, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 after she was fired from appellee state agency. Appellant sought declaratory judgment that the termination was void because unconstitutional, and requested reinstatement and back pay. Appellant contended appellee had taken her property without due process under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19. Appellee moved to dismiss on the basis of sovereign immunity. The trial court sustained the motion and rendered judgment dismissing the suit. The court held that it was bound to accept factual allegations in appellant's petition when reviewing trial court's decision. The court held that since appellee was not a political subdivision separate from the state, it was protected by the state's immunity. The court ruled that a state was not liable for damages for due process violations, but a person's whose constitutional rights have been violated may receive equitable relief. The court concluded that appellant had a property interest because she could be fired only for "just cause." The court reversed and remanded judgment in part with respect to the claim for equitable relief.


OUTCOME: Judgment of trial court which held that appellee state agency was immune from appellant former employee's civil rights suit on the basis of sovereign immunity was reversed in part because while appellee could not be held liable for damages for due process deprivations, appellant could receive equitable relief for violation of constitutional rights. To allow a state to impose a sovereign immunity defense would render due process meaningless.

Jeffery v. State


NO. 07-96-0123-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 324



January 29, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 140TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 95-421,405; HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the judgment entered below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 140th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas) which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault, and allowing the admission of extraneous evidence of prior sexual assaults during the punishment stage of his trial, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and alleged the trial court erred in failing to sustain his challenge to a juror, failing to provide the jury with a limiting instruction regarding its consideration of outcry testimony, failing to afford him appropriate latitude during cross-examination by failing to provide him with evidence pertaining to the child victim's credibility, and failing to exclude evidence of extraneous offenses during the punishment phase. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the trial court received deference in evaluating a venireman's credibility and appellant was not denied the right to cross-examine the victim. The court further held that appellant did not object or request a limiting instruction when outcry evidence was offered. The court also held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a) (1997) permitted the use of extraneous evidence of prior sexual assaults during the punishment phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault, holding that appellant failed to properly object or request a limiting instruction when appellee state offered outcry evidence from the victim. The court further held that Texas law permitted the admission of extraneous evidence of prior sexual assaults during the punishment phase of a trial.

Scott v. Denton


No. 05-95-01451-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 273



January 24, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 193rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-00446-L.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the decision of the 193rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) granting summary judgment to appellee physicians and hospital in a medical malpractice case, claiming that various issues of material fact precluded summary judgment and that the trial court erred in dismissing with prejudice her claims against appellee hospital because it could have imposed a lesser sanction.


OVERVIEW: After elective plastic surgery, appellant patient sued appellee physicians and hospital, alleging negligence, breach of warranties, and failure to obtain her informed consent. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee physicians and dismissed appellant's claims against appellee hospital as a sanction against appellant. The court affirmed the trial court, holding that no material issue of fact existed as to whether appellee surgeon negligently performed the surgery, a bad result alone being insufficient to establish negligence. The court also held that appellant's Deceptive Trade Practices Act (DTPA) claim was barred by the statute of frauds and that it did not violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 for the statute of frauds to bar appellant's DTPA claim. The court found summary judgment proper as to appellant's informed consent claims because appellant offered no controverting evidence to expert testimony establishing the absence of causation. The court determined that the trial court's dismissal of appellant's claims against appellee hospital was not an abuse of discretion, given appellant's gross misconduct and abuse of the judicial system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that no material issues of fact existed to preclude summary judgment and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing appellant patient's claims against appellee hospital with prejudice, in light of appellant's significant interference with the court's legitimate exercise of its core powers.

O'Bryant v. State


NO. 14-93-01173-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 82



January 9, 1997, rendered  
January 9, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 659,036.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 12, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4103.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing Granted. Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, convicting appellant of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged and convicted of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) after he was identified as one of a group who assaulted and shot a woman they were attempting to rob. On review, appellant raised a number of arguments, all of which were rejected by the appellate court. In one argument, appellant contended that the trial court erred by admitting testimony regarding an extraneous offense that appellant was involved in prior to the incident at issue. The court examined whether the probative value of the extraneous offense was substantially outweighed by unfair prejudice. It found that in view of appellant's testimony and his version of the facts, it could not say that the state had no need to offer the extraneous offense. In addition, although the state had other evidence to establish appellant's guilt, a rational jury could have found the extraneous offense to be both convincing and compelling evidence of appellant's intent. Therefore, the court found that the trial court was well within its discretion in admitting the challenged evidence.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for capital murder was affirmed because the court was not persuaded that any of appellant's contentions had merit, including appellant's contention that the trial court erred by admitting evidence of an extraneous offense. The court found that the probative value of the extraneous offense was not substantially outweighed by unfair prejudice.

Garay v. State


NOS. 01-94-00923-CR, 01-94-00924-CR, 01-94-00925-CR, 01-94-00926-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


940 S.W.2d 211; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 12



January 2, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 5. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 93-34981, 93-37189, 93-36020, 94-11922. HANNAH CHOW, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant part-time peace officers challenged an order by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5. Harris County, Texas, which convicted them of a class A misdemeanor offense for carrying firearms on duty in violation of The Private Investigators and Private Security Agencies Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb) 19(d)(1) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellant part-time peace officers sought review of their conviction of a class A misdemeanor offense under the Private Investigators and Private Security Agencies Act (the Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb) 19(d)(1) (1995), which permitted only full-time peace officers to carry firearms on duty. Appellants contended that the Act created an impermissible distinction between full-time and part-time peace officers and violated the unity of subject requirement for legislation. The court found that the applicable provisions of the Act were directly related to the general subject matter of the statute as expressed in the senate bill caption and that the statute was clearly intended to regulate the private security industry. The court concluded that the statute was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of protecting the public from unqualified or inexperienced officers. The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting appellants, finding that it was rational for the legislature to conclude that, as a class, part-time peace officers were not as qualified as full-time officers.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant part-time peace officers of a class A misdemeanor for carrying firearms while on duty was upheld because the statute authorizing only full-time officers to carry firearms was rationally related to the legitimate state interest in protecting the public from inexperienced officers.

Kendrick v. State


NO. 14-94-01263-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 2



January 2, 1997, rendered  
January 2, 1997, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 514,759.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a motion to abate his appeal and remand his case to the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas, which adjudicated his guilt. Appellant was charged with the aggravated sexual assault of a child and pleaded nolo contendere. The trial court deferred adjudication until the state alleged violations of probation. Appellant was adjudicated guilty and claimed that he was denied counsel during the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to the charge of sexual assault of a child. Appellant was represented by appointed counsel throughout his plea. The state later filed a motion to adjudicate on the ground that appellant violated the terms of his probation, and the record reflected that appellant was represented during the motion to adjudicate. In his motion to abate, appellant claimed that he was denied counsel during the time period for filing a motion for new trial and was forced to do so pro se. In denying the motion to abate, the court ruled that the mere filing of certain motions pro se did not mean that appellant was without counsel during the time in which other motions could have been filed. According to the court, appellant simply failed to timely request appointed counsel and did not show that he was denied counsel at any time. The court also ruled that appellant had no constitutional right to appellate review from a decision to adjudicate guilt in a deferred adjudication proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's motion to abate his appeal and remand to the trial court. The court ruled that appellant failed to timely request appointed counsel and did not show that he was denied counsel at any time. The judgment of guilt was therefore affirmed.

Texas Educ. Agency v. Maxwell


No. 11-95-234-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


937 S.W.2d 621; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 26



January 2, 1997, Decided  
January 2, 1997, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 295th District Court of Harris County.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant and Overrule of Appellees' Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 5, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4037.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part and reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state education agencies appealed the judgment of the 295th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which found Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 35.030 (1993), unconstitutional, and enter a permanent injunction against its enforcement. Plaintiff parents appealed the trial court's denial of attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parents filed suit against defendant state education agencies, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 35.030 91993), which prohibited review of the results of mandatory state administered achievement tests, was unconstitutional. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional, but failed to hold a hearing on plaintiff's claim for attorney fees until the time to hold a hearing expired by operation of law. Defendant appealed the trial court's judgment and plaintiff's cross-appealed the denial of attorney fees and the trial court's failure to find the statute unconstitutional on several other grounds. On appeal, the court dismissed defendant's cause for mootness, because the statute had been repealed during the pendency of the appeal. The court held that a party who prevails in an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 should be awarded attorney fees, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, unless there are circumstances which would make such an award unjust. The court reversed the denial of attorney fees to plaintiffs and remanded the case to the trial court to determine the reasonableness of the fees and to determine whether fees should be awarded.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot because the challenged statute had been repealed. The court reversed the denial of attorney fees to plaintiff parents who had prevailed below, and remanded the case to the trial court to hold a hearing to determine the reasonableness of the attorney fees and to determine whether to award fees.

Woody v. State


No. 05-95-00673-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5821



December 31, 1996, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 282nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F94-40582-IS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attacker challenged his conviction for assault in the 282nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), on the ground that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the conviction and sentence, the sentencing process was unfair, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.015 was unconstitutionally vague, and the trial court should not have denied him access to the victim impact statement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attacker and three other men became involved in a fight in a parking lot with the complainant. Appellant was convicted of assault and sentenced under the hate crime law, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.015. He claimed at trial and on appeal that he acted in self-defense and that he was misled into letting the judge sentence him because of comments by the judge that the crime was a state jail felony with mandatory probation. The court affirmed the conviction for assault because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient despite evidence to the contrary. However, the court agreed that the judge's comments about the sentencing, which led appellant to waive his right to have the jury assess his punishment under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(b) (1977), warranted reversal for a new sentencing hearing. The remaining issues on appeal were moot because of the sentencing reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant attackers' conviction because the jury's verdict that appellant did not act in self-defense was not so contrary to the overwhelming weight of the evidence as to be clearly wrong and unjust. The court agreed with appellant that he was deprived of his statutory right to have a jury assess punishment because of misleading comments by the court. It reversed the sentence and remanded the case for a new punishment hearing.

Carreras v. State


NO. 14-95-00297-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


936 S.W.2d 727; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5764



December 30, 1996, rendered  
December 30, 1996, Opinion filed

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 12. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-24826. Hon. Robin Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant female sought review of her conviction in County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas), where a jury found her guilty of disorderly conduct under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(2) (1991), for exposing her chest in public. Appellant asserted she was prosecuted in violation of the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions because the statute was being selectively and discriminatorily applied.


OVERVIEW: Appellant female and a male friend went to the beach. Both of them removed their tops and sat nude from the waist up, in a grassy area. Witnesses said that they found this conduct offensive. Appellant was arrested for and convicted of disorderly conduct under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(2) (1991). Appellant sought further review and contended that the trial court erred in overruling her motion to quash the complaint and her motion for a directed verdict, because the prosecution violated her right to equal protection of the laws by engaging in selective prosecution of her as a woman in violation of Tex. Const. art. 1, §§ 3 and 3a, and the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. IV. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellant had failed to prove her claim. Appellant had not made a prima facie case that her prosecution was discriminatory by showing other persistent instances where individuals in like circumstances had not been prosecuted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because it found that the appellant female produced no evidence to prove her claim of denial of equal protection of the laws and failed to meet her burden of establishing a prima facie case of selective prosecution.

Carrier v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 687049, 687840, & 688030.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged the decision of the 180th District Court (Texas), which sentenced him to 45 years in prison for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant entered a plea of guilty to three counts of aggravated robbery and was sentenced to 45 years in prison. Appellant claimed the trial court erred in imposing his sentence because the indictments he pleaded guilty to did not sufficiently allege the offense of aggravated robbery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03. On appeal, the court held that appellant waived his right to appeal all nonjurisdictional defects because he pleaded guilty without an agreed recommendation on punishment. The court held that a defect in an indictment was a nonjurisdictional defect. The court held that even though appellant couched his point of error as a punishment error, it was a nonjurisdictional challenge to a defect in the indictment and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant criminal defendant's conviction was affirmed because appellant waived his right to appeal nonjurisdictional defects in the indictment by voluntarily entering a guilty plea without an agreed recommendation on punishment.

AccuBanc Mortg. Corp. v. Drummonds


NO. 2-95-072-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


938 S.W.2d 135; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5690



December 19, 1996, DELIVERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's and Appellee's Motions for Rehearing Overruled February 27, 1997. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 141ST DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. HON. CATHERINE GANT.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a judgment from the 141st District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, which was returned in favor of appellee former president in his action alleging breach of contract, state constitutional tort claims, and federal constitutional tort claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former president and CEO of appellant company sued because its resolution trust corporation-controlled board of directors fired him. The jury returned a verdict in favor of appellee. On review, the court held that the trial court's rulings regarding appellee's breach of contract claim was proper because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to establish that appellant had a 12 month employment contract with appellee, and was not an at will employee. Therefore, the judgment was affirmed as to appellee's breach of contract claim. However, trial court erred in allowing appellee to recover under his Bivens and state constitutional tort claims. Specifically, the court held that no Bivens action was available against appellant because it was a private entity. Further, the court held that Texas law did not recognize common law causes of action for damages for alleged violation of state constitutional rights. Accordingly, the judgment was reversed and rendered in part.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered in favor of appellee former president was affirm with respect to appellee's breach of contract claim because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to establish that appellant company breached appellee's employment contract. However, the judgment entered in favor of appellee with regard to both his state and federal constitutional tort claims was reversed and rendered so that appellee take nothing.

Richardson v. State


NO. 01-92-00646-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5556



December 19, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 634710.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after he waived indictment and trial by jury and entered a plea of guilty in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after he waived indictment and trial by jury and entered a plea of guilty. Appellant sought review, contending that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977), the statute under which he pleaded guilty, was unconstitutional because it deprived him of his right to compulsory process, and denied him due process of law under both the state and federal constitutions. The court overruled appellant's point of error because the court had already held that article 1.15 was constitutional under the same attack that appellant had mounted in a prior case. The court also held that the trial court had not erroneously entered a judgment of guilt after it accepted appellant's guilty plea where the record did not reflect that appellant waived his right to compulsory process because there is no requirement that appellant specifically waive his right to compulsory process. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, holding that the statute under which appellant had pleaded guilty was constitutional, and that there had been no requirement that appellant specifically have waived his right to compulsory process before the court accepted his plea and entered a judgement of guilt.

Operation Rescue-National v. Planned Parenthood

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON

Weightman v. State


NO. 14-93-01094-CR, NO. 14-93-01095-CR, NO. 14-93-01096-CR, NO. 14-93-01097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5472



December 12, 1996, rendered  
December 12, 1996, Opinions filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 13, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 688. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted December 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 645211, 635638, 653936, 647408.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Reversed and Rendered in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, convicting him of nine counts of theft of trade secrets, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05 (1989), and two counts of commercial bribery, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(c) (1989).


OVERVIEW: During the course of a sting operation, appellant, a parts manufacturer, manufactured and sold replacement parts for certain proprietary machinery to an undercover operative. The drawings used to manufacture the parts were copied from actual designs by the companies that owned the rights to the part designs. Appellant was convicted of nine counts of theft of trade secrets, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05 (1989), and two counts of commercial bribery, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(c) (1989). On review, appellant raised numerous arguments, including that the drawings did not reflect trade secrets. With reference to one of the companies, the court agreed that the company did not take adequate measures to prevent the drawings from becoming available to persons other than those they designated. Therefore, the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that those drawings were trade secrets. However, as to other drawings, the court found sufficient evidence that the company maintained substantial secrecy of their trade secret drawings and the evidence was sufficient to maintain appellant's conviction. Accordingly, appellant's convictions were reversed in part and affirmed in part.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions for trade secret theft and commercial bribery were affirmed in part and reversed in part. The reversed convictions resulted from the court's finding that the owner of the part drawings did not take adequate measures to prevent the drawings from becoming available to persons other than those they designated.

McGowan v. State


NO. 14-93-01098-CR, NO. 14-93-01099-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


938 S.W.2d 732; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5498



December 12, 1996, Rendered  
December 12, 1996, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 13, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 686. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted December 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 647407, 653937. Kitzman, Hon. Oliver, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Reversed and Remanded in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his 182nd District Court for Harris County (Texas) convictions for two counts of commercial bribery, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(b), and one count of theft of trade secrets, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of commercial bribery, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(b), and one count of theft of trade secrets, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05. The court of appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court did not have jurisdiction over the claim for commercial bribery. Although money was wired to appellant from Texas and, presumably in exchange, documents were sent to Texas, these acts were not elements of the offense. For Texas to have had jurisdiction, appellant mush have solicited, accepted or agreed to accept a benefit from within Texas. However, the trial court did have jurisdiction over the state's allegations for theft of trade secrets because the offense was not completed until the communication of the trade secret was received in Texas. Thus, the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction as to commercial bribery, but did not err in denying appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction as to theft of trade secrets.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for theft of trade secrets was affirmed, but his conviction for two counts of commercial bribery was reversed because the court was without jurisdiction where none of the elements of the crime occurred in Texas.

Ochoa v. State


Appeal No. 04-95-00505-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5252

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 49th District Court of Webb County (Texas), which convicted him of taking a controlled substance into a jail facility in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.112 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a deputy sheriff who worked in a jail's mailroom, was suspected of delivering drugs to certain inmates in exchange for money. A prisoner agreed to assist in a sting operation and told appellant a package containing drugs would come for him. When the package arrived, appellant took it into the jail and left it with his supervisor's secretary. Appellant was convicted of taking a controlled substance into a jail facility. The court held that appellant could not assert the public duty defense because his actions were not reasonable in light of the available alternative courses of conduct, and that he could not assert the defense of entrapment because he attempted to prove that he did not commit the charged offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for taking a controlled substance into a jail facility because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the conviction and because appellant could not assert the defenses of public duty or entrapment.

 

929 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. City of Longview


NO. 12-95-00189-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


936 S.W.2d 413; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5448



November 27, 1996, delivered  
November 27, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 6, 1997. Released for Publication January 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 124TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF GREGG COUNTY, TEXAS. Khoury, Hon. Alvin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club owner sought review of a judgment of the 124th Judicial District Court of Gregg County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in a declaratory action filed by appellant to determine the validity of a local ordinance regulating sexually oriented activities at establishments serving alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant club owner operated a bar where women danced topless. After appellee city enacted an ordinance prohibiting nudity or semi-nudity in establishments serving or permitting the consumption of alcoholic beverages, appellant filed a declaratory action to determine the ordinance's validity. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed. When reviewing the validity of the city ordinance, the court presumed the ordinance was valid. The court lacked the authority to interfere unless the ordinance was unreasonable and arbitrary. The burden of showing that a city ordinance was invalid rested on the party attacking it. Appellee city was a home rule city; therefore, it had the full power of self-government and authority to do anything the state legislature could have authorized it to do. The Texas Alcoholic Beverage Code preempted only the regulation of the sale of alcoholic beverages. Other activities that took place on premises where alcohol was sold were subject to local regulation. Further, the state legislature had placed no restrictions on municipalities to regulate unwanted secondary activity.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellant club owner's declaratory action to determine validity of local ordinance regulating sexually oriented activities at establishments serving alcoholic beverages was affirmed. The state legislature had only preempted the regulation of the sale of alcoholic beverages, not regulation of secondary activities at the places where alcohol was sold.

Thorn v. State


No. 05-95-00865-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


961 S.W.2d 12; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5666



November 27, 1996, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2. Grayson County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-2-847.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for perjury in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.02 which was entered in the County Court at Law No. 2. of Grayson County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of perjury after he submitted a sworn affidavit with his application to be placed on a general election ballot which falsely stated that he had never been convicted of a felony for which he had not been pardoned or had his full rights of citizenship restored by other official action. Appellant had thirteen prior felony convictions for which he had not been pardoned. At his trial, appellant testified that he was confused by the language of the affidavit. Appellant sought review of his conviction, and the court affirmed. Under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.02, a person committed a perjury offense if, with intent to deceive and with knowledge of the statement's meaning, he made a false statement under oath. The state did not need to allege or prove that appellant knew the statement to be false when he made it. Under § 37.02, if a jury believed that appellant thought his statements was true, they would be unable to find that he intended to deceive, and acquittal would be required. However, because appellant was confused, no acquittal was required. Appellant would have known if some official action exonerating him of his prior felonies had taken place.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for perjury was affirmed. The fact that appellant stated that he was confused about the language used in the affidavit concerning whether he had been pardoned or had other official action taken which exonerated him from his prior felony convictions was not sufficient to acquit him of perjury.

City of San Antonio v. Beyer


Appeal No. 04-94-00383-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5113



November 20, 1996, Delivered  
November 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the 37th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 91-CI-18094. Honorable David Berchelmann, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and appellant company sought review after a jury in the 37th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) entered a judgment in favor of appellee employee in a claim for bad-faith refusal to settle, negligence, and misrepresentation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city refused to settle an accident within tort limits, which resulted in a judgment that exceeded tort limits for which appellee employee was liable. Appellee entered into a covenant with plaintiffs, dismissed his appeal of the judgment, and sued appellant city and appellant company, alleging bad faith. The court reversed and remanded as to appellant city and reversed as to appellant company. Appellant city acted in a proprietary capacity when it acted as a self-insurer and was not immune from liability, but the trial court committed reversible error by excluding the covenant because it was relevant to show bias under Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 408. Appellee was not a third-party beneficiary of the agreement between appellant city and appellant company; therefore, appellant company was not negligent because it did not owe appellee a duty of good faith and fair dealing. Appellant city had a disqualifying conflict of interest because of its limited liability and appellee's unlimited liability and because of appellee's assertion that the tires on his vehicle caused the accident (which hurt appellant city and helped appellee) that supported the jury's finding of negligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial as to appellant city and reversed as to appellant company in appellee employee's claim for bad-faith refusal to settle, negligence, and misrepresentation. The trial court committed reversible error by refusing to admit appellee's covenant to delay execution because it showed bias. The court reversed as to appellant company because it had no duty of good faith and fair dealing to appellee.

City of Euless v. Dallas/Fort Worth Int'l Airport Bd.


No. 05-95-00479-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


936 S.W.2d 699; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5656



November 20, 1996, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied February 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 162nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-4298-I.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed in Part, Affirmed in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cities sought review of a judgment on remand to the 162nd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which denied defendants' counterclaim against plaintiffs, airport board, member cities, and airport users, that the Texas Municipal Airports Act, 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 1025, 1046-57 (codified as Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 22.001-.159 (1997)) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered a declaratory judgment in favor of plaintiffs, airport board and airport users, on defendant cities' challenge to the constitutionality of the amended Texas Municipal Airports Act (Act), 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 1025, 1046-57 (codified as Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 22.001-.159 (1997)). The case had been remanded to the trial court for consideration of the validity, constitutionality, and applicability of 1993 amendments to the Act. The court determined that it lacked subject-matter jurisdiction to review the defendants' constitutional challenge because related litigation had disposed of the actual controversy concerning the constitutional issues in the case. The court concluded that the legislature had withdrawn defendants' eminent domain power over all roads within the airport's geographic boundaries and given that power to the Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport Board. The court held that the definitions of a municipality and a local government in the Act encompassed home rule cities.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant cities' counterclaim against plaintiffs, airport board, member cities, and airport users, for want of a continuing justiciable controversy to the extent that it sought declaratory relief as to the constitutional issues because the constitutional challenge was moot. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects because the trial court correctly interpreted the amended Texas Municipal Airports Act.

Morton v. State


Appeal No. 04-96-00367-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


935 S.W.2d 904; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4997



November 13, 1996, Delivered  
November 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 226th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-CR-3737. Honorable Sid L. Harle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 226th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) of the charge of making a false statement on a license application in violation of the Texas Racing Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179e, § 14.06 (Supp. 1996). Pursuant to a plea bargain, defendant pled nolo contendere to the charge and received nine years in prison and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Based on a nolo contendere plea, defendant was convicted of making a false statement on a license application in violation of the Texas Racing Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179e, § 14.06 (Supp. 1996), and sentenced to nine years confinement and a fine. On appeal, the court affirmed and found that defendant's general notice of appeal did not confer jurisdiction on the court to address matters that were not ruled on by the trial court, or matters that the trial court did not grant defendant permission to appeal. The court found that defendant's pre-trial motions did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence to support an indictment. The court rejected defendant's assertion that art. 179e, § 14.06 subjected him only to administrative penalties, because Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. 179e, § 15.01 (Supp. 1996) supplied a penalty for defendant's act. The court found no jurisdiction to consider whether the statute was unconstitutionally vague because the issue was not preserved for appeal, and rejected the assertion that the indictment contained prejudicial evidence because no jury was empanelled.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for making a false statement on a license application were affirmed. A general notice of appeal did not confer jurisdiction to consider matters not ruled on by the trial court, defendant was not only subject to administrative penalties, the statute conferred the proper penalty for the act and was not unconstitutionally vague, and no jury was empanelled to be prejudiced by information in the indictment.

DRAKE v. STATE


NO. 14-94-01043-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4982



November 7, 1996, rendered  
November 7, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9424163.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the denial of a writ of habeas corpus by the 174th District Court, Harris County (Texas), where the same criminal occurrence resulted in separate criminal charges and forfeiture proceedings.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was arrested for keeping a gambling place and his cash seized, the state brought two successive criminal proceedings. In the initial forfeiture matter, appellant agreed to surrender over $ 9,000 in cash seized from him upon arrest. In a subsequent criminal trial, appellant attacked the proceeding as violative of double jeopardy and cruel and unusual punishment principles, and challenged the state's application of old statutory penalties in his case. The trial court denied appellant's application for a writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the local criminal statute authorizing forfeiture was neither criminal nor punitive in nature for purposes of United States or state double jeopardy provisions. The court further denied habeas corpus relief, finding that appellant had an adequate remedy by appeal and would waste judicial resources. The court also refused to consider the penalty range issue, as its opinion thereon would only be advisory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's writ of habeas corpus, finding that double jeopardy provisions were not violated because the local criminal statute authorizing forfeiture was neither criminal nor punitive in nature.

 

936 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re M.A.


Appeal No. 04-96-00094-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


935 S.W.2d 891; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4882



November 6, 1996, Decided  
November 6, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied November 27, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 289th Judicial District of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-JUV-2174. Honorable Carmen Kelsey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the decision of the 289th Judicial District of Bexar County (Texas), that certified appellant to stand trial as an adult for the death of a four-year old that was the result of a drive-by shooting.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile challenged the trial court's decision that certified appellant to stand trial as an adult for the death of a four-year old child that was the result of a drive-by shooting. The court affirmed and found that the trial court had probable cause to believe that appellant committed the murder, and therefore to have allowed the waiver of jurisdiction and the prosecution of appellant as an adult. The court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 required intentional and knowing conduct for a prosecution for capital murder, but did not contain an additional mens rea requirement that attached to the age of the victim. The court rejected appellant's assertion that the trial court abused its discretion in waiving jurisdiction because the age of the victim was not a required element of capital murder, and there was factually sufficient evidence under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.02(f) that supported the transfer of appellant to the criminal court. The court found that there was no requirement that the trial court find appellant mature and sophisticated and failure to do so did not violate appellant's due process rights under the United States and Texas Constitutions.


OUTCOME: A decision to certify appellant juvenile to stand trial as an adult was affirmed because there was sufficient probable cause to believe he committed the murder of a four-year old child, there was no mens rea requirement that attached to the age of the victim, there was sufficient evidence to support certification, and there was no abuse of discretion, and because appellant's constitutional due process rights were not violated.

Texas Pac. Indem. Co. v. Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n


NO. 03-95-00732-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4951



November 6, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Writ of Error Denied June 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-00348, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 28, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3841.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Judgment Set Aside and Cause Dismissed in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant indemnity company sought review of the order of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), that denied appellant's request for injunctive relief and affirmed appellee commission's order as valid and ordered appellee employee's spinal surgery as recommended by appellee physician.


OVERVIEW: Appellant indemnity company challenged the trial court's order that denied its motion for injunctive relief and affirmed the validity of appellee commission's order for appellee employee's spinal surgery that was ordered by appellee physician. The court affirmed in part and dismissed in part and held that appellee commission's order was not binding because of its rules that permitted appellant to challenge the medical necessity of the surgery and its cost, after the surgery took place. The court noted that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 408.027(d) (1996) afforded appellant a right to a contested-case hearing before appellee commission, and that appellant's due process rights had not been infringed nor were its substantial rights prejudiced. The court found that appellant failed to exhaust its administrative remedies because it had not availed itself of the contested-case hearing before appellee commission, and the court dismissed appellant's request for judicial review of appellee commission's order. The court found that appellee commission had the discretion to issue an amended order on a matter that had not become final.


OUTCOME: An order that denied a motion for injunctive relief was affirmed in part and dismissed in part because the order of appellee commission was not binding, because appellant indemnity company could challenge the medical necessity and cost of a surgical procedure, because appellant failed to exhaust its administrative remedies, and because appellee commission had discretionary authority to amend an order that was not final.

Hodges v. Thompson


NO. 2-96-161-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


932 S.W.2d 717; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4726



October 24, 1996, Decided  
October 24, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 362ND DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Honorable John Narsutis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county clerk challenged a judgment from the 362nd District Court of Denton County (Texas) ordering a writ of mandamus to certify appellees' petition for election to legalize the sale of beer and wine.


OVERVIEW: Appellees collected 286 signatures on a petition for an election to legalize beer and wine sales. Appellant county clerk refused to certify the petition finding it lacked the requisite number of certified signatures under Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 251.10(b) (1995). The trial court ordered a writ of mandamus to certify the petition, finding § 251.10(b) was not mandatory. On appeal, the court reversed the part of the order requiring appellant to certify the number of all qualified voters who signed, regardless of compliance with § 251.10(b). The court held that § 251.10(b) was mandatory, as was § 251.10(a). The phrase "no signature may be counted" in § 251.10(b) meant signatures not in compliance with the subsection may not be counted. The phrase "may not" meant "shall not" and was mandatory.


OUTCOME: The order for a writ of mandamus to certify appellees' petition for election to legalize beer and wine sales was reversed and remanded as to requiring certification of the number of all qualified voters who signed regardless of statutory compliance but otherwise affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision by the 269th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee medical providers, on the basis that appellant's claim for medical malpractice was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient filed a medical malpractice claim against appellee medical providers and alleged that her attending physician failed to remove a surgical sponge from her body after the birth of her son. I, § 13, because appellant had a reasonable time within the limitations period to file suit. The court further held that appellant waived her right to claim fraudulent concealment, as a result of her failure to raise it in her pleadings or in her response to the motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant patient's action for medical malpractice against appellee medical providers was barred by the two-year statute of limitations.

 

940 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Willy v. Coastal States Mgmt. Co.


NO. 01-94-01261-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


939 S.W.2d 193; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4681



October 24, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 85-63746. MARK DAVIDSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a judgment rendered by the 11th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that denied him postjudgment interest in a wrongful termination action. Defendant employer sought review of the judgment that ruled in favor of plaintiff in the wrongful termination action.


OVERVIEW: A jury found that defendant employer wrongfully terminated plaintiff employee, an attorney, and awarded damages but not prejudgment interest. Defendant appealed the judgment. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's denial of prejudgment interest. The issue was whether plaintiff should be allowed to maintain a cause of action for retaliatory discharge under the Sabine Pilot exception to the employment-at-will doctrine. Under the Sabine Pilot exception, an employee could not be fired for refusing to perform an illegal act. Defendant asserted that plaintiff's claims were barred because of the nature of the attorney-client relationship. The reviewing court concluded that plaintiff's status as in-house counsel did not preclude him from maintaining a claim for wrongful termination if the claim could be proved without any violation of the attorney's obligation to respect client confidences. The reviewing court reversed the judgment, holding that plaintiff could not maintain his action without exposing attorney-client confidences.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment finding that plaintiff was wrongfully terminated because plaintiff could not use confidential client information to show that he was wrongfully terminated. The court overruled plaintiff's claim for prejudgment interest because it rendered judgment for defendant in the wrongful termination action.

Deakins v. State


No. 05-92-02530-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4652



October 18, 1996, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 195th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-03381-PN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery and assessment of court costs and expenses from the 195th District Court, Dallas County (Texas) alleging that his guilty plea was involuntary and the imposition of court costs and expenses unconstitutionally imprisoned him for debt.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to 25 years and assessed court costs and expenses. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment for two reasons. First, appellant entered his guilty plea knowingly and voluntarily pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 26.13 (1989) because the trial court had substantially complied with art. 26.13 when it admonished appellant both orally and in writing as to the range of punishment, and appellant failed to affirmatively show that he did not understand the consequences of his plea. Second, the court ruled that because the fees imposed were not the reason why appellant was confined, his argument that he was unconstitutionally imprisoned him for a debt because of his indigence was overruled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and fee assessment on two grounds. First, appellant knowingly and voluntarily entered his guilty plea because the trial court had substantially complied with the statute and appellant failed to affirmatively show he did not understand the consequences of his plea. Second, appellant was not unconstitutionally imprisoned for a debt because the fees were not the reason for his confinement.

Ludwick v. State


NO. 2-95-411-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


931 S.W.2d 752; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4621



October 17, 1996, Decided  
October 17, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 372ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Honorable Scott Wisch.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court reversed and cause remanded to trial court for acceptance of plea, adjudication, and assessment of punishment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 372nd District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), that revoked appellant's probation for aggravated possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, that adjudicated appellant guilty based on his previous plea, and that sentenced appellant to imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to aggravated possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, without benefit of a plea bargain. Appellant's adjudication was deferred. After he violated the conditions of his probation, the trial court adjudicated appellant guilty and sentenced him to imprisonment. Appellant challenged, arguing the trial court was not authorized to place him on deferred adjudication. The court held that the deferred adjudication statute that was in effect at the time appellant was charged, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(d), prohibited deferred adjudication for appellant's crime because appellant's crime was listed under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.107. The judgment placing appellant on deferred adjudication was void. Because appellant's guilty plea was voluntary, and not induced by the trial court's initial sentence, the guilty plea stood. The court reversed appellant's sentence, and remanded the case for acceptance of appellant's guilty plea, adjudication of guilt, and sentencing.


OUTCOME: Order adjudicating appellant guilty and sentencing him to imprisonment was reversed as void because deferred adjudication was not a valid sentence for appellant's crime at the time it was imposed. The case was remanded for acceptance of appellant's guilty plea, which remained valid, for adjudication of guilt, and for sentencing.

Houston Lighting & Power Co. v. City of Wharton


NO. 01-96-00642-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4634



October 17, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Writ of Error Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction June 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 127th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-016613.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit for under-calculation of franchise fees, defendant power company sought review of a decision from the 127th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted class certification to plaintiff cities.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff cities brought an action against defendant power company, alleging that it under-calculated franchise fees. Plaintiffs claimed breach of contract, specific performance, fraud, civil conspiracy, negligent misrepresentation, tortious interference with contract, and quantum meruit. Plaintiffs requested declaratory relief. They moved for class certification, and the trial court granted certification. Defendant sought review and contended that the trial court abused its discretion when it granted class certification under Tex. R. Civ. P. 42. The court affirmed. It found that the requirements for class certification were met because the class was so numerous that joinder of all members was impracticable, because there were questions of law or fact common to the class, because the claims or defenses of the representative parties were typical of the claims or defenses of the class, and because the representative parties would fairly and adequately protect the interests of the class. The court further found that a class action was superior to other available methods for the fair and efficient adjudication of the controversy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it granted class certification to plaintiff cities because plaintiffs demonstrated superiority of class action, numerosity, commonality, typicality, and adequacy of representation.

State v. Cerriteno


No. 05-96-00330-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4746



October 17, 1996, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellee's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB95-52382-B.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the County Criminal Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which granted appellee's motion to suppress blood test specimens obtained after he was arrested for driving while intoxicated because the police department procedures for administering alcohol tests to Spanish-speaking persons violated appellee's constitutional right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, who spoke only Spanish, was arrested for driving while intoxicated. A Spanish-language audiotape was used to give the statutory warnings and requested only a blood test, but did not offer a breath test. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the blood test on equal protection grounds. The state appealed and the court reversed, holding that the police department's procedure only needed to bear a rational relationship to a legitimate government interest. The court found that the state's procedures did not treat appellee differently based on a suspect factor. Therefore, the police department's procedures did not deprive appellee of any fundamental right because the arresting officer had the sole discretion to offer a blood or breath test, and were not a denial of equal protection rights. The court held that the police department's procedures were rationally related to obtaining admissible and accurate evidence of a suspect's alcohol concentration level. The court held that the equal protection provisions of Tex. Const. art. I, § 3 did not provide a broader protection than the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to grant appellee's motion to suppress evidence, holding that a Spanish speaking audiotape that only gave the option of a blood test in advising appellee of his rights after arrest for driving while intoxicated bore a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental interest in obtaining admissible and accurate evidence of a suspect's alcohol level, and was not a violation of equal protection.

Benavides v. Torres


Appeal No. 04-93-00753-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4555



October 16, 1996, Delivered  
October 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied December 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 166th Judicial District of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 89-CI-14794. Honorable John J. Specia, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client challenged an order of the 166th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted appellee attorney's motion for summary judgment on appellant's claim for fraud, legal malpractice, and violation of the Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.01 et seq., arising out of appellee's prior representation of appellant in a criminal matter.


OVERVIEW: Appellee attorney had represented appellant client in a criminal trial, after which appellant brought an action against appellee for fraud, legal malpractice, and violations of the Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.01 et seq. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment, and the court affirmed. In so ruling, the court held that the action was barred by the statute of limitations under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.001 (1996), under which imprisonment was not a legal disability. Further, the court noted that appellant demonstrated access to the courts by filing the instant suit while in prison, as well as filing a prior federal action for the same representation, which action had been dismissed. All of appellant's criminal appeals were exhausted when he filed the instant action, and he provided no support for his contention that the statute of limitations was unconstitutional. The court also held that because appellant had brought suit against appellee in federal court based upon the criminal representation, his suit was also barred by res judicata under Fed. R. Civ. P. 18(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee attorney on appellant client's claim of fraud, legal malpractice, and violation of the Deceptive Trade Practices Act arising out of appellee's representation of appellant in a criminal matter, because the statute of limitations had run on the claims and because the action was barred by res judicata as a prior federal action had been dismissed.

Laird v. State


NO. 14-93-01103-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


933 S.W.2d 707; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4425



October 10, 1996, rendered  
October 10, 1996, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 631,943.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile tried as an adult, sought review of his conviction, after a jury trial, for capital murder, claiming the trial court should have instructed on lesser included offenses, his oral statement should have been suppressed in accordance with Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 52.02, and the automatic life sentence under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.07(c) (1996) violated his due process and equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile tried as an adult, appellant sought review of his conviction, after a jury trial, for capital murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1994) and the automatic life sentence under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.07(c) (1996). Rejecting appellant's claim that the jury should have been instructed on lesser included offenses, the court decided that there was no evidence to show appellant acted recklessly rather than intentionally and no evidence to show that he had not already formed an intent to rob the victim before he shot him. The court found that a statement made to a Pennsylvania police officer was admissible because it was not made in response to custodial interrogation. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09(2) (1996). Affirming the conviction and life sentence, the court rejected appellant's claims it violated his right to a jury, constituted cruel and unusual punishment, and denied his rights to due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder and the life sentence imposed by statute because he was a juvenile tried as an adult. The court decided that it was proper for the trial court to refuse instructions on lesser included offenses, a noncustodial statement was admissible, and the automatic life sentence did not violate his rights under the Texas or federal constitution.

Grossnickle v. Grossnickle


No. 06-95-00008-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 102nd Judicial District Court. Bowie County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95 C 0831-102.

DISPOSITION: Appellee's Motion for Rehearing GRANTED. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing OVERRULED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged a judgment of the 102nd Judicial District Court, Bowie County (Texas), which entered a judgment dividing marital property in connection with appellant's divorce from appellee husband. A divorce was granted earlier in the case and appellant previously appealed from the property division. The court's remand on the previous appeal was on the property division only.

The court found that there was no need for the additional requested findings and conclusions based on its opinion. The court found that the only item remaining to be determined after appellant's first appeal was the division of the community estate, so temporary spousal support and attorney's fees set forth in the trial court's first judgment were not final. The court set aside as void the portion of the order denying appellant the use of estate assets pending appeal and set aside the order limiting appellant's freedom of speech. The court affirmed the property division, because the errors, at the most, amounted to three percent of the community estate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court as to the division of the property. The court found that errors in the division of property did not constitute an abuse of discretion. The court set aside orders prohibiting appellant wife's access to property awarded to her and limiting appellant's freedom of speech.

Wadsworth v. Wadsworth


Appeal No. 04-95-00462-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4327



October 2, 1996, Delivered  
October 2, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th Judicial District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CI-00316. Honorable David Peeples, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of a judgment of the 224th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas) rendering a take-nothing judgment against her in her lawsuit against appellee ex-husband for partition of his teacher retirement benefits and fraudulent conversion.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-wife filed suit against appellee ex-husband for a division of his retirement benefits and fraudulent conversion. Appellee unequivocally repudiated appellant's ownership interest in the benefits and communicated that to appellant, orally or in writing, before the lawsuit, so the trial court rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant. The court affirmed the judgment, finding error one waived by appellant's failure to plead the unconstitutionality of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.90(c). In error two, there was nothing to review because the fraud action did not appear in the transcript, which was the only record on appeal. No evidence was claimed to communicate the repudiation of the interest, but in the absence of a statement of facts, the court had to presume that sufficient evidence existed. Last, because appellant had provided the court with no ruling, no transcript of the charge conference, no requested questions, no record references, and no authority supporting error in bifurcating the trial by striking the fraud claim and submitting to the jury only a limitations and laches defense, appellant's point of error was waived under Tex. R. App. P. 52(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing judgment against appellant ex-wife in her suit against appellee ex-husband for a division of his retirement benefits and fraudulent conversion where appellee unequivocally repudiated appellant's interest, and error was either waived or unreviewable due to a lack of record, lack of evidence, or lack of statement of facts; and presumptions favored appellee.

 

950 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roberts


NO. 12-95-00128-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


932 S.W.2d 700; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4334



September 30, 1996, delivered  
September 30, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 114TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS. Kent, Hon. Cynthia S., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order entered by the 114th Judicial District Court of Smith County, Texas, which dismissed appellee's second indictment for attempted murder. The state claimed that because it did not consent to the dismissal with prejudice, the order was void.


OVERVIEW: After the state obtained a dismissal of its first indictment against appellee for attempted murder, it reindicted him. At the time for trial on the reindictment, the trial court denied the state's motion for a continuance, and the state filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court told the state the case would be tried or dismissed with prejudice. The dismissal order declared that the case was dismissed, but the trial judge added by interlineation that it was dismissed with prejudice. In his motion to dismiss the third indictment, appellee claimed that because the reindictment was dismissed with prejudice, jeopardy barred the state's third indictment on the same charges. The court reversed the second dismissal and remanded for trial. The court held that the dismissal order was void because the state did not consent to dismissing the case with prejudice. The court stated that jeopardy did not attach because a jury was not impaneled and sworn. The court observed that the trial court did not have the authority to dismiss the case with prejudice because the state did not agree to it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing appellee's third indictment for attempted murder. The court held that the order that dismissed the second indictment for the same offense was void because the state did not consent to dismissal of the indictment with prejudice. The court also held that jeopardy did not attach to the second indictment because a jury was never impaneled and sworn. The case was remanded for trial.
