City of El Paso v. Alvarez


No. 08-96-00237-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


931 S.W.2d 370; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4192



September 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 16, 1996. Released for Publication October 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: The City's Petition for writ of mandamus conditionally granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to enforce a municipal ordinance, relator municipality sought a writ of mandamus regarding a decision from the El Paso County Court (Texas), which issued writs of habeas corpus to the real parties in interest and which stayed the municipal court proceeding against the real parties in interest.


OVERVIEW: Relator municipality prosecuted defendants, the real parties in interest, for violations of the adult entertainment ordinance. Defendants challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance and petitioned for writs of habeas corpus and for a stay of proceedings. The trial court issued the writs and granted the stay. Relator petitioned court for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent trial court to lift the stay and to terminate the writs. Respondent's position was that relator lacked standing to seek mandamus relief and that only the county district attorney could prosecute. The court granted the writ of mandamus. It found that relator had standing to petition for relief because relator had a justiciable interest in the validity of a municipal ordinance. It further found that under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 45.01, the city attorney, not the county district attorney, was required to prosecute. Furthermore, it was an abuse of discretion to grant the writs because a writ of habeas corpus was proper only where an applicant was actually restrained or deprived of liberty. The filing of a complaint in municipal court alone did not confine defendants or restrain their liberty.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus and ordered the trial court to withdraw the issuance of the writs of habeas corpus and to terminate the stay of proceedings because relator municipality had standing and was a real party in interest.

 

952 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Sharp v. Caterpillar, Inc.


NO. 03-95-00272-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


932 S.W.2d 230; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4181



September 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 14, 1996. Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 20, 1996. Released for Publication November 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-11176, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, comptroller and other state officials, sought review of the decision of the Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee corporation-taxpayer, which sought a refund of franchise taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: After exhausting its administrative remedies, appellee corporation-taxpayer sued appellants, comptroller and other state officials, in district court for a refund of franchise taxes paid under protest. The district court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, overruling appellants' motion for summary judgment, and appellants sought review of that order. The court reversed the district court's judgment and remand the cause, finding that appellee's future tax liability was not a sum certain and that it could not be deducted from its tax debt under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.109(a)(1) (1992). The court also found that the federal Employee Retirement Income Security Act, 29 U.S.C.S. §§ 1001-1461, did not preempt the state legislature's enactment of § 171.109(a)(1); thus, the legislation was valid. Finally, the court determined that the state statute did not violate the requirement that all taxpayers be subject to the same tax and deductions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment granted by the district court in favor of appellee corporation-taxpayer and against appellants, comptroller and other state officials. The state statute regarding the disputed tax was not preempted by federal law and did not violate the Texas constitution by failing to uniformly tax like taxpayers and appellee could not deduct uncertain amounts from its tax debt. The cause was remanded.

 

953 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Steiner v. State


Appeal No. 04-95-00031-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4052



September 11, 1996, Delivered  
September 11, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 198th Judicial District Court of Kerr County. Trial Court No. B93-158. Honorable Emil Karl Prohl, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for capital murder from the 198th Judicial District Court of Kerr County (Texas), claiming that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motions to suppress his oral and written statements.


OVERVIEW: In oral and written statements, appellant admitted to planning and killing the victims. Before trial on the charge of capital murder, appellant moved to suppress the statements, alleging that the statements were unconstitutionally taken after invoking his right to counsel and were not taken in compliance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 39(a)(2). The trial court denied the motions and, thereafter, found appellant guilty as charged. Appellant sought review, claiming that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motions. The court affirmed the decision. Although unrebutted allegations of coercive acts rendered a confession inadmissible as a matter of law, the rule applied only when the accused established that the unrefuted allegations standing on their own initially showed coercion. Implicit in the trial court's ruling that appellant waived his invoked right to an attorney freely and voluntarily, without promises threats, or coercion was the finding that appellant's will was not overborne by a police officer's threat to throw appellant to the wolves if he did not cooperate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motions to suppress. Allegations of coercive acts did not render appellant's confession inadmissible because appellant failed to show that the allegations standing alone showed coercion.

 

954 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Li v. State


NO. 03-95-00560-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4094



September 11, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BELL COUNTY, 27TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 45,402, HONORABLE JOE CARROLL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found him guilty of capital murder, appellant sought review of his conviction and life sentence imposed by the District Court of Bell County, 27th Judicial District (Texas). Appellant challenged the admission of crime-scene photographs, hearsay testimony, and the sufficiency of the evidence. He contended that the capital-murder punishment statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of capital murder and sentenced to life imprisonment in the robbery and fatal stabbing of a pawnshop clerk. On appeal, the court held that the admission of photos of the victim for their probative value was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion. Noting that statements by a coconspirator made during the course and in furtherance of the conspiracy were not hearsay, the court held that the exception applied to testimony by accomplice witnesses. The court held that the evidence showed that appellant had agreed with his coconspirators to rob the pawnshop and kill the clerk, which was corroborated by non-accomplice testimony and evidence. Appellant had not objected to much of the evidence that linked him to the crime. Based on the jury charge of the parties on the offense and the law, the court affirmed his conviction, holding that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to find that appellant had taken part in the robbery and murder. The court rejected appellant's claim that the capital murder sentencing statute was unconstitutional because of mitigation of the death penalty as statutorily granted by his status as a minor and resulting life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder in the robbery and stabbing death of a pawnshop clerk. The court held that photos of the victim were properly admitted for their probative value, that testimony by coconspirators was not hearsay, that the appellant's participation was corroborated by non-accomplice evidence sufficient to support a finding of guilt, and that his life sentence as a minor was not unconstitutional.

Hawkins v. State


NO. 14-95-00819-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4017



September 5, 1996, rendered  
September 5, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 656561.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 176th District Court, Harris County (Texas) which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child. The trial court previously deferred an adjudication of guilt and placed appellant on probation for a term of 10 years after he pled guilty without the benefit of a plea agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a guilty plea to aggravated sexual assault of a child and was placed upon probation. On appeal, the court affirmed the adjudication. Appellant contended that the admonition of the trial court, asking appellant if he understood that he could be sentenced to life in prison if he violated the conditions of his probation, failed to adequately warn him of the possible consequences of a violation and rendered his plea involuntary. The court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 (Supp. 1996) did not require that appellant be informed of the possible consequences of a probation violation prior to his plea. The court rejected appellant's contention that the trial judge was required to admonish appellant that if he was not a citizen, he could face the possibility of deportation, because the judge asked appellant whether or not he was a citizen and he responded that he was. The court found that while Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (Supp. 1996) applied only to cases where a defendant has chosen to enter a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, it did not prevent appellant from offering exculpatory evidence; thus, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child; he was properly admonished as to the consequences of probation violation and of deportation.

 

956 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Texas Educ. Agency v. Maxwell


No. 11-95-234-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 4037



September 5, 1996, Decided  
September 5, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from 295th District Court of Harris County



DISPOSITION: The injunction is vacated and set aside as moot, and the denial of attorney's fees is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state education agency and appellee parents each sought review of the judgment of the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas) which enjoined appellant from administering the Texas Assessment of Academic Skills test unless appellee was given an opportunity to view a correct copy of the test after it was administered and graded.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents brought suit against appellant state education agency, alleging that their constitutional rights had been violated. The trial court found, under the then existing statute, that the statute unconstitutionally infringed upon the fundamental right of parents to direct the upbringing and education of their children. Thereupon, the trial court enjoined appellant from administering the Texas Assessment of Academic Skills test unless appellee was provided the opportunity to view a true and correct copy of the test after it had been administered and graded. In addition, the court did not award attorney's fees to appellee. On review, the court vacated the injunction, set it aside as moot, and affirmed the denial of attorney's fees. The court noted that the legislature had subsequently repealed the statute in question and therefore the constitutionality of that statute was moot. In addition, the court found that appellee was not entitled to attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, because appellant was not a "person" subject to liability under a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellee parent's injunction against appellant state education agency, set the injunction aside as moot, and affirmed the denial of appellee's request for attorney's fees. The court noted that the legislature had repealed the statute at issue and that therefore the constitutionality of the statute was moot. The court also noted that appellant was not a "person" subject to liability for attorney's fees under appellee's claim.

 

957 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re D.S.


Appeal No. 04-95-00597-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3865



August 30, 1996, Delivered  
August 30, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 73rd District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-JUV-0766. Honorable Frank Montalvo, Judge Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Appellant's Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 12, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2328.



DISPOSITION: APPELLANT'S MOTION FOR REHEARING DENIED; JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order entered by the 73rd District Court of Bexar County, Texas, which transferred jurisdiction of appellant's capital murder case from the juvenile court to the criminal district court. Appellant claimed that his constitutional and statutory rights were violated by the admission of references to his statements, criminal history, hearsay reports, and a report from a psychological evaluation based on an ex-parte order.


OVERVIEW: After appellant's capital murder case was transferred from the juvenile court to the criminal district court, appellant claimed that his constitutional and statutory rights were violated because the transfer hearing judge admitted statements he made to the police, his criminal history, reports based on hearsay, and a psychological report that was ordered on an ex-parte basis. The court affirmed the transfer. The court held that any error in the admission of the statements was harmless error because the statements were not critical to finding of probable cause because there was other independent evidence that established it. The court held that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.02(e) required appellant's prior criminal history to be considered in the transfer hearing. The court held that Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 101(b) permitted the juvenile court to consider reports that were otherwise hearsay. The court observed that appellant not only had notice that the hearsay reports were going to be introduced, but also had a copy of the reports. Finally, the court held that there was no constitutional violation in admitting the psychological evaluation because appellant was given a copy of it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the transfer of appellant's capital murder case from the juvenile court to the criminal district court. The court held that it was harmless error to admit appellant's statements because there was independent evidence to establish probable cause. The court held that the transfer statute required consideration of appellant's prior criminal history, and that evaluation reports were admissible as an exception to hearsay.

 

958 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Shwarts


No. 10-95-064-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


929 S.W.2d 609; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3914



August 30, 1996, delivered  
August 30, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From the 13th District Court. Navarro County, Texas. Trial Court # 94-00-03932-CV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants mother and father challenged an order from the 13th District Court, Navarro County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees doctor and hospital based on the statute of limitations as an affirmative defense in a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother was treated by appellees doctor and hospital in the emergency room prior to the birth of her child. After the birth and subsequent death of that child, appellants mother and father filed a wrongful death action against appellees, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees based on the statute of limitations as an affirmative defense. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court order, holding that in wrongful death actions based on medical malpractice, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 was the controlling limitations statute, not Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) (1986). The court found that the trial court correctly calculated the limitations period from the precise date of the alleged breach of duty, not from the date of the child's birth. The court rejected appellants' claim that the continuous course of treatment doctrine applied, holding that appellant mother was treated on a specific date and that her seven-day wait for lab results was inconsequential to her claim that appellee failed to diagnose her condition. The court concluded that appellants' wrongful death action was barred by art. 4590i, § 10.01.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment in favor of appellees doctor and hospital based on the statute of limitations as an affirmative defense in a wrongful death action because the trial court applied the proper Texas statute and correctly calculated the limitations period from the date of the alleged tort.

Lugo v. State


NO. 14-95-00548-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3854



August 29, 1996, rendered  
August 29, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 313th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 78,041.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the 313th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that imposed a lengthy determinate sentence with appellant being transferred to the institutional division of the department of corrections. Appellant claimed she was unconstitutionally imprisoned as the result of a civil proceeding, which was neither criminal nor a conviction. She also claimed that her sentence was not supported by the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was hired by the complainant's estranged relatives to kill the complainant for the sum of seventy-five dollars. The complainant, an elderly woman, suffered serious continuing injuries from the attempted murder. After conviction, during the punishment proceeding, the trial court, in its findings was moved by the gravity of appellant's offense finding that murder-for-hire was a repulsive and serious offense and that crime was attempted in a premeditated and stalking fashion. The court found no conflict between the determinate sentencing statute and the constitution. The court also noted that, the trial court was under no duty to follow the recommendations of the youth commission and that the determinate sentencing system was designed to strike a balance between the criminal justice system's goal of protecting the public by punishing offenders, and the juvenile system's purpose of providing for the care, the protection, and the moral, mental, and physical development of children. Finally, the court noted that the trial court had sufficient evidence before it from which to make a rational choice as to what punishment to impose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's transfer order that imposed a lengthy determinate sentence with appellant being transferred to the institutional division of the department of corrections. The court found that appellant was not unconstitutionally imprisoned as the result of a civil proceeding, which was neither criminal nor a conviction. Appellant's sentence was proper as it was guided by the evidence and the statutory factors.

Kidd v. State


No. 06-95-00184-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5359


August 23, 1996, Submitted  
August 23, 1996, Decided  
August 23, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 1, 1996. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 6th Judicial District Court. Lamar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 15466.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 6th Judicial District Court, Lamar County (Texas), which accepted defendant's guilty plea of aggravated robbery and sentenced defendant to confinement for 35 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 15 years old at the time of the offense of aggravated burglary. Defendant pled guilty to the charge and a jury trial on punishment resulted in confinement for 35 years. On appeal, defendant argued that his constitutional rights were violated because he was not given Miranda warnings prior to a psychological evaluation, was not afforded effective counsel, and that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.02(d)(1996) was unconstitutional on its face. The state argued that there was no evidence that warnings were not given and that no objection was made to the testimony of the doctor. The court affirmed and held that defendant did not object to the doctor's testimony and therefore waived any rights on appeal. The court held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because it was possible that some of counsel's decision were strategic. The court held that there was a strong presumption in favor of reasonable professional assistance and defendant failed to overcome that presumption. The court held that § 54.02 was constitutional to the extent that diagnostic examinations of a juvenile were conducted and used at the transfer certification hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated burglary. The court held that defendant failed to object to the testimony of the doctor and therefore waived any error on appeal. The court held that defendant failed to overcome the strong presumption that defendant's counsel rendered ineffective assistance.

Markel v. World Flight


Appeal No. 04-95-00893-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


938 S.W.2d 74; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3694



August 21, 1996, Delivered  
August 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 288th Judicial District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court Case Number 95-CI-15486. Honorable Peter Michael Curry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; TEMPORARY INJUNCTION DISSOLVED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public relations company sought review of a temporary injunction ordered by the 288th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), in favor of appellee client.


OVERVIEW: Appellee client alleged that appellant public relations firm was not completing the work as planned, and appellant allegedly intimated that it would discuss the difficulties of the parties with appellee's business contacts. Appellee sought an injunction to prevent such discussions. The injunction precluded communication with over 100 individuals and entities. The court found that appellee had not presented any evidence that could support an injunction, and that it was granted in error. The court determined that appellee failed to show any irreparable injury. The court determined that there was neither trade secret nor confidential relationship between the parties. The court found that the injunction restricted appellant's freedom of expression without evidence of a harmful effect. The court dissolved the injunction and dismissed the appeal from the remainder of the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the temporary injunction and dismissed the appeal from the remainder of the trial court's order, having determined that the injunction was overly broad and restricted appellant public relations company's freedom of expression without evidence of potential harm.

Nelson v. State


No. 05-95-01186-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3752



August 19, 1996, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 3-83925-94.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the County Court at Law No. 3 of Collin County (Texas), which convicted defendant of failure to wear an approved motorcycle helmet pursuant to Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 6701c-3 (1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of failure to wear an approved motorcycle helmet pursuant to Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 6701c-3 (1995). The trial court assessed a $ 50.00 fine against defendant. Defendant challenged his conviction and alleged the statute he was convicted under was unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court noted that because defendant's punishment did not exceed one hundred dollars, the court could only address whether the statute was void on its face and not whether it was unconstitutionally applied to defendant. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 4.03 (1996). The court held that because article 6701-3 could be constitutionally applied to a motorcyclist ridding without a helmet or with a helmet that lacked the required labeling, the statute was not facially unconstitutional. The court reasoned defendant was required to establish that no set of circumstances existed under which the statute would be valid. The court held the fact that the statute did not list the standards and delegated the Department of Public Safety the authority to set and change the standards did not render the statute void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that convicted defendant of failure to wear an approved motorcycle helmet. The court held the statute that defendant was convicted under was constitutional on its face because it could be constitutionally applied to individuals who either failed to wear a helmet or wore an unapproved helmet. The court held the statute was not void where standards were not listed in statute and the standards could be changed.

Fontenot v. State


NO. 2-95-228-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


932 S.W.2d 185; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3650



August 16, 1996, Decided  
August 16, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. SAM HOUSTON.



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of assault from the County Court at Law, Denton County, Texas, where he pleaded nolo contendere pursuant to a plea bargain agreement and was assessed punishment of 90 days in the county jail plus a fine of $ 100, probated for 12 months, in accordance with the state's recommendation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his conviction of assault following his plea of nolo contendere. Pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1), the court determined that it lacked jurisdiction to review defendant's claims of a right to counsel and the alleged involuntariness of his plea, which were nonjurisdictional defects. The court found that defendant had the opportunity to request permission to raise both complaints on appeal in the proceedings related to his motion for new trial, but he failed to do so. Because defendant did not request permission to appeal these issues, the court was without jurisdiction to consider them. The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of his assault conviction. The court held that it lacked jurisdiction because defendant's claim that he did not make a knowing and voluntary waiver of his right to counsel was not jurisdictional and could not be reviewed unless permission to appeal was obtained from the trial court.

 

964 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wooden v. State


No. 08-95-00194-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


929 S.W.2d 77; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3649



August 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 142nd District Court of Midland County, Texas. (TC # CRA-21,032). Trial Court Judge: Hon. George D. Gilles.



DISPOSITION: Having considered and overruled each of Wooden's points of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his aggravated robbery conviction from the 142nd District Court, Midland County (Texas) together with his corresponding sentence of 40 years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged errors under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § (3) in the admission of an extraneous offense in the punishment phase of his trial. Appellant claimed that Tex Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § (3) was unconstitutional because a ruling was not required within a reasonable time prior to trial. The court found that appellant had filed a notice and objection under said statute approximately two weeks before trial and that the trial court had made a ruling within a week of his request. The court found that appellant had not made any specific objection at trial comporting to the errors raised on appeal and concluded that those errors had not been preserved for appeal. The court found that there was no authority for imposing a reasonable time frame on decisions under art. 37.07, § (3), and even if there were, the actions taken by the trial court were timely. In addition, the court determined that the right to a jury trial did not extend to the punishment phase so that appellant's jury election for his punishment did not involve a constitutional right. Accordingly, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's aggravated robbery conviction because appellant had not preserved for appellate review the purported errors concerning the admission of an extraneous offense. The court found that appellant's constitutional rights had not been violated by the admission of the extraneous offense during the punishment phase.

 

965 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Texas Woman's Hosp.


NO. 01-94-00941-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


930 S.W.2d 717; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3658



August 15, 1996, Delivered  
August 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 334th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-00926A. RUSSELL LLOYD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent disputed entry of summary judgment against him by the 334th District Court, Harris County (Texas), on his claim for medical malpractice against appellee corporation. The issue was whether the limitations period of the Medical Liability Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 45990i, § 10.01 (1996) controlled over a survival statute, 1955 Tex. Gen. Laws 239, 294 (current version at Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 7.12 (Supp. 1996)).


OVERVIEW: Appellant parent's son was born with injuries at appellee hospital. Shortly thereafter, appellee increased its malpractice insurance. Appellee dissolved without notifying appellant. When appellant sued for malpractice, the trial court granted summary judgment against him based on the expiration of the corporate survival statute, 1955 Tex. Gen. Laws 239, 294 (current version at Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 7.12 (Supp. 1996)). On appeal, the court noted that appellant had timely filed within the statute of limitations provided by the Medical Malpractice Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 45990i, § 10.01 (1996). The court held that the corporate survival statute governed the case. However, 1967 Tex. Gen. Laws 1717, 1725 (current version at Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 6.04 (Supp. 1996)), required appellee to have given notice of the dissolution to all "known claimants." The court held that there was a material issue of fact as to whether appellant was a "known claimant." Appellee had no basis in the record to argue otherwise. Any issue of appellant's failure to plead the issue had been waived. Therefore, summary judgment was not proper. The court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the corporate survival statute governed the case, not the statute of limitations. The court held that there was an issue of fact as to whether appellant parent was a known claimant who should have received notice of the dissolution of appellee corporation. Any issue of his failure to plead it had been waived. There was no evidence excluding the possibility that appellant was a known claimant.

Grothues v. City of Helotes


Appeal No. 04-93-00151-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


928 S.W.2d 725; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3584



August 14, 1996, Delivered  
August 14, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 285th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 92-CI-11565. Honorable Andy Mireles, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order of the 285th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) granting summary judgment for appellees, arguing that appellee municipality had no authority to grant an exclusive garbage-collection contract to appellee corporation, and to require them to pay its charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellee municipality enacted an ordinance that granted an exclusive garbage-collection contract to appellee corporation. At the same time, another ordinance was enacted that required residents to use appellee corporation exclusively, to pay its charges, and authorized criminal sanctions for failure to do so. Appellants, who were residents and landowners within the city, refused to pay. When they were threatened with a fine, appellants filed suit to declare the ordinances unconstitutional and void. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. The court held that appellee, a general-law municipality, as distinguished from a home-rules municipality, had the authority to grant the contract to appellee corporation. Moreover, enforcement of the comprehensive garbage collection plan was clearly within the police power granted to all municipalities.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment for appellee municipality was affirmed because the enforcement of a comprehensive garbage collection plan was clearly within the police power granted to all municipalities.

Francis v. Gill

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3602

August 14, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 278th District Court of Walker County, Texas. Trial Court No. 18,947-C. Honorable Jerry A. Sandel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the judgment of the 278th District Court of Walker County (Texas), which dismissed as frivolous, pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001, his in forma pauperis complaint against appellee prison food service employees, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, in which appellant alleged that appellees conspired to deprive him of his rights under U.S. Const. amends. I & XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a written grievance with the Texas Department of Criminal Justice, complaining of unequal treatment by appellee prison food service employees. Thereafter, appellees allegedly placed him in fear of his life, capriciously changed their procedures to mislead him, and spread rumors about him. Appellant filed an in forma pauperis complaint against appellees, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging that appellees conspired to deny him of his rights, under U.S. Const. amends. I & XIV. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing as frivolous appellant inmate's in forma pauperis complaint against appellee prison food service employees for conspiring to deny his First and Fourteenth Amendment rights, as appellant's complaint was without basis in law or fact, and that the statute allowing dismissal of in forma pauperis complaints as frivolous was constitutional.

 

968 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tivoli Corp. v. Jewelers Mut. Ins. Co.


Appeal No. 04-95-00135-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


932 S.W.2d 704; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3616



August 14, 1996, Delivered  
August 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied October 10, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Overruled September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 61st District Court of Harris County. Trial Court No. 92-46202. Honorable Shearn Smith, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company challenged the entry of summary judgment favoring defendant insurer and agent by the 61st District Court of Harris County (Texas), denying plaintiff's claim for coverage under an insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff company purchased an insurance policy from defendant insurer to cover jewelry and precious stones. The jewelry was subsequently stolen out of the trunk of one of plaintiff's salesman while the salesman was away from the car. Defendant insurer denied plaintiff's claim for coverage of the loss. Plaintiff filed suit and the trial court granted summary judgment favoring defendant insurer and defendant agent. The court affirmed. It was undisputed that the loss occurred while the jewelry was in transit. The insurance policy provided that the insured property was covered while in transit only if it was in the possession of the person who was transporting it. The policy expressly disclaimed coverage for losses associated with a vehicle that was left unattended. The court rejected plaintiff's contention that the assignment of the judge in the matter was violative of the state constitution. The court held that the legislature was authorized to assign a judge when the elected judge was absent, disabled or otherwise disqualified. Notice to the parties of such assignment was not required. Procedural defects regarding the summary judgment motions and hearing were harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of summary judgment by the district court, favoring defendant insurer and agent. The jewelry which plaintiff insured under a policy with defendant insurer was left unattended in a vehicle at the time of the theft and therefore was excluded from coverage under the express language of the policy. The judge deciding the motion was authorized to do so and procedural defects pertaining to the motion were harmless.

Walker v. Argonaut Southwest Ins. Co.


No. 06-96-00031-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


929 S.W.2d 499; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3533


August 6, 1996, Submitted  
August 12, 1996, Decided  
August 12, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 76th Judicial District Court. Titus County, Texas. Trial Court No. 24,891.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and the cause REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged a judgment from the 76th Judicial District Court, Titus County (Texas), in an action for workers' compensation benefits, where the trial court had dismissed his appeal for want of jurisdiction. Appellant contended that the trial court had jurisdiction to hear his appeal from the final order of the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment dismissing his case for want of jurisdiction to hear his appeal from a final decision of the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission. Appellant had been injured in an on-the-job accident. He filed for and received workers' compensation but was dissatisfied with the award. He appealed within agency guidelines, and the appeals panel affirmed the award. He then sought judicial review of the decision, alleging that the award was not supported by the evidence and that the new version of the Workers' Compensation Act was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that it lacked jurisdiction and dismissed the case. The appellate court reversed and remanded. The constitutionality of a provision of the workers' compensation act was subject to judicial review. The fact that the outcome was questionable or even that a loss on the merits was likely did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction over the constitutionality issue. Even if it appeared from a surface reading of the petition that appellant would have lost on the merits, that would not have divested the trial court of jurisdiction over the case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment from the trial court dismissing, on jurisdictional grounds, appellant claimant's appeal from a final order from the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission (Commission), because the fact that the outcome of appellant's cause before the Commission was questionable did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction.

Snare v. State


No. 05-91-01102-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3537



August 12, 1996, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 5. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F90-16138-L.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision from the Criminal District Court No. 5, Dallas County (Texas), which revoked his deferred adjudication probation, found appellant guilty of burglary of a habitation, and assessed his punishment at 10 years confinement and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled to burglary of a habitation and later had his deferred adjudication probation revoked and was found guilty for the offense. He appealed his conviction arguing, inter alia, that his plea was not voluntarily given because he was not properly admonished about the consequences of a violation of probation. The court held that, although the information requirement was mandatory, the trial court's failure to admonish him before accepting his plea did not render his plea involuntary. The court held that the legislature placed the informational requirement after the acceptance of the plea language thereby showing that it did not intend the informational requirement to be a condition precedent to a voluntary plea. The court also held that, because appellant filed a general notice of appeal, he failed to confer jurisdiction on the appellate court to hear anything other than jurisdictional issues. The general notice of appeal foreclosed even review of constitutional issues. The court therefore dismissed the other errors for want of jurisdiction and affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed because the trial court's failure to admonish him as to the consequences of a probation violation did not render his plea involuntary, and because appellant failed to confer jurisdiction on the appellate court to hear his other issues by filing only a general notice of appeal.

Clarke v. State


NO. 2-94-250-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


928 S.W.2d 709; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3513



August 8, 1996, Decided  
August 8, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 19, 1996.
Rehearing overruled by, 09/19/1996
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 04/02/1997
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion denied by Clarke v. Dir., 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 55302 (E.D. Tex., June 30, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Clarke v. Dir., Tex. Dep't of Crim. Justice-Corr. Insts. Div., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 133885 (E.D. Tex., Aug. 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 158TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. PHILLIP VICK.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of February 29, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 815.
Clarke v. State, 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 815 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, Feb. 29, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Having overruled all eight points of error, we affirm Clarke's conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 158th District Court of Denton County (Texas) of aggravated sexual assault. The court previously handed down an opinion and published only those portions of the opinion addressing the speedy trial and venue points of error. Appellant filed his amended motion for rehearing in the case, which the court granted.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault. On appeal, he argued that the state violated his right to a speedy trial because his punishment was tried two years and five months after the United States Supreme Court denied certiorari on his first case. He argued that the court incorrectly applied an abuse of discretion standard in reviewing the trial court's analysis of a speedy trial claim. The court held there was not a valid reason for a delay. Because the state did not meet its burden in excusing the delay, the delay weighed against the state. However, because appellant delayed in asserting his right for over two years, filed his motion with 32 others, failed to separately set it for hearing, and pursued a dismissal rather than an accelerated trial setting, the court could not say that he timely asserted his right. Appellant argued the delay impaired his defense. The court held appellant failed to make a prima facie showing of prejudice caused by the delay because of missing character witnesses. While there was prejudice when the jury considered the convictions in appellant's extraneous offenses, the prejudice weighed equally between the parties. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault. The court applied a balancing test de novo to find that while the delay triggered the speedy trial analysis, and there was no valid reason for the delay, defendant failed to timely assert his right and this contributed greatly to the impairment of the defense.

Jackson v. State


NO. 14-95-00761-CR, NO. 14-95-00765-CR, NO. 14-95-00769-CR

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 694,354; 694,658; 694,659.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions, entered in the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), for robbery by felony.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea agreement, appellant pleaded guilty to three counts of robbery by felony. In accordance with the plea agreement, the trial court sentenced appellant to 15 years of confinement. Appellant filed a notice of appeal, but neither the notice of appeal nor the record reflected that permission to appeal was sought from or granted by the trial court. The court held that, because appellant pleaded guilty and the punishment did not exceed that recommend as a result of the plea bargain, Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) required appellant to obtain the permission of the trial court prior to appeal, except in certain circumstances. The court found that none of the exceptions to Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) applied. The court held that it did not have jurisdiction to consider the appeal. Therefore, the trial court dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction because appellant's convictions were pursuant to a guilty plea, and appellant failed to get the trial court's permission to appeal.

Blessing v. State


NO. 01-95-00251-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


927 S.W.2d 310; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3329



August 1, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 152nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-47811. P.K. REITER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) that entered a judgment of forfeiture of real estate that was used in the commission of a felony, pursuant to Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. 481 (Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: The district court entered a judgment of forfeiture of real estate that was used in the commission of a felony, pursuant to Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. 481 (Supp. 1996). Appellants argued that the forfeiture judgment violated the double jeopardy clauses of the U.S. Constitution, U.S. Const. amend V, and Texas Constitution, Tex. Const. art. I, § 14. The appeals court affirmed, holding that the forfeiture of the real estate was not punishment for the purposes of the double jeopardy clauses. The forfeiture was a civil sanction and it did not constitute punishment for the purpose of the state and federal double jeopardy clauses. The criminal action and the civil forfeiture were parallel proceedings and did not violate appellant's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the district court that entered a judgment of forfeiture of real estate that was used in the commission of a felony, holding that the forfeiture was a civil sanction and it did not constitute punishment for the purpose of the state and federal double jeopardy clauses. Thus, the forfeiture did not violate the double jeopardy clauses of the state and federal constitutions.

Ben Robinson Co. v. Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n


NO. 03-95-00522-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


934 S.W.2d 149; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3277; 1997 OSHD (CCH) P31,201; 17 OSHC (BNA) 1689



July 31, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 16, 1996. Released for Publication October 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-03955, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order from the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee Workers' Compensation Commission and its members and denying appellant's request for a declaratory judgment that the Occupational Safety and Health Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 651, preempted the Extra-Hazardous Employer Program, Tex. Lab. Code. Ann. § 411.041 (1996).


OVERVIEW: After a fatal accident at the workplace of appellant employer, the Workers' Health and Safety Division of the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission identified appellant as an extra-hazardous employer pursuant to the Extra-Hazardous Employer Program (Program), Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 411.041(b) (1996). Although appellant challenged this designation, it complied with the statutory requirements, and the commission removed appellant's extra-hazardous status. Appellant filed a petition in the trial court seeking a declaratory judgment that the Occupational Safety and Health Act (OSHA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 651, preempted the Program, but the trial court denied appellant's request. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order, holding that a controversy still existed and that appellant could challenge the constitutional validity of the Program outside of the statutory remedy. The court determined that the Program addressed workplace safety issues for which an OSHA standard was already in effect; therefore, the Program was preempted by OSHA. The court also found that appellant was entitled to costs and attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying appellant employer's request for a declaratory judgment because the Occupational Safety and Health Act (OSHA) preempted Texas' Extra-Hazardous Employer Program on workplace safety issues where an OSHA standard was in effect. The case was remanded to the trial court for an award of costs and attorney's fees.

McCollister v. State


No. 11-94-180-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


933 S.W.2d 170; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3191



July 25, 1996, Decided  
July 25, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 90th District Court of Stephens County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his murder conviction entered in the 90th District Court of Stephens County (Texas). Defendant contended that a defendant must have had knowledge that the murder victim was under the age of six years to be convicted under Tex. Penal. Code. Ann. § 19.03(a)(8) (1994). Defendant also argued that state improperly commented upon his failure to testify at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. The record showed defendant murdered his 23-month-old step-daughter. Defendant hit the victim with his fist above her eye, causing her to fall against the couch. Defendant then hit the victim's head again. Then, defendant picked the victim up and shook her until he noticed blood coming out of her mouth. He washed her off, put her in the car, and took her to the nursing home where his wife was working. The victim was unconscious when she arrived at the nursing home and remained unconscious until she died four days later. The victim died from trauma to her brain due to blunt force injuries of the head. The court affirmed the conviction and found that any impropriety in state's remarks were invited by defendant and, because he did not object, the error was not preserved for review. The court noted that defendant's remaining issues turned on his contention that the statute required that he have knowledge that the victim was under six years of age. The court found that the language of the statute contained no such requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder because defendant's lack of knowledge that the victim was under six years old did not show that his conviction was improper because knowledge of the victim's age was not an element of the offense. Moreover, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and state's arguments, if improper, were not preserved for appellate review.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision from the 189th District Court. Harris County (Texas), which found appellee bar and bartender not liable for 19-year old's injuries sustained in an automobile accident after she and driver purchased beer from appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant 19-year old was injured in an automobile accident after she and driver had obtained beer using a fake identification card. The jury found appellant to be 100 percent liable for her injuries and no liability on the part of appellee bar or bartender. On appeal, appellant argued appellees violated a statutory standard of care when they sold alcohol to appellant and she should have been permitted to pursue a common law action for negligence against appellees. The court found no violation of the Equal Protection Clause as its purpose was not arbitrary and capricious. The court held that appellant child's comparative negligence defense, which barred all or part of appellant's recovery and had the same effect on the parent's recovery for loss of consortium. Because the jury found appellant 100 percent liable, all recovery was barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying recovery for injuries sustained in an automobile accident because the Dram Shop Act, which precluded her maintaining an action against appellee bar and bartender, was not arbitrary and capricious, and the jury finding that she was fully liable for her injuries barred recovery by her parents.

In re B.N.E.


NO. 01-95-01101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


927 S.W.2d 271; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3044



July 18, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 314th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 75,969 Re-Opened. MARY CRAFT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a decision by the 314th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which waived jurisdiction over her and transferred her to the criminal district court for criminal proceedings against her for aggravated robbery and robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was charged by petition in the juvenile court with delinquent conduct: aggravated robbery and robbery. The juvenile court waived its jurisdiction and transferred appellant for trial as an adult in the criminal district court. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court considered appellant's argument that the juvenile court erred in its refusal to allow appellant to present alibi witnesses at the certification hearing. The court found no error and explained that the juvenile court was not required to receive appellant's alibi evidence, because probable cause that appellant committed the offenses had been established to the juvenile court's satisfaction. The court rejected appellant's argument that the juvenile court erred in refusing to permit appellant to make an offer of proof after the juvenile court had ruled appellant's alibi witnesses could not testify. The court found that the juvenile court allowed appellant to make an offer of proof in which appellant summarized the testimony of her alibi witnesses. The court rejected appellant's argument that the juvenile court considered inadmissible evidence in her transfer hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the juvenile court properly waived jurisdiction over appellant and transferred her case to the district court for criminal proceedings. The juvenile court was not required to consider the testimony of alibi witnesses, nor was it required to accept an offer of proof in question and answer form.

Emerson v. Borland


NO. 03-95-00023-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


927 S.W.2d 709; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3010



July 17, 1996, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 435,470, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), for appellee claiming they were immune from liability on the basis of qualified and official immunity in appellee's action for false imprisonment pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellee brought a false imprisonment action against appellants, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, following appellee's arrest and imprisonment for violating a state statute prohibiting the sale of fire extinguishers which were not approved by a nationally recognized or state approved testing laboratory. Appellants challenged a judgment for appellee on grounds that they were immune from suit on the basis of qualified and official immunity. The court reversed the judgment, holding appellants were entitled to qualified immunity because their lack of knowledge did not give rise to an inference of bad faith or reckless conduct, and appellee's arrest and detention were not unlawful under state law, as it was objectively reasonable for appellants to believe that their superiors' interpretation of the law was correct and the warrant was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee on a false imprisonment charge, holding appellants were entitled to qualified immunity because their conduct was not reckless or in bad faith. Appellee's detention was legal because it was objectively reasonable for appellants to believe that their superiors' interpretation of state law was correct.

Sills v. State


NO. 14-94-00770-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2919



July 11, 1996, rendered  
July 11, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 678279.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas) that convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault of a child on the ground that he was denied the right to compulsory process, that there was no waiver, that the sentence was cruel and unusual, and that the trial court erred in reviewing a presentence report prior to the verdict and in considering an extraneous unadjudicated sexual assault allegation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated sexual assault of a child and pled guilty without an agreed recommendation as to punishment. The trial court withheld a finding of guilt until a presentence report had been prepared and then entered a finding of guilt and assessed punishment. Defendant contended his conviction and sentence were improper because he was unconstitutionally denied his right to compulsory process, his plea of guilty did not contain a waiver of his right to compulsory process, his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment, and the trial court erred in reviewing his presentence report prior to entering its finding of guilt and in considering an extraneous unadjudicated sexual assault allegation during the punishment phase of trial. The court affirmed the judgment and held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 1.15 was not unconstitutional and did not deprive defendant of compulsory process. The court found defendant waived any rights by entering a guilty plea and that the presentence report did not influence the trial judge except to determine an appropriate sentence. The court ruled that defendant's failure to object to admitting evidence waived any error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child was affirmed because there was no constitutional denial of compulsory process, and defendant waived any rights with a guilty plea. Moreover, the sentence imposed was within the range prescribed by statute, and the review of the presentence report did not influence the trial judge. Finally, defendant waived any error regarding cumulative testimony by failing to object at trial.

 

981 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hocutt v. State


NO. 2-95-533-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


927 S.W.2d 201; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2946



July 11, 1996, Decided  
July 11, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Motion for Rehearing En Banc Overruled September 12, 1996. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 211TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. L. DEE SHIPMAN.



DISPOSITION: Affirm the conviction and reverse and remand for new trial on punishment only.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction of felony driving while intoxicated entered by the 211th District Court of Denton County (Texas). Defendant contended that the trial court erred by submitting a special issue to the jury regarding the use of a deadly weapon because defendant was not given adequate notice of the state's intent to seek such a finding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony driving while impaired and appealed, contending that the trial court erred by charging the jury at the punishment phase with a special issue in regard to the use of a deadly weapon. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but reversed and remanded for a new trial on punishment. The court found that the state did not give defendant notice of its intent to seek a deadly weapon finding until the Friday before her Monday trial date. In addition, the notice that was faxed to defendant's counsel did not specify the nature of the deadly weapon. The court concluded that the state failed to provide adequate notice of its intent to submit a deadly weapon special issue, and that this failure constituted fundamental error. The court determined that the jury was concerned about the effect of a deadly weapon finding based upon a note it sent to the trial court asking about the implications of the special issue. Thus, the court could not conclude that the error in submitting the special issue to the jury was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but reversed and remanded for a new trial on punishment. The court held that defendant was not given adequate notice of the state's intent to seek a deadly weapon finding, and that the error in submitting the special issue to the jury was not harmless.

Hughes v. Aycock


NO. 01-95-01181-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 3489



July 11, 1996, rendered and delivered  
July 11, 1996, filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS TULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Writ of Error Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction March 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-59763.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctors sought review of an judgment from the 234th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied appellants motion for summary judgment in their bill of review action and granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, medical partnership and individuals. Appellants also challenged the orders of the trial court that awarded appellees sanctions against appellants and denied appellants' request for sanctions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant doctors filed a bill of review action that sought to overturn a permanent injunction that was ordered against them that prohibited them from filing a new cause of action against appellees, medical partnership and individuals, without leave of court. Appellants also sought to have appellees perform an accounting. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees and awarded sanctions against appellants. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the injunction did not violate the open courts doctrine of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court noted that a permanent injunction could be issued for vexatious, harassing litigation. The court found appellants claim for accounting was barred by four-year statute of limitations. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.004 (c) (1986). The court held that sanctions were proper against appellants where bill of review filed by appellants was groundless.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed the summary judgment that was granted in favor of appellees, medical partnership and individuals, because appellant doctors' bill of review claim for accounting was barred by statute of limitations and claim that sought relief from permanent injunction was groundless. L.E.S. v. State


Appeal No. 04-95-00677-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2812



July 10, 1996, Delivered  
July 10, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 225th Judicial District of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-JUV-2556. Honorable Robert L. Eschenburg, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 225th Judicial District of Bexar County (Texas), which found him guilty of aggravated sexual assault of a child, claiming that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the defense of mistake of fact, and that the state sexual assault statute unfairly discriminates based on age.


OVERVIEW: Appellant adult male had sexual intercourse with a 14-year old female, whom he thought was 15. Appellant was tried and convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Tex. Penal Code Ann. §22.021 (1996). Appellant challenged his conviction, arguing that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the defense of mistake of fact, and that the state sexual assault statute unfairly discriminated against him on the basis of age. The court held that when a charge of any sexual offense against a child is made, mistake of fact or appellant's ignorance of the victim's age was not a valid defense. The court also determined that the classification created by the statute was justified in protecting children under a certain age who are more vulnerable to the emotional trauma brought on by sexual contact. The court stated that enhanced punishment for aggravated sexual assault bore a fair and substantial relation to the objective of protecting children under the age of fourteen. The court concluded that appellant was correctly charged with aggravated sexual assault and therefore could not use the defense that he and the victim were less than three years apart.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, upholding appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child, stating that mistake of fact or appellant's ignorance of the victim's age was not a valid defense, and that the state criminal statute for aggravated sexual assault bore a fair and substantial relation to the objective of protecting children under the age of fourteen, and therefore was not illegal age discrimination.

McLendon v. Mandel


No. 05-96-00160-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS

Appellant contended that the trial court exceeded its postjudgment jurisdiction when it granted the injunction, that the injunction was erroneous because it constituted an unconstitutional garnishment of appellant's wages, and that the injunction was erroneous because it seized property exempt by statute. Wemken v. State


No. 05-92-02842-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2762



July 3, 1996, OPINION FILED


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F90-00965-JI.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 2 Dallas County, Texas, which convicted defendant of misapplication of fiduciary property and assessed punishment at 10 years confinement, probated for three years, and fined at $ 500.00.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of misapplication of fiduciary property. On appeal defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction because defendant paid back a certain amount of the funds therefore making unlikely the property would be recovered as opposed to there being a substantial risk of loss. The defendant also argued that the trial court erred in not setting aside his conviction and dismissing the indictment pending defendant's appeal. The court affirmed and stated that substantial risk of loss need not rise to a level of substantial certainty, but had to be a positive possibility. The court held that a rational trier of fact could have found that the funds would not have been recovered if defendant were not confronted. The court held that the trial court's authority to take any action not expressly permitted by statute remains suspended until they received the mandate from the court. The court held that defendant's terms of probation did not commence until the clerk of the trial court received the mandate of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of misapplication of fiduciary property because the evidence supported a positive possibility that the funds would not have been recovered if defendant was not confronted. The court held that the trial court did not have authority to enter any order unless expressly permitted by statute, and that defendant's term of probation did not begin until the trial court received the mandate from the court.

Wright v. State


No. 05-95-00778-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


930 S.W.2d 131; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2766



July 3, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F94-59989-TK.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 4, Dallas County, Texas, which convicted defendant of delivery of less than one gram of cocaine, after he pled nolo contendere to the charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of delivery of less than one gram of cocaine after he pled nolo contendere to the charge. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient because it only showed that he possessed the cocaine and also argued that the assessed fine violated his rights under U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV. The court affirmed and held that when a defendant pleads nolo contendere, he cannot be convicted upon his plea alone without sufficient evidence. The court stated that defendant waived in writing the appearance, confrontation and cross-examination of witnesses and consented to a stipulation of evidence by affidavits. The court held that the evidence defendant stipulated to encompassed the factual allegations and embraced every essential element of the offense charged. The court held that constitutional rights may be waived by failure to make a timely assertion of that right. The court stated that even if defendant preserved error on his assessed fine, the court concluded it was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of delivery of less than one gram of cocaine. The court held that defendant stipulated to evidence which reiterated his waiver of appearance, confrontation, and cross-examination of witnesses. The court stated that the stipulation of evidence is a judicial confession because in it defendant conceded the factual allegations in the indictment to be true and correct.

Loughry v. State


NO. 2-95-161-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


926 S.W.2d 382; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2774



July 3, 1996, Decided  
July 3, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF WICHITA COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. TOM BACUS.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed, and this case is remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the County Court At Law, No. 2 of Wichita County, (Texas), which found him guilty of perjury, a class A misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of perjury and argued that the trial court erred when it granted state's challenge for cause of a qualified juror. Defendant argued that there was insufficient proof that venireperson had been convicted of theft, the basis of state's challenge. The court reversed and held that when state used all of its peremptory challenges on other venirepersons, it was improper for the trial court to grant state a challenge for cause because the juror was not absolutely disqualified. The court held that where a juror who served on the jury was shown to be absolutely disqualified, defendant need not show harm for the case to be reversed. The court held that where a venireperson unequivocally denied a theft or felony conviction and defendant questioned the source of state's information supporting the challenge for cause, state must disclose the basis for its information.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of perjury because the state used all of its peremptory challenges and when the trial court granted a challenge for cause where the juror was not absolutely disqualified, it in effect granted state an additional peremptory challenge and was an abuse of discretion.

Johnson v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine in the 363rd District Court of Dallas County, (Texas), and on appeal, she contended that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the conviction, and that appellant should have been punished as a state jail felon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged her conviction for possession of cocaine. In short, the appellate court affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of cocaine, finding the evidence was legally and factually sufficient, appellant had waived some errors by failing to object at trial, and that she was sentenced according to the appropriate statute, which was not the state jail felon statute, as it had been amended prior to the offense.
