Johnson v. State


NO. 14-94-00900-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2466



June 20, 1996, rendered  
June 20, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 641370.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 263rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which found him guilty of murder and which assessed his punishment at confinement for a term of 60 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the offense of murder without an agreed recommendation as to punishment. The trial court entered a finding of guilt after an investigation report was prepared and then sentenced defendant to 60 years confinement. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court determined that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1996), which required that the state introduce evidence into the record showing defendant's guilt where he pled guilty or nolo contendere, was not unconstitutional because defendant was not prohibited from offering rebuttal evidence. The court further determined that defendant's plea of guilty constituted an affirmative waiver of his right to compulsory process. Moreover, the court determined that because defendant's sentence fell within the statutorily prescribed range, it was not cruel or unusual. The court concluded that because defendant had pled guilty, had signed a confession, and had stipulated to evidence of his guilt, the trial court's review of the presentence report could not have influenced the judge, except in considering the appropriate punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court found that defendant had waived his right to compulsory process by pleading guilty, that his sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment because it was within the range allowed by statute, and that the trial court's review of the sentence report could not have affected its determination of guilt.

Ramos v. State


NO. 14-94-00526-CR, NO. 14-94-00528-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


928 S.W.2d 160; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2467



June 20, 1996, Rendered  
June 20, 1996, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 679,162 and 679,164. Hon. Wendell Odom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendants of delivery of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer negotiated a sale of cocaine with a narcotics broker, who arranged for his sources to deliver the cocaine to his apartment. Shortly after the officer arrived at the apartment, defendants joined him and produced a package that actually contained dominoes but that appeared to the officer to be cocaine. Defendants were arrested and convicted of delivery of a controlled substance. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that defendants should have been indicted for the lesser offense of delivery of a simulated controlled substance because it was the more specific statute and because it proscribed the particular conduct of which they were accused. A prior case dictated that the offense of delivery of a controlled substance was complete when someone offered to sell what he represented to be a controlled substance, but the statute making delivery of a simulated controlled substance had not been enacted at the time the prior case was decided.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendants' convictions for delivery of a controlled substance with instructions for the trial court to dismiss the indictment against them. The court concluded that when two statutes were in pari materia, the more specific statute that addressed the particular conduct of the accused should have been applied.

Bloch v. Dowell Schlumberger Inc.


NO. 01-95-01548-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


925 S.W.2d 301; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2306



June 6, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from County Court at Law Number One. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 645704. EUGENE CHAMBERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the order of the County Court at Law, Harris County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in appellant's breach of contract action for recovery of severance pay under appellee's written severance plan. Appellant claimed that a wage claimant was not required to exhaust all administrative remedies through the Texas Workforce Commission before filing a civil lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee brought a breach of contract action for severance pay benefits owed him under appellee employer's severance plan. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, holding that The Payday Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. 61.001-.095 (1996) provided that an administrative wage claim through the Texas Workforce Commission (commission) was a mandatory prerequisite to filing a civil suit. On appeal, the court reversed and held that appellant did not have to exhaust administrative remedies before filing suit for severance pay. Appellee argued that appellant was prohibited from relying on an unpublished case pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 90(1) to support its position on appeal. The court held that the prohibition against citation to "unpublished" opinions only prohibited citation to opinions not designated for publication. The court further held that the exhaustion of administrative remedies through the commission was not a mandatory prerequisite to filing a civil action. Because the Payday Act was neither cumulative of the common-law remedy, nor did it negate or deny the common-law remedy, it would have been unconstitutional if it were a mandatory remedy.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in appellant's breach of contract action for recovery of severance pay benefits owed him under appellee's written severance plan was reversed because the exhaustion of administrative remedies through the commission was not a mandatory prerequisite to filing a civil action.

Patterson v. State


NO. 01-94-00615-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2196



May 30, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 278th District Court. Grimes County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 12,803.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reformed and affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 278th District Court, Grimes County (Texas), which convicted him of murder. Appellant complained of errors in the refusal of the trial court to, among other things, instruct on self-defense, on lesser included offenses, and in disregarding the prosecutor's argument on sudden passion.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder and reformed the judgment to show the correct commencement date of his sentence. The victim had been stabbed with a knife on a sidewalk after an altercation in a nightclub. The court found that the trial court did not err in refusing to submit a jury instruction on self-defense, because the evidence did not raise the issue of self-defense. The evidence showed that the victim did not utilize deadly force. The trial court did not err in refusing to charge the jury on the lesser included offenses of involuntary manslaughter and criminally negligent homicide because all of the evidence showed that appellant intended to kill the victim. Appellant's claims that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury to disregard the prosecutor's argument on sudden passion were overruled by the court because appellant waived error by not asking for an instruction to disregard or a mistrial. The court found that the trial court did not err under Tex. R. Crim. P. 405(a) in allowing the state to cross-examine two of appellant's character witnesses during the punishment phase about appellant's prior arrest for possession of cocaine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder because the trial court properly refused to instruct on self-defense where the evidence showed that the victim did not utilize deadly force. An instruction of lesser included offenses was not required since there was nothing in the record to suggest that the stabbing was anything but intentional.

Rao v. Rodriguez


No. 09-95-256 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


923 S.W.2d 176; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1995


January 18, 1996, Submitted  
May 16, 1996, Delivered  
May 16, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 75th District Court, Liberty County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 47789. Honorable J. C. Zbranek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a tenant, sought review of the judgment n.o.v. from the 75th District Court, Liberty County, Texas that set aside the jury verdict in his favor on his common law claims and claims under the Texas smoke detector statute, Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 92.252 (1995), against appellees, his landlords and the apartment manager, for their failure to have a working smoke detector in his apartment where his wife and child died in a fire.


OVERVIEW: The wife and child of appellant, a tenant, were killed in a fire in an apartment they rented from appellee landlords and which was managed by appellee manager. Appellant sued appellees for common law negligence and under the Texas smoke detector statute, Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 92.252 (1995), alleging that his smoke detector wasn't working. The jury rendered a verdict for appellant, but the trial court granted a judgment n.o.v. to appellees. On review, the court held that because appellant did not request appellee landlords to inspect the smoke detector as required by Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 92.259 (1995 and Supp. 1996), because only the landlords were statutorily liable and the statutory remedies were in lieu of common law under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. §§ 92.001(2) (1995) and 92.252(a) (1995), appellant had no claims against appellee landlords and no statutory claims against appellee manager. However, because appellee manager inspected the smoke detector when appellant rented the apartment, appellant had common law claims against him. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment n.o.v. except for the common law claim against appellee manager, and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed only the judgment n.o.v. on the common law claims against appellee manager on appellant, a tenant's, claims for his family's death in an apartment fire and remanded the case for new trial. Because appellant did not ask appellee landlords to inspect his smoke detector as required by the smoke detector law he had no claims against them but appellee manager's inspection of the detector gave appellant common law claims against him.

Hoffman v. State


No. 10-94-246-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


922 S.W.2d 663; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1945



May 15, 1996, delivered  
May 15, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 249th District Court. Somervell County, Texas. Trial Court # 228.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from the 249th District Court of Somervell County (Texas) that convicted him of indecency with a child and aggravated assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 21.11 and 21.021 (1994 & Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his convictions for aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 21.11 and 21.021 (1994 & Supp. 1996). The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding no fundamental error at trial. The court rejected the argument that it was fundamental error to permit a convicted felon to sit on the jury. The court explained the juror received a probated sentence for a felony burglary as a teen. The court determined that the state of Texas and Illinois, where the juror was convicted, did not have a strong policy against permitting previously convicted persons from sitting on juries if they successfully completed terms of community supervision and the charges were then dismissed against them. The court further explained, assuming it was error to allow the juror to sit, appellant's knowledge of the information during voir dire constituted consent and the verdict was not void. The court next determined there was no abuse of discretion in the lower court's refusal to disqualify jurors for cause when the jurors were vacillating on the ability to consider the full range of punishment, but ultimately indicated an ability to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child and aggravated assault, because it was not error to allow a convicted felon to sit on jury when charges were dropped after successful completion of community supervision and the state did not have a strong public policy against allowing such individuals to participate as jurors and rejection of challenge to vacillating jurors was not an abuse of discretion.

Radloff v. Dorman


NO. 07-96-0022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


924 S.W.2d 416; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1993



May 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 242ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HALE COUNTY; NO. B-27,551-9407; HONORABLE MARVIN F. MARSHALL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a wife and husband, appeal from a take-nothing summary judgment rendered against them by the 242nd Judicial District Court of Hale County (Texas) upon the basis that the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1996), barred their action to hold appellee, a physician, liable for medical negligence.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a wife and husband, brought a medical negligence action against appellee, a physician, under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 1.03(a)(4) (1996). The court affirmed the take-nothing summary judgment entered in favor of appellee because appellants' action was barred by the statute of limitations of that act, art. 4590i, § 10.01. The court held that because the record lacked any evidence to raise a fact issue as to whether four months from the discovery of the negligence was a reasonable time for appellants to bring their action, they did not rebut appellee's summary judgment evidence supporting the application of this statute of limitations. The court ruled that art. 4590i, § 10.01 served to abolish the "discovery rule" in health care liability claims in appellants' alternative common law cause of action under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. 16.003(a) (Supp. 1996). The court ruled that the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, §13, rendered art. 4590i, § 10.01, unconstitutional only insofar as it purported to cut off a cause of action before it was known to exist or before suit could be brought.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing summary judgment rendered against appellants, a wife and husband, by the trial court based upon the statute of limitations barring their action to hold appellee, a physician, liable for medical negligence because the record lacked any evidence to raise a fact issue as to whether four months was a reasonable time for appellants to bring the action after discovery of the negligence.

Davis v. State


NO. 09-94-340 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


923 S.W.2d 781; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1994


April 18, 1996, Resubmitted  
May 15, 1996, Delivered  
May 15, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 159th Judicial District Court of Angelina County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 17,473. Honorable Gerald Goodwin, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 6, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 999.

This Opinion Substituted on Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 4, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1334.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the 159th Judicial District Court of Angelina County (Texas) judgment of conviction and sentence for possession of marijuana, violation of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002(38) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by the police when the vehicle he was driving was observed weaving from line to line. He refused to give consent for a vehicle search and was told he could leave the scene, but the vehicle was detained for an on-scene investigation. Sniff dogs searched the vehicle and marijuana was discovered in the trunk. Appellant was convicted and sentenced for possession of marijuana pursuant to Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002(38) (1992). On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the evidence was sufficient for a trier of fact to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant possessed marijuana by knowingly exercising actual care, custody, control, or management over it. The court determined that a reversal of the conviction was not warranted just because the circumstantial evidence failed to eliminate every innocent hypothesis. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion to suppress the evidence because the initial stop was valid and the officers had reasonable articulable suspicion to continue the detention, which was sufficiently brief and minimally intrusive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence for possession of marijuana because the circumstantial evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion to suppress the evidence.

Norton v. State


NO. 07-94-0258-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


930 S.W.2d 101; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1889



May 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 08/28/1996
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Norton v. Cockrell, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20609 (N.D. Tex., Dec. 11, 2001)
Writ of mandamus denied, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part In re Norton, 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 8793 (Tex. App. Amarillo, Nov. 24, 2008)
Writ of mandamus denied In re Norton, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 8592 (Tex. App. Amarillo, Nov. 5, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Norton v. State, 2017 Tex. App. LEXIS 7812 (Tex. App. Amarillo, Aug. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 47TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 33,796-A; HONORABLE RON ENNS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from the 47th Judicial District Court of Potter County (Texas) that convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his capital murder conviction claiming that the trial court erred by denying defense counsel's request for the appointment of an independent psychiatrist to examine him on the issue of insanity. The court found appellant failed to make the required threshold showing that his sanity was likely to be a significant factor at trial and entitled to the appointment of a independent expert. The court held that appellant waived any error, resulting from the trial court's failure to appoint an expert, by his refusal to submit to a court-ordered psychiatric examination and subsequent withdrawal of his insanity plea. The court found that appellant was represented by competent counsel, who expressly acknowledged in the motion to withdraw the insanity defense that he had advised appellant to invoke his Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights, and that appellant concurred with such advice. The court held that this was sufficient to show a knowing and voluntary waiver of known rights. The court rejected appellant's argument that certain statements made by the prosecutor during the jury panel voir dire were prejudicial. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction, holding that appellant failed to show that he was entitled to the appointment of a independent psychiatrist and waived any error by his refusal to submit to a court-ordered psychiatric examination and his subsequent withdrawal of an insanity plea. The court held that appellant was not prejudiced by appellee state's comments during voir dire and had waived this error also.

Lone Starr Multi Theatres v. State


NO. 03-95-00502-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


922 S.W.2d 295; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1859



May 8, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-15302, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant movie theater corporation challenged an order of the 345th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), dismissing appellant's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellees, state and attorney general, for want of jurisdiction under the Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-.011.


OVERVIEW: Appellant movie theater corporation sought declaratory and injunctive relief against appellees, state and attorney general, that the obscenity statutes found in Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21-.26 were unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the action, finding it had no jurisdiction under the Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act (UDJA), Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-.011. On appeal, the court affirmed, because appellee attorney general had no power to enforce the criminal obscenity statutes. Instead, that power belonged to the county and district attorneys under Tex. Const. art. V, § 21. Consequently, the court found that a declaratory judgment would not terminate the controversy between the parties as required by the UDJA, because no controversy existed. Additionally, injunctive relief could only run against persons engaging in the activity sought to be enjoined, which did not include appellees.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Appellant movie theater corporation's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding the constitutionality of obscenity statutes was properly dismissed, because appellee attorney general lacked authority to enforce the statutes.

 

1000 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Graves v. Morales


NO. 03-95-00415-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


923 S.W.2d 754; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1708



May 1, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 3, 1996. Released for Publication July 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-14229, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the grant of appellee state officials' motion for summary judgment, and the denial of appellant's motion for summary judgment, by the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), which held that the Attorney Occupation Tax, Tex. Code Tax Ann. §§ 191.141-191.145, was constitutional and refused to provide appellant relief from the tax owed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney challenged Texas' attorney occupation tax, Tex. Code Tax Ann. §§ 191.141, 191.142 (1996), on the grounds that it was inequitable and unconstitutional in that appellee state officials did not collect the tax from state-employed attorneys. Appellees' theory was that they were simply offsetting monies received by monies dispersed. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, holding that the tax was constitutional. The court agreed with appellees that their policy merely offset monies they would have collected by monies that would be dispersed, and appellees' policy was rationally related to its purpose of efficiently collecting and remitting taxes. This was not an unconstitutional transfer of public funds to private persons because the policy provided a public benefit, that of providing an incentive to work for the state. The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment for appellant because even if the tax were unconstitutional, he offered no proof that he was entitled to relief of his tax burden because he could not demonstrate that his taxes were excessively higher because the other group was not taxed.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee state officials and the denial of summary judgment to appellant attorney were affirmed because an occupation tax that was not collected from state-employed attorneys was not an unconstitutional equal protection violation. Appellant would not have been entitled to relief anyway because he did not offer proof that his taxes were excessively higher because the other group was not taxed.
